Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
تقرير الأصول: The Principle of Taqrir al-Usul with Donkey's Leftover Water
This passage explains the usul principle of taqrir al-usul and applies it to the case of donkey's leftover water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of taqrir al-usul to resolve conflicts between proofs of equal strength by maintaining the original legal status of each element.

Core Idea
When proofs conflict equally, maintain both origins: purity of water and impurity of the person.

This passage introduces a cornerstone of Hanafi usul: when evidences are in equilibrium and no preference (tarjih) is possible, each matter is kept on its original legal footing. The author demonstrates this through the classic case of a donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar). By following the reasoning, you will see how conflicting hadith and analogies lead to a composite ruling—both wudu and tayammum—rather than a simple binary of pure or impure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting proofs
Locate the two hadith narrations (Jabir's permission and Anas's prohibition) and the contradictory analogical comparisons (to sweat, milk, dog's leftover, cat's leftover) presented in the passage.
The hadith differ in ruling; the analogies yield conflicting results because of varying degrees of need.
2
Attempt tarjih (preference)
Evaluate whether any proof can be preferred over another. The passage shows that all attempts at analogical attachment fail due to differences in necessity, and the hadith are equally authentic.
Tarjih is impossible; the door of preference is closed.
3
Invoke taqrir al-usul
When tarjih fails, apply the principle: establish each element upon its original legal status. Water is originally pure (tahir); a person without ablution is originally in a state of hadath (ritual impurity).
Both origins are maintained simultaneously.
4
Derive the composite ruling
From the two maintained origins, conclude that one must perform wudu with the water (since it is originally pure) and also perform tayammum (since the person's hadath is certain and not removed).
The ruling is not simply 'pure' or 'impure'; it is 'mushtabah' (doubtful) requiring both acts.

وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى فَجَاسَةٍ سُورهَا وَالْقَيَاسِنَانِ أَيْضًا مُتَعَارِضَانِ لانه لايُمْكِنُ الْحَاقَّهُ بِالْعِرقِ لِيَكُونُ طَاهِرًا لِقِلْةٍ الضُّرُورَةِ فِيْهِ وَكَثْرَتِهَا فِي الْعِرْقِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ الْحَاقُهُ بِاللَّبَنِ لِيَكُونَ نَجْسًا بِجَامِعِ التَّوَلُدِ مِنَ اللَّحْمِ لِوُجُودِ الضَّرُورَةِ فِي السَّوْرِ دُونَ اللَّبَن وَكَذَا لَا يُمْكِنُ الْحَاقَّة بِسوْرِ الْكَلْبِ لِيَكُونَ نَجَسًا لِكَيْن الضَّرُورَةِ فِي الْحِمَارِ دُونَ الْكَلْبِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ الْحَاقَّة بسور الهرة لِيَكُونَ طَاهِرًا لِوُجُودِ الضَّرُورَةِ فِي الْهرُةَ أَكْثَرِ مِمَّا يَكُونُ فِي الْحِمَارِ فَلَمَّا تَعَارَضَ هَذَا كَلُّهُ وَانْسَدَّ بَابُ التَّرْجِيْحِ وَجَبَ تَقْرِيرُ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِن الْمُتَوَضَى وَالْمَاءِ إِلَى أَصْلِهِ فَقِيْلَ إِنَّ الْمَاءَ عُرِفَ طَاهِرًا فِي الْأَصْلِ فَلَا يَتَنَجَّسُ فَوَجَبَ اسْتِعْمَالُ الطَّاهِرِ وَالتَّوْضِي بِهِ وَالأَدَمِنْ لَمَّا كَانَ فِي الْأَصْلِ مُحَدَثًا بَقِيَ كَذَلِكَ وَلَمْ يَزَلْ بِهِ الْحَدَتْ لِلتَّعَارُضِ فَوَجَبَ ضَمُّ التَّيَمُّمِ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يُقَالُ إِنَّ الْمَاءِ كَان فِي الأَصْلِ مُطَرًا فَمَا الاحتياج إلى ضم التيمم لأنا نَقُولُ لَوْ أَبْقَيْنَا الْمَاءَ مُطَرًا لأَنَّا لَفَاتِ أَصلُ الآدَمِن وَهُوَ الْحَدَث فَلَمْ يَكُنْ تَقَرِيرُ الأصول بَل تَقْرِيرُ الْمَاءِ فَقَط وَلَا يُقَال إِن الْمُبِيْعَ وَالْمُحَرِّمَ إِذَا تَعَارَضَا تَرَبَّحُ الْمُحَرِّمُ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَتَرَبَّحَ الْمُحَرَّمُ وَلَا يَقْضَى الى الشك لأنَّا نَقُولُ إِنْ هَذَا التَّرْجِيْحَ كَانَ لِلاِحْتِيَاطِ وَالاحْتِيَاطُ هَبْنَا فِي جَعَلِهِ مَشكُوكًا يَتَرَضاً بِهِ وَيُتَيَهُمُ وَسُمَّى أَى سُورِ الْحِمَارِ مَشْكُوكًا لِهَذَا أَنْ لَأَجَلٍ التَّعَارُضِ لَا أَن يُعنى بِهِ الْجَهْلُ أَي لايُعنى به أَنْ حُكْمَة مَجْهولٌ لِيَكُونَ مِنْ قَبِيل لا أدرى بَلْ حُكْمُهُ مَعْلُومٌ وَهُوَ وَجُوْبُ التَّوَضَى وَضَمُ التيمم آلَيْهِ وَأَمَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ التَّعَارَضَ بَيْنَ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ فَلَمْ يَسْقُطًا بِالتَّعَارُضِ لِيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوجَدُ بَعْدَ الْقَيَاسِ دَلِيلُ يُصَارُ إِلَيْهِ إِلا الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِحُجَةٍ عِنْدَنَا وَإِنَّمَا يُصَارُ إِلَيْهِ فِي سَوْرِ الْحِمَارِ الضرورة.
وَأَيْضًا رَوَى جابر أنه سئل الخ اور اسی طرح حضرت جابڑ تے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے ترجمه د تشریح جناب نبی کریم عے سے دریافت کیا کہ ہم اس پانی سے وضو کر سکتے ہیں جو گدھوں کے پینے سے بیچ جاتا ہے آپ نے فرمایا ہاں اور حضرت انس نے روایت کیا ہے کہ ہی کریم ہو نے پالتو گدھوں کے بچے ہوئے پانی سے وضو کرنے سے منع فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ یہ پاک ہے یہ روایت سور ( بچے ہوئے) کے نجس ہونے پر دلالت کوئی ہے۔ وَالْقَهَاستانِ أَيْضا مُتَعَارِضَانِ۔ اور دو قیاس بھی متعارض ہو جاتے ہیں کیوں کہ ان کے سور کو ان کے پینے کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس وجہ سے سور الحمار کی ضرورت کم ہے اور پینے میں ضرورت زیادہ ہے۔ اسی طرح سور الحمار کو دودھ کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ نجس ہونے کا حکم دیدیا جائے کیوں کہ دودھ اور پسینہ دونوں گوشت سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں (جامع علت موجود ہے) مگر ایسا اس لئے نہیں کر سکتے کہ سور کی ضرورت نہا سکہ ہے اور اس کے مقابلے میں اس کے دودھ کی ضرورت کم ہے اس طرح سور الحمار کو سور الکلب (سکتے کا جھوٹا) سے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ نجس ہو جائے کیوں کہ ضرورت سور الحمار کی زائد ہے اور سور الکلب کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ سوزھرہ (بیلی کا جھوٹا) کے ساتھ بھی لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے طاھر ہونے کا حکم دیدیا جائے کیوں کہ مور ہرہ میں ضرورت زائد ہے بمقابلہ سور الحمار سکے جب سور الحمار کا ان سب کے ساتھ تعارض ہوا ۔ اور تری کا باب بند ہو گیا تو واجب ہوا کہ ہر دو کو اپنی جگہ باقی رکھا جائے لہذا وضو کرنا اور پانی دونوں اپنی اپنی جگہ بر قرار ہیں۔ فَقِيلَ إِنَّ المَاءَ عرف میں چنانچہ کہا گیا ہے کہ چوں کہ اصل میں پانی طاھر ہونے میں معروف ہے لہذا وہ نجس نہیں ہو گا لہذا بے وضو آدمی کے لئے ماہ طاھر کا استعمال اور اس سے وضو کرنا واجب ہو گیا۔ اور آدمی اصل میں نجس تھا اس لئے وہ محدث ہی باقی رہا۔۔
He taught two rak'ahs containing one bowing and two prostrations, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed four bowings and four prostrations, so both are contradictory. Therefore, after this, recourse was made to analogy (qiyas), and that is that the eclipse prayer is analogized to other prayers. And when unable, establishing the original principles (taqrir al-usul) is obligatory; that is, when from the aforementioned matters inability and compulsion become apparent, such that the sayings of the Companions are contradictory and the analogies also contradict each other, or after these things no proof exists, then establishing the original principles is obligatory, and each thing must be kept upon its original state, and whatever is established upon something must remain upon it. As in the chapter of the donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar), when all proofs conflicted, establishing the original principle became obligatory. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the Day of Khaybar forbade eating the meat of domestic donkeys and ordered the overturning of the pots in which their meat was cooking. And Qalb bin Fihr (?) narrated that he said to the Prophet: 'I have nothing left except a few donkeys and nothing remains.' The Prophet said: 'Eat from your beneficial (fat) wealth.' In this hadith, he permitted eating donkeys. Thus when contradiction occurred about donkey meat, confusion arose about their leftover water because the saliva is formed from it. Also, Jabir narrated that he asked: 'May we perform ablution with water that is the leftover of donkeys?' He said: 'Yes.' And Anas narrated that he forbade the leftover water of domestic donkeys and said: 'It is impure (rijs).' This indicates the impurity of their leftover water. And the two analogies are also contradictory because it is not possible to attach it to sweat to be pure due to the scarcity of need in it and its abundance in sweat; nor is it possible to attach it to milk to be impure due to the commonality of generation from meat, because need exists in leftover water but not in milk. Likewise, it is not possible to attach it to a dog's leftover water to be impure because need exists in the donkey but not the dog; nor is it possible to attach it to a cat's leftover water to be pure because need in a cat is greater than in a donkey. When all this contradicted and the door of preference (tarjih) was closed, it became obligatory to establish each of the person performing ablution and the water to its original state. So it was said: Water was known to be pure in origin, so it does not become impure; therefore it became obligatory to use the pure water and perform ablution with it. And the person, since he was in a state of hadath (impurity) originally, remained as such, and his hadath was not removed due to the contradiction; so it became obligatory to add tayammum (dry ablution) to it. And let it not be said: Water was originally pure, so what is the need to add tayammum? Because we say: If we kept water pure, then the origin of the person, which is hadath, would be lost; then it would not be establishing the original principles, but only establishing the water. And let it not be said: If the permissive and prohibitive contradict, the prohibitive prevails, so the prohibited must prevail and one should not resort to doubt. Because we say: This preference (tarjih) was for caution, and caution we have accepted in making it doubtful; he performs ablution with it and performs tayammum. And the leftover water of the donkey is called 'doubtful' for this reason—due to the contradiction—not meaning that its ruling is unknown, such that it would be a case of 'I do not know'; rather, its ruling is known: it is the obligation of ablution and adding tayammum to it. And as for when contradiction occurs between two analogies, they do not fall due to contradiction, so acting upon the current state (hal) is not obligatory because after analogy there is no proof to which one can resort except acting upon the current state, and that is not a proof (hujjah) according to us; rather, it is resorted to in the case of donkey's leftover water out of necessity. Also, Jabir narrated that he asked... and similarly, Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated that he asked the Prophet: 'Can we perform ablution with water that remains after donkeys drink?' He said: 'Yes.' And Anas narrated that he forbade performing ablution with the leftover water of domestic donkeys and said: 'It is pure.' This narration indicates the impurity of the leftover water. And the two analogies are also contradictory because their leftover water cannot be attached to their sweat to be pure, because the need for leftover water is less and the need for sweat is great. Similarly, it cannot be attached to milk to rule it impure because milk and sweat both originate from meat (the commonality exists); but it cannot be done because the need for leftover water is great and the need for its milk is less in comparison. Thus, it cannot be attached to a dog's leftover water to be impure because need in donkey's leftover water is greater and there is no need for dog's leftover water. Nor can it be attached to a cat's leftover water to rule it pure due to need, because need in cat is greater compared to donkey's leftover water. When the donkey's leftover water contradicted with all these, and the door of tarjih was closed, it became obligatory to keep both in their place. So it was said that since water is known to be pure in origin, it does not become impure; therefore for a person without ablution, using pure water and performing ablution with it became obligatory. And the person was impure in origin, so he remained in hadath.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents the usul principle known as 'taqrir al-usul' (establishing the original ruling) when conflicting evidences cannot be reconciled through tarjih (preference). The author first illustrates the problem with the eclipse prayer example, then states the rule: when one is unable to resolve contradictions among proofs (such as conflicting hadith, companion opinions, or analogies), one must return each matter to its original legal status. The detailed case study is the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey. There are contradictory hadith: some indicate it is pure (Jabir's narration: the Prophet permitted using it for wudu), while others indicate it is impure (Anas's narration: the Prophet forbade it and called it rijs). Analogical reasoning also yields conflicting results: if compared to sweat (which is pure), it would be pure; if compared to milk (which is impure? actually milk is pure in Hanafi, but the text says impure? careful: the text states attaching to milk to be impure is problematic; the Hanafi ruling: donkey's milk is impure? I recall donkey's milk is considered impure in Hanafi? Actually donkey's milk is impure according to Hanafi. The text says 'attaching to milk to be impure due to commonality of generation from meat'—so both come from the donkey's body. But need in leftover water is greater, so the analogy fails. Similarly, comparing to dog's leftover water (impure) would give impurity, but need in donkey's leftover water is greater than for dog's water. Comparing to cat's leftover water (pure) would give purity, but need for cat's water is even greater. Thus all analogies are inconclusive. Since no preference (tarjih) is possible, the principle of taqrir al-usul is applied: the water remains in its original state of purity, and the person remains in his original state of hadath (ritual impurity). Therefore, the ruling is that one must perform both wudu (using the water, assuming it is pure) and tayammum (since the water's purity is doubtful due to conflict, but the person's hadath is certain). This composite ruling is known as 'wudu and tayammum combined' for the case of donkey's leftover water. The author also addresses potential objections: if water is originally pure, why add tayammum? Because otherwise the person's hadath would be disregarded, which would not be establishing both origins. Also, the objection that the prohibitive should prevail (since caution dictates avoiding impurity) is answered: caution here leads to combining both acts (wudu and tayammum), treating the water as doubtful, not ruling it impure outright.

Key Terms
تقرير الأصول (taqrir al-usul): Establishing each thing upon its original legal status when conflicting evidences cannot be reconciled.
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The water leftover after a donkey drinks from it, considered legally doubtful in Hanafi fiqh.
تعارض (ta'arud): Contradiction between two proofs of equal strength such that neither can be preferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle of taqrir al-usul as explained in this passage, what is the ruling on performing wudu with the leftover water of a domestic donkey?
A) It is pure, so wudu is valid without tayammum.
B) It is impure, so tayammum must be performed instead.
C) It is doubtful; one must perform both wudu with the water and tayammum.
D) It is prohibited to use it at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of taqrir al-usul resolves proof conflicts by returning each element to its original legal status, resulting in composite rulings that honor both origins.

Explains the ruling on donkey's leftover water and the method to resolve contradictory analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method for resolving contradictory analogies (ta'arud al-qiyasayn) to the specific case of su'ur al-himar and derive the required ruling.

Core Idea
When two analogies contradict, the Hanafi school applies both rulings — su'ur al-himar requires both wudu and tayammum.

This lesson explores a classic Hanafi usul case: the leftover water of a donkey (su'ur al-himar). The primary sources appear contradictory, and the analogies drawn from them also conflict. Instead of abandoning one evidence, the Hanafis treat the water as 'doubtful' (mashkuk) and combine both rulings. This demonstrates a key principle: when contradictory analogies are equally strong, the mujtahid does not drop both, but rather applies both until further evidence or preference (tarjih) can be established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary evidence
The passage cites hadiths from Jabir and Anas. Both are ahad and appear contradictory: one permits wudu with su'ur al-himar, the other forbids it.
These hadiths are the basis for the contradictory analogies.
2
Recognize the two analogies
One analogy measures su'ur al-himar to water (original purity) due to necessity; the other measures it to the donkey's meat (impurity) due to common origin.
Both analogies are plausible.
3
Analyze the contradiction
The two analogies are equally strong; neither can override the other because their bases (necessity vs. analogy to meat) are both valid.
No external evidence tips the scale.
4
Apply the Hanafi resolution
Since the analogies contradict and no external proof provides preference, the rulings of both are applied: wudu (from the permission analogy) and tayammum (from the impurity analogy, ensuring purity).
This results in the water being classified as mashkuk (doubtful).
5
Distinguish from ignorance
The ruling is known; it is not that the ruling is unknown, but a practical necessity to combine both acts due to contradictory evidences.
The category 'mashkuk' here is a legal designation, not a state of uncertainty.

فِي الأَصْلِ مُطَرًا فَمَا الاحتياج إلى ضم التيمم لأنا نَقُولُ لَوْ أَبْقَيْنَا الْمَاءَ مُطَرًا لأَنَّا لَفَاتِ أَصلُ الآدَمِن وَهُوَ الْحَدَث فَلَمْ يَكُنْ تَقَرِيرُ الأصول بَل تَقْرِيرُ الْمَاءِ فَقَط وَلَا يُقَال إِن الْمُبِيْعَ وَالْمُحَرِّمَ إِذَا تَعَارَضَا تَرَبَّحُ الْمُحَرِّمُ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَتَرَبَّحَ الْمُحَرَّمُ وَلَا يَقْضَى الى الشك لأنَّا نَقُولُ إِنْ هَذَا التَّرْجِيْحَ كَانَ لِلاِحْتِيَاطِ وَالاحْتِيَاطُ هَبْنَا فِي جَعَلِهِ مَشكُوكًا يَتَرَضاً بِهِ وَيُتَيَهُمُ وَسُمَّى أَى سُورِ الْحِمَارِ مَشْكُوكًا لِهَذَا أَنْ لَأَجَلٍ التَّعَارُضِ لَا أَن يُعنى بِهِ الْجَهْلُ أَي لايُعنى به أَنْ حُكْمَة مَجْهولٌ لِيَكُونَ مِنْ قَبِيل لا أدرى بَلْ حُكْمُهُ مَعْلُومٌ وَهُوَ وَجُوْبُ التَّوَضَى وَضَمُ التيمم آلَيْهِ وَأَمَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ التَّعَارَضَ بَيْنَ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ فَلَمْ يَسْقُطًا بِالتَّعَارُضِ لِيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوجَدُ بَعْدَ الْقَيَاسِ دَلِيلُ يُصَارُ إِلَيْهِ إِلا الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِحُجَةٍ عِنْدَنَا وَإِنَّمَا يُصَارُ إِلَيْهِ فِي سَوْرِ الْحِمَارِ الضرورة.
وَأَيْضًا رَوَى جابر أنه سئل الخ اور اسی طرح حضرت جابڑ تے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے ترجمه د تشریح جناب نبی کریم عے سے دریافت کیا کہ ہم اس پانی سے وضو کر سکتے ہیں جو گدھوں کے پینے سے بیچ جاتا ہے آپ نے فرمایا ہاں اور حضرت انس نے روایت کیا ہے کہ ہی کریم ہو نے پالتو گدھوں کے بچے ہوئے پانی سے وضو کرنے سے منع فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ یہ پاک ہے یہ روایت سور ( بچے ہوئے) کے نجس ہونے پر دلالت کوئی ہے۔ وَالْقَهَاستانِ أَيْضا مُتَعَارَضَانِ۔ اور دو قیاس بھی متعارض ہو جاتے ہیں کیوں کہ ان کے سور کو ان کے پینے کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس وجہ سے سور الحمار کی ضرورت کم ہے اور پینے میں ضرورت زیادہ ہے۔ اسی طرح سور الحمار کو دودھ کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ نجس ہونے کا حکم دیدیا جائے کیوں کہ دودھ اور پسینہ دونوں گوشت سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں (جامع علت موجود ہے) مگر ایسا اس لئے نہیں کر سکتے کہ سور کی ضرورت نہا سکہ ہے اور اس کے مقابلے میں اس کے دودھ کی ضرورت کم ہے اس طرح سور الحمار کو سور الکلب (سکتے کا جھوٹا) سے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ نجس ہو جائے کیوں کہ ضرورت سور الحمار کی زائد ہے اور سور الکلب کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ سوزھرہ (بیلی کا جھوٹا) کے ساتھ بھی لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے طاھر ہونے کا حکم دیدیا جائے کیوں کہ مور ہرہ میں ضرورت زائد ہے بمقابلہ سور الحمار سکے جب سور الحمار کا ان سب کے ساتھ تعارض ہوا ۔ اور تری کا باب بند ہو گیا تو واجب ہوا کہ ہر دو کو اپنی جگہ باقی رکھا جائے لہذا وضو کرنا اور پانی دونوں اپنی اپنی جگہ بر قرار ہیں۔ فَقِيلَ إِنَّ المَاءَ عرف میں چنانچہ کہا گیا ہے کہ چوں کہ اصل میں پانی طاھر ہونے میں معروف ہے لہذا وہ نجس نہیں ہو گا لہذا بے وضو آدمی کے لئے ماہ طاھر کا استعمال اور اس سے وضو کرنا واجب ہو گیا۔ اور آدمی اصل میں نجس تھا اس لئے وہ محدث ہی باقی رہا۔

کرنا ضروری ہے اور یہ بھی نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ یہ تو شک کی طرف لے جاتا ہے کیوں کہ ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ ترجیح احتیاط کی وجہ سے تھی اور احتیاط اس جگہ مشکوک قرار دینے ہی میں ہے تاکہ اس ماء مشکوک سے وضو بھی کرے اور ٹیم بھی کرے۔ وسمی اور نام رکھا گیا یعنی سور حمار کا مشکوک لہذ ا مشکوک اسی وجہ سے یعنی تعارض کی وجہ سے سور حمار کو اس تعارض کی وجہ سے مشکوک کے نام سے موسوم کیا گیا ہے نہ اس وجہ سے کہ اس کا حکم نا معلوم ہے یعنی اس سے مراد یہ نہیں لیا جا سکتا کہ اس کا حکم مجھول ہے تاکہ از قبل لا ادری ( میں نہیں جانتا ہو جائے بلکہ اس کا حکم معلوم ہے اور وہ ہے وجوب التوضی وضو کا واجب ہونا اور اس کے ساتھ یتیم کا بعمل بالحال کے اور عمل بالحال ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے اور سور حمار میں عمل بالحال کی طرف ضرورت کی ورنہ سے جایا جاتا ہے۔ بَلْ يَعْمَلُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ بِأَيِّهِمَا شَاءَ بِشهَادَةٍ قَلْبِهِ يَعْنِي يَتَحَرَّىٰ قَلْبُهُ إِلَى أَحَدٍ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ الَّذِى إِطْمَانُ إِلَيْهِ بِنُورِ الْفِرَاسَةِ الَّتِي أَعْطَاهَا اللهُ لِكُلِّ مُؤْمِنٍ وَعِندَ الشافَعِيُّ لأَتَسْتَرِطُ شَهَادَةُ الْقَلْبِ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ لَهُ فِي كُلِّ مَسْئَلَةٍ قَوْلَانِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فِي زَمَانٍ وَاحِدٍ بِخِلافِ أَبْعَتِنَا فَإِنَّهُ مَا تَرُوَى عَنْهُمْ رَوَايَتَانِ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الا بِحَسَبِ الزَّمَانَيْنِ ولَكِنْ لَمْ يُعْرِفِ التَّارِيحُ لَيُعْمَلَ بِالآخِيْرِ فَقَط فَلِهَذَا إِدَارَ الفتَوى بَيْنَهُمَا هَكَذَا قِيْلَ وَلَمَّا كَانَ هَذَا بَيَانُ الْمُعَارَضَةِ الحقيقية الذي حُكْمُهَا الشَّتَاقُطُ فَالآن شرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ مُعَارَضَةٍ صُورِيَةٍ وَحُكْمُهَا التَّرْجِيْحُ وَالتَّوْفِيقِ فَقَالَ وَالمُخلص عَنِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ أَمَّا أَن يَكُونَ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحُجَةِ بِأَنْ لَمْ يَعْقِدُ لا بِأَنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا مَشْهُورًا وَالآخَرُ أَحَادًا وَيَكُونُ أَحَدُهُمَا نَما وَالآخَرُ ظَاهِرًا فَيُتَرَبَّحُ الأَعْلَى عَلى الأدْنى وَقَدْ مَرَّ مِثَالُهُ غَيْرَ مَرَّةٍ أَوْ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحُكْمِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمُ الدُّنْيَا وَالآخَرُ حُكْمُ الْعَقْنِي كَايَتَى الْيَمِيْنِ فِي سُوْرَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ
In the origin it is pure, so what is the need to attach tayammum? We say: if we kept the water as pure, then the original of man, which is hadath, would be lost, and there would be no establishment of the origin but only establishment of the water. And it is not said that when the permissive and the prohibitory are contradictory, the prohibitory is given preference, so the prohibited must be given precedence and it does not lead to doubt. Because we say: this preference was for precaution, and precaution here is in making it doubtful so that he performs wudu with it and also performs tayammum. And it is called 'doubtful' for this reason, i.e., because of contradiction, not that its ruling is unknown, nor that its ruling is unknown so that it falls under 'I do not know', rather its ruling is known: the obligation of wudu and attaching tayammum to it. And when contradiction occurs between two analogies, they are not abrogated by contradiction so as to necessitate acting on the current state, because after analogy there is no evidence to resort to except acting on the current state, and acting on the current state is not a proof according to us; it is only resorted to in su'ur al-himar due to necessity. Also Jabir narrated that he was asked... and similarly, Hadrat Jabir narrated that he asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) whether we can perform wudu with water that is left after donkeys drink; he said yes. And Hadrat Anas narrated that the Prophet forbade performing wudu with water left by domesticated donkeys and said it is pure. This narration indicates the impurity of su'ur (leftover). And the two analogies are also contradictory. And two analogies also become contradictory because their leftover cannot be attached to their drinking; for this reason, the necessity of su'ur al-himar is less and the necessity of drinking is greater. Similarly, su'ur al-himar cannot be attached to milk so that it be ruled impure, because milk and sweat both originate from flesh (the common cause exists), but it is not done because the necessity of su'ur is extreme and compared to it the necessity of its milk is less. Similarly, su'ur al-himar cannot be attached to su'ur al-kalb (leftover of dog) so that it be impure, because the necessity of su'ur al-himar is greater and su'ur al-kalb has no necessity. Nor can it be attached to su'ur al-baqar (leftover of cow) so that it be ruled pure due to necessity, because the necessity of su'ur al-baqar is greater compared to su'ur al-himar. When su'ur al-himar contradicted all these and the door of preference was closed, it became necessary to keep both in their places; hence wudu and water both remain in their places. So it was said: water is known in origin [as pure], therefore it will not become impure; so for the person without wudu, using pure water and performing wudu with it became obligatory. And the human being was originally impure, so he remained in hadath. And hadath persisted with him; and since due to contradiction hadath remained (could not be removed), it became obligatory to attach tayammum to it. And it should not be objected: water was purifying from its origin, so why the need to attach tayammum? Because we answer: if we keep water as purifying, then the original of man (i.e., hadath) would be lost, so in that case the establishment of the origin would not remain; only the establishment of water would occur. And it is not said: when the permissive and the prohibitory contradict, the prohibitory is given precedence, so the prohibited must be acted upon; and it cannot be said that this leads to doubt. Because we answer: the preference was for precaution, and precaution here is in making it doubtful so that he performs wudu with that doubtful water and also performs tayammum. And it was named: su'ur al-himar is called 'doubtful' for this reason, i.e., due to contradiction, not because its ruling is unknown, meaning it is not intended that its ruling is unknown so that it becomes from the category of 'I do not know'; rather its ruling is known: the obligation of wudu and attaching tayammum to it. And when contradiction occurs between two analogies, they are not abrogated so that acting on the current state becomes necessary, because after analogy there is no proof to act upon except acting on the current state, and acting on the current state is not a proof according to us; it is only resorted to in su'ur al-himar out of necessity. Rather, the mujtahid acts on whichever of the two he wishes, with the testimony of his heart, meaning his heart inclines to one of the two analogies to which he feels reassured, by the light of insight that Allah gives to every believer. And according to al-Shafi'i, the testimony of the heart is not a condition; therefore he has in every question two or more opinions in one time, unlike our imams, for no two narrations are related from them in a single question except according to two times, but the dates are not known to act only by the later; therefore the fatwa is rotated between them. This is said. And since this is the explanation of real contradiction, whose ruling is abrogation, now he began to explain formal contradiction, whose ruling is preference and reconciliation. He said: The way out of contradiction is either from the side of the proof, in that one of them is mashhur and the other ahad, or one is nass and the other zahir, so the higher is given preference over the lower; examples have passed many times. Or from the side of the ruling, in that one is a ruling of this world and the other a ruling of the afterlife, like the two verses on oath in Surah al-Baqarah.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Hanafi method for resolving contradiction (ta'arud) between analogies (qiyas), using the specific case of the leftover water of a donkey (su'ur al-himar). The author first addresses the problem: water is originally pure (mutahhir) and the human is originally in need of purification (hadath). The hadith reports from Jabir and Anas seem contradictory regarding the purity of donkey's leftover. The Hanafis reconcile by considering the water 'doubtful' (mashkuk), requiring both wudu and tayammum. This is not due to ignorance but due to a genuine contradiction between the two analogies: one analogy considers the water pure by origin, the other considers the donkey's saliva impure by analogy to its meat (which is impure). Since neither qiyas can override the other, both rulings are applied. The passage then generalizes: when two qiyas contradict and no external proof can settle, the mujtahid may choose based on his inner conviction (shahadat al-qalb) — a distinctively Hanafi doctrine. This contrasts with al-Shafi'i, who does not require such inner testimony and thus may hold multiple opinions on a single issue. The passage then distinguishes between real contradiction (where one evidence abrogates the other) and formal contradiction (where preference and reconciliation are possible). The discussion of 'mubah' versus 'muharram' is addressed: the rule that the prohibitory takes precedence in case of doubt does not apply here because the ruling is known (it is obligatory to combine wudu and tayammum). The Hanafi position relies on the concept of istihsan (juristic preference) to resolve the impasse.

Key Terms
سؤر الحمار (su'ur al-himar): The leftover water from which a donkey has drunk.
تعارض (ta'arud): Contradiction between two or more evidences that appear conflicting and cannot be reconciled directly.
شهادة القلب (shahadat al-qalb): The inner conviction or testimony of the heart that inclines the mujtahid to one of two contradictory analogies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul presented in this passage, why is su'ur al-himar considered mashkuk (doubtful) rather than simply impure or pure?
A) Because the hadiths are weak and contradictory.
B) Because the two analogies are contradictory and cannot be reconciled.
C) Because the water is naturally impure.
D) Because the scholars could not decide on a ruling.

Key Takeaway
When two analogies contradict and cannot be reconciled, the Hanafis apply both rulings; su'ur al-himar requires both wudu and tayammum.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Choosing Between Contradictory Analogies: The Testimony of the Heart (Shahadat al-Qalb)
Explains the ruling on donkey's leftover water and the method to resolve contradictory analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of shahadat al-qalb as a method for choosing between contradictory qiyas and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
When analogies contradict, the Hanafi mujtahid relies on inner conviction to choose one; Shafi'i allows multiple opinions.

In the previous lesson, we saw a case where contradictory analogies were both applied. However, in many cases, a mujtahid must choose one. This lesson introduces the Hanafi doctrine of shahadat al-qalb (testimony of the heart) — a unique condition for ijtihad that allows the mujtahid to make a decisive choice based on inner certainty. We also distinguish between real contradiction (where one proof abrogates the other) and formal contradiction (where preference and reconciliation are possible).

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Two analogies contradict and no external evidence (like a clear text or consensus) tips the scale.
This is different from the su'ur al-himar case where combination was possible.
2
Learn the Hanafi principle
The mujtahid may act on whichever analogy his heart testifies to (shahadat al-qalb), by the light of insight given to every believer.
This inner conviction provides the necessary certainty to issue a single ruling.
3
Contrast with Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i does not require shahadat al-qalb and thus allows multiple opinions (qawlan) on a single issue at the same time.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi gives one fatwa; Shafi'i may have two or more.
4
Distinguish real vs. formal contradiction
Real contradiction leads to abrogation of one proof; formal contradiction requires preference (tarjih) or reconciliation.
The passage ends by explaining that formal contradiction can be resolved by superiority of proof or by the nature of the ruling (dunya vs. akhirah).
5
Note the exception
In the su'ur al-himar case, necessity drove the combination, not shahadat al-qalb. The general rule for contradictory qiyas is either combination (if possible) or choice through shahadat al-qalb.
Shahadat al-qalb is for cases where combination is not feasible.

فِي الأَصْلِ مُطَرًا فَمَا الاحتياج إلى ضم التيمم لأنا نَقُولُ لَوْ أَبْقَيْنَا الْمَاءَ مُطَرًا لأَنَّا لَفَاتِ أَصلُ الآدَمِن وَهُوَ الْحَدَث فَلَمْ يَكُنْ تَقَرِيرُ الأصول بَل تَقْرِيرُ الْمَاءِ فَقَط وَلَا يُقَال إِن الْمُبِيْعَ وَالْمُحَرِّمَ إِذَا تَعَارَضَا تَرَبَّحُ الْمُحَرِّمُ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَتَرَبَّحَ الْمُحَرَّمُ وَلَا يَقْضَى الى الشك لأنَّا نَقُولُ إِنْ هَذَا التَّرْجِيْحَ كَانَ لِلاِحْتِيَاطِ وَالاحْتِيَاطُ هَبْنَا فِي جَعَلِهِ مَشكُوكًا يَتَرَضاً بِهِ وَيُتَيَهُمُ وَسُمَّى أَى سُورِ الْحِمَارِ مَشْكُوكًا لِهَذَا أَنْ لَأَجَلٍ التَّعَارُضِ لَا أَن يُعنى بِهِ الْجَهْلُ أَي لايُعنى به أَنْ حُكْمَة مَجْهولٌ لِيَكُونَ مِنْ قَبِيل لا أدرى بَلْ حُكْمُهُ مَعْلُومٌ وَهُوَ وَجُوْبُ التَّوَضَى وَضَمُ التيمم آلَيْهِ وَأَمَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ التَّعَارَضَ بَيْنَ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ فَلَمْ يَسْقُطًا بِالتَّعَارُضِ لِيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوجَدُ بَعْدَ الْقَيَاسِ دَلِيلُ يُصَارُ إِلَيْهِ إِلا الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِحُجَةٍ عِنْدَنَا وَإِنَّمَا يُصَارُ إِلَيْهِ فِي سَوْرِ الْحِمَارِ الضرورة.
وَأَيْضًا رَوَى جابر أنه سئل الخ اور اسی طرح حضرت جابڑ تے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے ترجمه د تشریح جناب نبی کریم عے سے دریافت کیا کہ ہم اس پانی سے وضو کر سکتے ہیں جو گدھوں کے پینے سے بیچ جاتا ہے آپ نے فرمایا ہاں اور حضرت انس نے روایت کیا ہے کہ ہی کریم ہو نے پالتو گدھوں کے بچے ہوئے پانی سے وضو کرنے سے منع فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ یہ پاک ہے یہ روایت سور ( بچے ہوئے) کے نجس ہونے پر دلالت کوئی ہے۔ وَالْقَهَاستانِ أَيْضا مُتَعَارَضَانِ۔ اور دو قیاس بھی متعارض ہو جاتے ہیں کیوں کہ ان کے سور کو ان کے پینے کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس وجہ سے سور الحمار کی ضرورت کم ہے اور پینے میں ضرورت زیادہ ہے۔ اسی طرح سور الحمار کو دودھ کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ نجس ہونے کا حکم دیدیا جائے کیوں کہ دودھ اور پسینہ دونوں گوشت سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں (جامع علت موجود ہے) مگر ایسا اس لئے نہیں کر سکتے کہ سور کی ضرورت نہا سکہ ہے اور اس کے مقابلے میں اس کے دودھ کی ضرورت کم ہے اس طرح سور الحمار کو سور الکلب (سکتے کا جھوٹا) سے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ نجس ہو جائے کیوں کہ ضرورت سور الحمار کی زائد ہے اور سور الکلب کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ سوزھرہ (بیلی کا جھوٹا) کے ساتھ بھی لاحق نہیں کر سکتے تاکہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے طاھر ہونے کا حکم دیدیا جائے کیوں کہ مور ہرہ میں ضرورت زائد ہے بمقابلہ سور الحمار سکے جب سور الحمار کا ان سب کے ساتھ تعارض ہوا ۔ اور تری کا باب بند ہو گیا تو واجب ہوا کہ ہر دو کو اپنی جگہ باقی رکھا جائے لہذا وضو کرنا اور پانی دونوں اپنی اپنی جگہ بر قرار ہیں۔ فَقِيلَ إِنَّ المَاءَ عرف میں چنانچہ کہا گیا ہے کہ چوں کہ اصل میں پانی طاھر ہونے میں معروف ہے لہذا وہ نجس نہیں ہو گا لہذا بے وضو آدمی کے لئے ماہ طاھر کا استعمال اور اس سے وضو کرنا واجب ہو گیا۔ اور آدمی اصل میں نجس تھا اس لئے وہ محدث ہی باقی رہا۔

کرنا ضروری ہے اور یہ بھی نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ یہ تو شک کی طرف لے جاتا ہے کیوں کہ ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ ترجیح احتیاط کی وجہ سے تھی اور احتیاط اس جگہ مشکوک قرار دینے ہی میں ہے تاکہ اس ماء مشکوک سے وضو بھی کرے اور ٹیم بھی کرے۔ وسمی اور نام رکھا گیا یعنی سور حمار کا مشکوک لہذ ا مشکوک اسی وجہ سے یعنی تعارض کی وجہ سے سور حمار کو اس تعارض کی وجہ سے مشکوک کے نام سے موسوم کیا گیا ہے نہ اس وجہ سے کہ اس کا حکم نا معلوم ہے یعنی اس سے مراد یہ نہیں لیا جا سکتا کہ اس کا حکم مجھول ہے تاکہ از قبل لا ادری ( میں نہیں جانتا ہو جائے بلکہ اس کا حکم معلوم ہے اور وہ ہے وجوب التوضی وضو کا واجب ہونا اور اس کے ساتھ یتیم کا بعمل بالحال کے اور عمل بالحال ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے اور سور حمار میں عمل بالحال کی طرف ضرورت کی ورنہ سے جایا جاتا ہے۔ بَلْ يَعْمَلُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ بِأَيِّهِمَا شَاءَ بِشهَادَةٍ قَلْبِهِ يَعْنِي يَتَحَرَّىٰ قَلْبُهُ إِلَى أَحَدٍ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ الَّذِى إِطْمَانُ إِلَيْهِ بِنُورِ الْفِرَاسَةِ الَّتِي أَعْطَاهَا اللهُ لِكُلِّ مُؤْمِنٍ وَعِندَ الشافَعِيُّ لأَتَسْتَرِطُ شَهَادَةُ الْقَلْبِ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ لَهُ فِي كُلِّ مَسْئَلَةٍ قَوْلَانِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فِي زَمَانٍ وَاحِدٍ بِخِلافِ أَبْعَتِنَا فَإِنَّهُ مَا تَرُوَى عَنْهُمْ رَوَايَتَانِ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الا بِحَسَبِ الزَّمَانَيْنِ ولَكِنْ لَمْ يُعْرِفِ التَّارِيحُ لَيُعْمَلَ بِالآخِيْرِ فَقَط فَلِهَذَا إِدَارَ الفتَوى بَيْنَهُمَا هَكَذَا قِيْلَ وَلَمَّا كَانَ هَذَا بَيَانُ الْمُعَارَضَةِ الحقيقية الذي حُكْمُهَا الشَّتَاقُطُ فَالآن شرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ مُعَارَضَةٍ صُورِيَةٍ وَحُكْمُهَا التَّرْجِيْحُ وَالتَّوْفِيقِ فَقَالَ وَالمُخلص عَنِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ أَمَّا أَن يَكُونَ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحُجَةِ بِأَنْ لَمْ يَعْقِدُ لا بِأَنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا مَشْهُورًا وَالآخَرُ أَحَادًا وَيَكُونُ أَحَدُهُمَا نَما وَالآخَرُ ظَاهِرًا فَيُتَرَبَّحُ الأَعْلَى عَلى الأدْنى وَقَدْ مَرَّ مِثَالُهُ غَيْرَ مَرَّةٍ أَوْ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحُكْمِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمُ الدُّنْيَا وَالآخَرُ حُكْمُ الْعَقْنِي كَايَتَى الْيَمِيْنِ فِي سُوْرَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ
In the origin it is pure, so what is the need to attach tayammum? We say: if we kept the water as pure, then the original of man, which is hadath, would be lost, and there would be no establishment of the origin but only establishment of the water. And it is not said that when the permissive and the prohibitory are contradictory, the prohibitory is given preference, so the prohibited must be given precedence and it does not lead to doubt. Because we say: this preference was for precaution, and precaution here is in making it doubtful so that he performs wudu with it and also performs tayammum. And it is called 'doubtful' for this reason, i.e., because of contradiction, not that its ruling is unknown, nor that its ruling is unknown so that it falls under 'I do not know', rather its ruling is known: the obligation of wudu and attaching tayammum to it. And when contradiction occurs between two analogies, they are not abrogated by contradiction so as to necessitate acting on the current state, because after analogy there is no evidence to resort to except acting on the current state, and acting on the current state is not a proof according to us; it is only resorted to in su'ur al-himar due to necessity. Also Jabir narrated that he was asked... and similarly, Hadrat Jabir narrated that he asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) whether we can perform wudu with water that is left after donkeys drink; he said yes. And Hadrat Anas narrated that the Prophet forbade performing wudu with water left by domesticated donkeys and said it is pure. This narration indicates the impurity of su'ur (leftover). And the two analogies are also contradictory. And two analogies also become contradictory because their leftover cannot be attached to their drinking; for this reason, the necessity of su'ur al-himar is less and the necessity of drinking is greater. Similarly, su'ur al-himar cannot be attached to milk so that it be ruled impure, because milk and sweat both originate from flesh (the common cause exists), but it is not done because the necessity of su'ur is extreme and compared to it the necessity of its milk is less. Similarly, su'ur al-himar cannot be attached to su'ur al-kalb (leftover of dog) so that it be impure, because the necessity of su'ur al-himar is greater and su'ur al-kalb has no necessity. Nor can it be attached to su'ur al-baqar (leftover of cow) so that it be ruled pure due to necessity, because the necessity of su'ur al-baqar is greater compared to su'ur al-himar. When su'ur al-himar contradicted all these and the door of preference was closed, it became necessary to keep both in their places; hence wudu and water both remain in their places. So it was said: water is known in origin [as pure], therefore it will not become impure; so for the person without wudu, using pure water and performing wudu with it became obligatory. And the human being was originally impure, so he remained in hadath. And hadath persisted with him; and since due to contradiction hadath remained (could not be removed), it became obligatory to attach tayammum to it. And it should not be objected: water was purifying from its origin, so why the need to attach tayammum? Because we answer: if we keep water as purifying, then the original of man (i.e., hadath) would be lost, so in that case the establishment of the origin would not remain; only the establishment of water would occur. And it is not said: when the permissive and the prohibitory contradict, the prohibitory is given precedence, so the prohibited must be acted upon; and it cannot be said that this leads to doubt. Because we answer: the preference was for precaution, and precaution here is in making it doubtful so that he performs wudu with that doubtful water and also performs tayammum. And it was named: su'ur al-himar is called 'doubtful' for this reason, i.e., due to contradiction, not because its ruling is unknown, meaning it is not intended that its ruling is unknown so that it becomes from the category of 'I do not know'; rather its ruling is known: the obligation of wudu and attaching tayammum to it. And when contradiction occurs between two analogies, they are not abrogated so that acting on the current state becomes necessary, because after analogy there is no proof to act upon except acting on the current state, and acting on the current state is not a proof according to us; it is only resorted to in su'ur al-himar out of necessity. Rather, the mujtahid acts on whichever of the two he wishes, with the testimony of his heart, meaning his heart inclines to one of the two analogies to which he feels reassured, by the light of insight that Allah gives to every believer. And according to al-Shafi'i, the testimony of the heart is not a condition; therefore he has in every question two or more opinions in one time, unlike our imams, for no two narrations are related from them in a single question except according to two times, but the dates are not known to act only by the later; therefore the fatwa is rotated between them. This is said. And since this is the explanation of real contradiction, whose ruling is abrogation, now he began to explain formal contradiction, whose ruling is preference and reconciliation. He said: The way out of contradiction is either from the side of the proof, in that one of them is mashhur and the other ahad, or one is nass and the other zahir, so the higher is given preference over the lower; examples have passed many times. Or from the side of the ruling, in that one is a ruling of this world and the other a ruling of the afterlife, like the two verses on oath in Surah al-Baqarah.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Hanafi method for resolving contradiction (ta'arud) between analogies (qiyas), using the specific case of the leftover water of a donkey (su'ur al-himar). The author first addresses the problem: water is originally pure (mutahhir) and the human is originally in need of purification (hadath). The hadith reports from Jabir and Anas seem contradictory regarding the purity of donkey's leftover. The Hanafis reconcile by considering the water 'doubtful' (mashkuk), requiring both wudu and tayammum. This is not due to ignorance but due to a genuine contradiction between the two analogies: one analogy considers the water pure by origin, the other considers the donkey's saliva impure by analogy to its meat (which is impure). Since neither qiyas can override the other, both rulings are applied. The passage then generalizes: when two qiyas contradict and no external proof can settle, the mujtahid may choose based on his inner conviction (shahadat al-qalb) — a distinctively Hanafi doctrine. This contrasts with al-Shafi'i, who does not require such inner testimony and thus may hold multiple opinions on a single issue. The passage then distinguishes between real contradiction (where one evidence abrogates the other) and formal contradiction (where preference and reconciliation are possible). The discussion of 'mubah' versus 'muharram' is addressed: the rule that the prohibitory takes precedence in case of doubt does not apply here because the ruling is known (it is obligatory to combine wudu and tayammum). The Hanafi position relies on the concept of istihsan (juristic preference) to resolve the impasse.

Key Terms
سؤر الحمار (su'ur al-himar): The leftover water from which a donkey has drunk.
تعارض (ta'arud): Contradiction between two or more evidences that appear conflicting and cannot be reconciled directly.
شهادة القلب (shahadat al-qalb): The inner conviction or testimony of the heart that inclines the mujtahid to one of two contradictory analogies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the role of shahadat al-qalb when contradictory analogies cannot be combined?
A) It is not used; the mujtahid must wait for consensus.
B) It allows the mujtahid to choose one analogy based on inner conviction.
C) It permits the mujtahid to issue multiple opinions on the same issue.
D) It is used only when the analogies involve forbidden matters.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when two analogies contradict and cannot be combined, the mujtahid chooses based on shahadat al-qalb, ensuring a single ruling per issue.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Conflicting Qiyas and Shahadat al-Qalb
Usul rule explaining the Hanafi approach to conflicting qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on resolving conflicting qiyas and identify the role of shahadat al-qalb.

Core Idea
Conflicting qiyas both stand; the mujtahid chooses with divine insight.

When two qiyas appear to conflict, Hanafi usul holds that neither falls automatically. Instead, the mujtahid must rely on an inner conviction (shahadat al-qalb) to choose. This contrasts with al-Shafi'i, who allows multiple opinions on one issue simultaneously. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi method of choice and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of conflicting qiyas
Recognize that when two qiyas conflict, the Hanafi school does not deem both invalid. The mujtahid must still act upon one of them, as there is no underlying text (nass) to apply directly.
Qiyas is a derivative proof; it does not fall simply because another qiyas conflicts.
2
Define shahadat al-qalb
Shahadat al-qalb ('testimony of the heart') is the heart's inclination towards one qiyas, based on divine light (nur al-firasah) given to every believer. This inner peace guides the mujtahid's choice.
It is not mere emotion but a divinely granted faculty.
3
Distinguish Hanafi from Shafi'i positions
Imam al-Shafi'i does not require shahadat al-qalb, so he can hold multiple contradictory opinions on the same issue at the same time. The Hanafi school avoids this because inner conviction prevents simultaneous adoption of conflicting views.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that Hanafi imams are not reported to have two conflicting opinions on a single issue at one time.
4
Identify the practical outcome (thamarah)
When two opinions from a Hanafi imam exist from different times but dates are unknown, fatwa is given on both, circulating between them. This preserves the school's consistency.
This is a unique Hanafi response to the problem of historical ambiguity.

وَأَمَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ التَّعَارض اور جب دو قیاموں کے درمیان تعارض واقع ہو تو وہ دونوں ساقط نہ ہوں گے تا کہ حال کے ساتھ عمل ہو جائے کیوں کہ قیاس کے نیچے کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے جس عمل کیا جائے بجر بعمل بالحال کے اور عمل بالحال ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے اور سور حمار میں عمل بالحال کی طرف ضرورت کی ورنہ سے جایا جاتا ہے۔ بَلْ يَعْمَلُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ بِأَيِّهِمَا شَاءَ بِشهَادَةٍ قَلْبِهِ يَعْنِي يَتَحَرَّىٰ قَلْبُهُ إِلَى أَحَدٍ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ الَّذِى إِطْمَانُ إِلَيْهِ بِنُورِ الْفِرَاسَةِ الَّتِي أَعْطَاهَا اللهُ لِكُلِّ مُؤْمِنٍ وَعِندَ الشافَعِيُّ لأَتَسْتَرِطُ شَهَادَةُ الْقَلْبِ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ لَهُ فِي كُلِّ مَسْئَلَةٍ قَوْلَانِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فِي زَمَانٍ وَاحِدٍ بِخِلافِ أَبْعَتِنَا فَإِنَّهُ مَا تَرُوَى عَنْهُمْ رَوَايَتَانِ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الا بِحَسَبِ الزَّمَانَيْنِ ولَكِنْ لَمْ يُعْرِفِ التَّارِيحُ لَيُعْمَلَ بِالآخِيْرِ فَقَط فَلِهَذَا إِدَارَ الفتَوى بَيْنَهُمَا هَكَذَا قِيْلَ وَلَمَّا كَانَ هَذَا بَيَانُ الْمُعَارَضَةِ الحقيقية الذي حُكْمُهَا الشَّتَاقُطُ فَالآن شرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ مُعَارَضَةٍ صُورِيَةٍ وَحُكْمُهَا التَّرْجِيْحُ وَالتَّوْفِيقِ فَقَالَ وَالمُخلص عَنِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ أَمَّا أَن يَكُونَ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحُجَةِ بِأَنْ لَمْ يَعْقِدُ لا بِأَنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا مَشْهُورًا وَالآخَرُ أَحَادًا وَيَكُونُ أَحَدُهُمَا نَما وَالآخَرُ ظَاهِرًا فَيُتَرَبَّحُ الأَعْلَىٰ عَلى الأدْنىٰ وَقَدْ مَرَّ مِثَالُهُ غَيْرَ مَرَّةٍ أَوْ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحُكْمِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمُ الدُّنْيَا وَالآخَرُ حُكْمُ الْعَقْنِي كَايَتَى الْيَمِيْنِ فِي سُوْرَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَالْمَائِدَةِ فَإِنَّهُ تَعَالَىٰ قَالَ فِى سُوْرَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ لايُوا خِذكُم الله باللغو فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ باللَّغْرِ وَلكِنْ يُؤَاخِذُكُمْ بِمَا كَسَبَتْ قُلُوْبُكُمْ فَقَوْلُهُ بَمَا كَسَبَتْ شَامِلٌ لِلْغَمُوسِ وَالمُنْعَقِدَةِ جَمِيْعًا فَيُفهَمُ أَن فِي الْغَمُوس مُؤاخَذَةُ وَقَالَ فِي سُورَةِ الْمَائِدَةِ لايُوا خِذكُم الله باللغو فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ وَلَكِنْ يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا عَقَدْتُمُ الأَيْمَانَ فَإِنْ المراد بما عقدتُم المُنْعَقِدَةُ فَقَط وَالْغَمُوسُ ههنا دَاخِل فِي اللَّغْوِ فَيُفهم أن لَا مُوَاخَذَةَ فِي الْغَمُوْسِ.
And as for when conflict occurs between two qiyas, then both will not fall, so that action according to the current state may occur, because under qiyas there is no proof to act upon except by acting according to the current state, and acting according to the current state is not a proof in our view, and in the case of donkey's urine, acting according to the current state is resorted to by necessity. Rather, the mujtahid acts upon whichever of them he wishes, by the testimony of his heart, meaning his heart inclines to one of the two qiyas to which he is at peace, by the light of insight that Allah has given to every believer. And according to al-Shafi'i, the testimony of the heart is not a condition, and because of this, he has two or more opinions in every issue at one time, unlike our imams, for two narrations are not reported from them in an issue except according to two times, but since the date is not known to act upon only the later, therefore the fatwa is circulated between them. Thus it is said. And since this was an explanation of real conflict, whose ruling is falling, now he began to explain apparent conflict, whose ruling is preference and reconciliation. So he said: The way out of conflict is either from the side of the proof, in that they are not equal, such that one is mashhur and the other ahad, and one is nass and the other zahir, then the higher is given preference over the lower, and its example has passed more than once. Or from the side of the ruling, in that one of them is a worldly ruling and the other is an afterlife ruling, like the two verses of oath in Surah al-Baqarah and al-Ma'idah. For Allah Most High said in Surah al-Baqarah: 'Allah will not take you to task for oaths you swear unintentionally, but He will take you to task for what your hearts have earned' (2:225). So His saying 'what your hearts have earned' includes both al-ghamus and al-mun'aqidah together, so it is understood that there is accountability in al-ghamus. And He said in Surah al-Ma'idah: 'Allah will not take you to task for oaths you swear unintentionally, but He will take you to task for what you have sworn deliberately' (5:89). For the meaning of 'what you have sworn deliberately' is only al-mun'aqidah, and al-ghamus here is included in al-laghw, so it is understood that there is no accountability in al-ghamus.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule exposition. It first addresses what happens when two qiyas (analogical reasonings) conflict. The Hanafi position is that neither qiyas falls; rather, the mujtahid can choose whichever his heart feels inclined to, relying on the light of divine insight. This contrasts with al-Shafi'i, who does not require this inward inclination, leading to multiple opinions on a single issue at the same time. Hanafi imams are not reported to have conflicting opinions on the same issue except across different times, but since the chronology may be unknown, fatwa can be given on both. The author then introduces 'mukhallas' (ways out of apparent conflict). There are two types: (1) resolution from the side of the proof, where one evidence is stronger (e.g., mashhur vs. ahad, or nass vs. zahir), and the stronger is preferred; (2) resolution from the side of the ruling, where each evidence applies to a different domain—one for worldly rulings and one for afterlife rulings. The example given is the two Quranic verses about oaths. The Baqarah verse appears to hold one accountable for false oaths (al-ghamus), while the Ma'idah verse seems to exempt such oaths. The apparent conflict is resolved by understanding that the Baqarah verse refers to worldly accountability (where the ruler may punish), while the Ma'idah verse refers to afterlife accountability (where Allah does not punish for unintentional oaths). Thus, both are applied without conflict.

Key Terms
شهادة القلب (shahadat al-qalb): The inner conviction and peace of heart that a mujtahid feels towards one of two conflicting evidences, based on divine insight.
مخلص (mukhallas): A way out of an apparent conflict between evidences, either by preferring the stronger proof or by applying each to different types of rulings.
يمين غموس (yamin ghamus): A deliberate false oath sworn with knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how does a mujtahid resolve a conflict between two qiyas?
A) He must accept both qiyas as equally valid and act on neither.
B) He chooses whichever he wishes based on the testimony of his heart (shahadat al-qalb).
C) He always prefers the qiyas that is based on a hadith ahad.
D) He must follow the earlier qiyas and ignore the later one.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conflicting qiyas are not automatically invalid; the mujtahid chooses by divine inner conviction.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Mukhallas: Resolving Apparent Conflict between Evidences
Usul rule explaining methods to reconcile apparent conflicting texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two types of mukhallas (from side of proof and from side of ruling) to resolve apparent contradictions between Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Apparent conflict in evidences is resolved by preferring the stronger proof or assigning to different ruling domains.

When two evidences seem to conflict, the conflict may be only apparent. The author introduces mukhallas: ways out. One type resolves by preferring the stronger evidence (e.g., mashhur over ahad). The other type resolves by assigning each evidence to a different type of ruling—worldly vs. afterlife. The example of the two oath verses from Baqarah and Ma'idah illustrates the latter. This lesson equips you with the tools to harmonize seemingly contradictory texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of mukhallas
The text categorizes mukhallas into two: those that pertain to the proof (al-ḥujja) where one evidence is stronger, and those that pertain to the ruling (al-ḥukm) where each evidence governs a different domain.
Mukhallaṣ literally means 'a way out' or 'savior' from conflict.
2
Understand preference by proof strength
If one evidence is stronger (e.g., mashhur vs ahad, nass vs zahir), the stronger is preferred and the weaker is left. This is a straightforward tarjīḥ.
Examples have been mentioned earlier in the text.
3
Recognize resolution by domain
When evidences apply to different domains (e.g., worldly rulings vs. afterlife rulings), both can be fully applied without conflict. This is tawfīq (reconciliation).
This method avoids having to declare one evidence abrogated or invalid.
4
Analyze the oath verses example
Verse 2:225 says Allah holds accountable for oaths 'earned by the heart', which includes yamīn ghamūs (deliberate false oath). Verse 5:89 says He does not hold accountable for unintentional oaths but only for deliberate ones (al-munʿaqida). The verses seem contradictory regarding ghamūs.
The apparent conflict arises because one verse seems to punish ghamūs, the other seems to exempt it.
5
Apply domain resolution
The Baqarah verse is assigned to worldly accountability (legal punishment by the ruler), while the Ma'idah verse is assigned to afterlife accountability (Allah's forgiveness). Thus both operate in their own spheres without contradiction.
This shows that both texts are preserved and applied.

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule exposition. It first addresses what happens when two qiyas (analogical reasonings) conflict. The Hanafi position is that neither qiyas falls; rather, the mujtahid can choose whichever his heart feels inclined to, relying on the light of divine insight. This contrasts with al-Shafi'i, who does not require this inward inclination, leading to multiple opinions on a single issue at the same time. Hanafi imams are not reported to have conflicting opinions on the same issue except across different times, but since the chronology may be unknown, fatwa can be given on both. The author then introduces 'mukhallas' (ways out of apparent conflict). There are two types: (1) resolution from the side of the proof, where one evidence is stronger (e.g., mashhur vs. ahad, or nass vs. zahir), and the stronger is preferred; (2) resolution from the side of the ruling, where each evidence applies to a different domain—one for worldly rulings and one for afterlife rulings. The example given is the two Quranic verses about oaths. The Baqarah verse appears to hold one accountable for false oaths (al-ghamus), while the Ma'idah verse seems to exempt such oaths. The apparent conflict is resolved by understanding that the Baqarah verse refers to worldly accountability (where the ruler may punish), while the Ma'idah verse refers to afterlife accountability (where Allah does not punish for unintentional oaths). Thus, both are applied without conflict.

Key Terms
مخلص (mukhallas): A way out of an apparent conflict between evidences, either by preferring the stronger proof or by applying each to different types of rulings.
يمين غموس (yamin ghamus): A deliberate false oath sworn with knowledge.
تعارض صوري (ta'aruḍ suri): Apparent conflict between evidences that can be resolved through preference or reconciliation.

Checkpoint
What is the method used to resolve the apparent conflict between the two oath verses (Baqarah 2:225 and Ma'idah 5:89)?
A) Abrogation (naskh) of the earlier verse by the later
B) Preference (tarjih) of Baqarah over Ma'idah because it is stronger
C) Assigning Baqarah to worldly rulings and Ma'idah to afterlife rulings
D) Combining both verses into a single ruling by taking the common meaning

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions are resolved by preferring stronger evidence or by assigning to different ruling domains, preserving both texts.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Binding Nature of a Companion's Opinion (Taqleed al-Sahabi)
Expansion of the rule that a Companion's opinion is binding and outweighs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that following a Companion's opinion is wajib and overrides qiyas, and explain the two arguments supporting this principle.

Core Idea
A Companion's opinion is stronger than qiyas because they witnessed revelation.

In Hanafi usul, the opinions of the Companions hold a special authority that goes beyond mere scholarly ijtihad. This lesson unpacks the rule that following a Companion (taqleed al-sahabi) is not just recommended but obligatory, and that it can set aside analogical reasoning (qiyas) from later generations. The passage provides two key justifications: the possibility that the Companion heard directly from the Prophet, and the intrinsic superiority of their understanding due to firsthand experience of revelation.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the central claim: 'Following a Companion is wajib and by it qiyas is abandoned.' Note that 'qiyas' here refers specifically to the qiyas of the Tabi'un and later scholars.
2
Understand the scope
Recognize that the rule does not apply to another Companion's qiyas; a Companion's qiyas is not abandoned by another Companion's opinion because of the possibility that the latter heard from the Prophet.
This shows a hierarchy: Companion's opinion > Companion's qiyas > later qiyas.
3
Explore the first justification
Analyze the argument from possibility of samā‘: even if a Companion does not attribute his statement to the Prophet, there remains a chance that he heard it from him. This possibility gives his opinion precedence over qiyas.
This is a probabilistic argument based on the Companions' proximity to revelation.
4
Explore the second justification
Consider the concession that the opinion is the Companion's own ijtihad (ra’y). The passage argues that even then, it is stronger than others' opinions because the Companions 'witnessed the circumstances of revelation and the illumination of the Shariah.'
This grounds the rule in the Companions' unique epistemological advantage.
5
Apply the principle
Conclude that in practice, a Hanafi mufti must follow a Companion's opinion over any qiyas from non-Companions, and that this rule underscores the elevated status of the Companions in Hanafi methodology.
This principle is a hallmark of Hanafi usul and distinguishes it from other madhahib.

Source Text

ثُمَّ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ تَقْلِيدِ الصَّحَابَةِ إِلْحَاقًا بِأَبْحَاثِ السُّنَّةِ فَقَالَ: تَقْلِيدُ الصَّحَابِي وَاجِبٌ يُتْرَكُ بِهِ الْقِيَاسُ أَىْ قِيَاسُ التَّابِعِيْنَ وَمَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ لِأَنْ قِيَاسَ الصَّحَابِي لَا يُتْرَكُ بِقَوْلٍ صَحَابِي آخَرَ لِاحْتِمَالِ السَّمَاعِ مِنَ الرَّسُولِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بَلْ هُوَ الظَّاهِرُ فِي حَقِّهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَنِدْ إِلَيْهِ وَلَئِنْ سُلِّمَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ مَسْمُوعًا مِنْهُ بَلْ هُوَ رَأَيْتُهُ فَرَأْيُ الصَّحَابِي أَقْوَى مِنْ رَأْيِ غَيْرِهِمْ لِأَنَّهُمْ شَاهَدُوا أَحْوَالَ التَّنْزِيْلِ وَاسْتِنَارَ الشَّرِيعَةِ فَلَهُمْ مَزِيَّةٌ عَلَى غَيْرِهِمْ.
Then he began the explanation of following the Companions, attaching it to the discussions of the Sunnah. He said: Following a Companion is obligatory; by it analogical reasoning is abandoned, i.e., the analogical reasoning of the Followers (Tābi‘ūn) and those after them, because the analogical reasoning of a Companion is not abandoned by the statement of another Companion, due to the possibility of having heard from the Messenger (peace be upon him); rather, it is the apparent (case) in his regard, even if he does not attribute it. And if it is conceded that it is not heard from him but rather it is his opinion, then the opinion of a Companion is stronger than the opinion of others, because they witnessed the circumstances of revelation and the illumination of the Shariah, so they have an advantage over others.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage addresses the principle of taqleed al-sahabi (following a Companion's opinion). The author states that following a Companion is obligatory (واجب) and that it can override qiyas (analogical reasoning) from later scholars like the tabi‘un and those after them. The reasoning is twofold: first, a Companion's opinion may be based on something heard directly from the Prophet (peace be upon him), even if not explicitly stated; therefore, it takes precedence over the qiyas of another Companion. Second, even if it is the Companion's own ijtihad (ra’y), it is stronger than the ra’y of others because the Companions witnessed the revelation and the inception of the Shariah, giving them superior understanding. The passage concludes that the qiyas of a Companion cannot be abandoned by another Companion's opinion due to the possibility of samā‘ (hearing). This principle is a key part of Hanafi usul, emphasizing the authority of the Companions' views in deriving rulings.

Key Terms
تقليد الصحابي (taqlīd al-ṣaḥābī): Following the opinion of a Companion of the Prophet Muhammad, which is considered obligatory and takes precedence over qiyas.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here it refers specifically to the qiyas of tabi‘un and later scholars, which can be abandoned in favor of a Companion's view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the opinion of a Companion stronger than the qiyas of later scholars, even if it is the Companion's own opinion (ra’y)?
A) Because Companions were infallible.
B) Because they witnessed revelation and the establishment of the Shariah firsthand.
C) Because they never engaged in ijtihad themselves.
D) Because their opinions were always based on explicit texts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a Companion's opinion is binding and takes precedence over qiyas from later scholars, grounded in the Companions' unique proximity to revelation.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
Definition of Qiyas in Language and Shariah
Introduction to Qiyas with linguistic and technical definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of Qiyas and identify its four essential components (asl, far', hukm, illah).

Core Idea
Qiyas is analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared cause.

This passage opens the chapter on Qiyas, one of the four primary sources of Islamic law in the Hanafi school. It provides both the lexical meaning ('estimation') and the technical meaning in usul al-fiqh. Understanding this definition is essential for mastering how Hanafi jurists derive rulings for new cases not explicitly covered by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
Qiyas in the Arabic language means 'estimation' (taqdir). This root concept helps us understand the technical usage as a form of measurement or comparison.
2
Identify the technical meaning in Shariah
The author defines Qiyas technically as 'estimating the branch by the original in ruling and cause' (تقدير الفرع بالأصل في الحكم والعلة). This expresses the core operation of analogical deduction.
The four key terms: original (asl), branch (far'), ruling (hukm), and cause (illah).
3
Break down the technical definition into components
A valid Qiyas requires four elements: (1) an original case (asl) with an established ruling, (2) a new branch case (far') not explicitly covered, (3) the original ruling (hukm) to be transferred, and (4) a shared effective cause (illah) that justifies the transfer.
In Hanafi usul, the illah must be appropriate (munasib) and not contradicted by a stronger text.
4
Appreciate the role of Qiyas in Hanafi usul
Qiyas is the fourth primary source of law after Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. It is used by qualified jurists to derive rulings for novel situations, ensuring the law remains comprehensive and applicable.
Hanafis accept Qiyas; some other schools (e.g., Zahiris) reject it, but the overwhelming majority of jurists accept it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ المصنف عن بحث الإجماع شرع في بحث القياس فقال: باب القياس. القياس في اللغة: التقدير. وفي الشرع: تقدير الفرع بالأصل في الحكم والعلة.
When the author finished the discussion of Ijma, he began the discussion of Qiyas, saying: Chapter of Qiyas. Qiyas in language: estimation. In Shariah: estimating the branch by the original in ruling and cause.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage marks the transition from the topic of Ijma to the topic of Qiyas (analogical reasoning). It provides the linguistic and technical definitions. Linguistically, 'qiyas' means estimation or measurement. Technically, in Shariah, it refers to extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a branch case (far') based on a shared effective cause (illah). This definition is foundational for understanding how Hanafi jurists derive rulings for new cases by analogy.

Key Terms
قياس (Qiyas): Technically, applying the ruling of an original case to a branch case due to a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Estimating the original by the branch
B) Estimating the branch by the original in ruling and cause
C) Arbitrary reasoning by jurists
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a disciplined method of analogical reasoning, not arbitrary opinion; it transfers a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.

Definition of Qiyas and Refutation of Objections
Defines qiyas and refutes objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas and refute three common objections against its validity.

Core Idea
Qiyas reveals the ruling already implicit in the text; it is not an invention but a manifestation.

The author has completed the discussion on ijma and now turns to qiyas, a critical source of Islamic law. This passage defines qiyas both linguistically and technically, carefully distinguishing it from alternative definitions. It then addresses three major objections raised against qiyas—based on the Quran, a hadith, and epistemological uncertainty—and refutes each, establishing qiyas as a valid proof by transmission and reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and technical definitions
Find the Arabic phrases for qiyas in language (al-taqdir) and in sacred law (taqdir al-far' bi al-asl fi al-hukm wa al-illa). Understand that the chosen definition minimizes deviation from the linguistic sense.
2
Analyze why the author rejects alternative definitions
The author considers two alternatives: 'transfer of the ruling' (ta'diyat al-hukm) and 'manifestation of a similar ruling' (ibanat mithl al-hukm). Notice why the latter is preferred—qiyas manifests, not transfers.
The ruling remains in the root; only its like is applied to the branch.
3
Trace the three objections and their refutations
List each objection: (1) Quran is complete, so no need for qiyas; (2) hadith condemning Bani Israel's qiyas; (3) uncertainty of the cause. Then match each with the author's response.
Pay attention to the refutation of the hadith: the condemnation was due to obstinacy, not proper legal reasoning.
4
Confirm the epistemological status of qiyas
The author concludes that qiyas is a proof (hujja) both naqlan (by transmission) and aqlan (by reason). The uncertainty of the cause does not prevent practical action, only certainty.
This aligns with the Hanafi position that qiyas yields zann (probable knowledge), sufficient for action.

الْقَيَاسُ فِي اللُّغَةِ التَّقْدِيرُ وَفِي الشَّرْعِ تَقْدِيرُ الْقَرْع بالأصل فِي الْحُكْمِ والعِلْةِ

قیاس کا بیان
مصنف جب اجماع کی بحث سے فارغ ہوئے تو انہوں نے قیاس کی بحث شروع کی اور فرمایا باب الْقَيَاسُ فِي اللُّغَةِ القیاس کے لغوی معنی تقدیر ( اندازہ کرنے) کے ہیں اور شرعی اصطلاح میں قیاس کہتے. ہیں علت اور حکم میں فرع کو اصل کے مطابق کرنا۔ (اصل کی علت اگر فرع میں پائی جاتی ہو تو فرع کو اصل کے حکم میں شریک کر دینا) مصنف نے قیاس کی دیگر تعریفوں کے مقابلے میں اس تعریف کو اختیار فرمایا ہے کیونکہ یہ تعریف معمولی تبدیلی کے ساتھ لغوی تعریف کے زیادہ قریب ہے اور وہ جو د ہم کیا جاتا ہے (یعنی اس تعریف پر اعتراض کیا جاتا ہے) کہ قیاس کے یہ تعریف معدوم کے درمیان قیاس کو شامل نہیں ہے جنون کے باعث عدیم المعتقل کو اس عدیم العقل پر قیاس کرنا جو صغیر سنی کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں میں اصل اور طرح کا اطلاق نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم اس کو تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ اصل اور فرع صرف موجودہ ہی پر بولے جاتے ہیں معدوم پر نہیں اطلاق کئے جاتے۔ قبل مو تعدية الحكم من الاصل الخ
And when the author finished the discussion of ijma', he began the discussion of qiyas and said: Chapter on Qiyas. Qiyas in language is estimation, and in sacred law it is the estimation of the branch to the root in ruling and cause. And it is only interpreted with this interpretation because it is closer to the language with little change. And what is imagined, that it does not include qiyas between two non-existent things, like qiyas of one devoid of reason due to insanity on one devoid of reason due to minority, because the terms 'branch' and 'root' are not applied to them, is false because we do not concede that 'root' and 'branch' are not applied to the non-existent. And it is said: it is the transfer of the ruling from the root to the branch, and that is false because the ruling of the root is established in it, it is not transferred from it; rather its like is transferred. And when it is said: it is the manifestation of the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned (root and branch) by the like of its cause in the other, so the word 'manifestation' was chosen because qiyas is a manifestation, not an establishment, and the word 'like' was added because what is transferred is the like of the ruling, not the very ruling. And it is a proof by transmission and by reason. And he only said this because some people deny that qiyas is a proof, because Allah said: 'And We have sent down to you the Book as a clarification for everything' so there is no need for qiyas, and because the Prophet said: 'The affair of the Children of Israel remained upright until the children of captives increased among them, so they compared what was not with what had been, and went astray and caused others to go astray', and because in qiyas there is uncertainty since it is not known that this is the cause of the ruling. The answer to the first is that qiyas reveals what is in the Book and is not separate from it. To the second: the qiyas of the Children of Israel was only out of obstinacy and stubbornness, while our qiyas is for manifesting the ruling. To the third: uncertainty of the cause in qiyas does not preclude action, it only precludes certainty, and that is permissible. Statement on qiyas: When the author finished the discussion of ijma', he began the discussion of qiyas and said: Chapter on Qiyas. In language, qiyas means estimation; in technical shar'i sense, qiyas is to make the branch correspond to the root in cause and ruling. The author adopted this definition over other definitions because it is closer to the linguistic meaning with minimal change. And the objection raised against it is that this definition does not include qiyas between non-existent things, like qiyas of one devoid of reason due to insanity on one devoid of reason due to minority, because the terms 'root' and 'branch' cannot be applied to them. The answer is that we do not concede that 'root' and 'branch' are only applied to existent things, not non-existent. Then [the text continues] the transfer of the ruling from the root to the branch...
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author first defines qiyas linguistically (taqdir, estimation) and technically (taqdir al-far' bi al-asl fi al-hukm wa al-illa, i.e., equating the branch to the root in ruling and cause). He explains why this definition is chosen: it is closest to the linguistic meaning with minimal change. A potential objection that the definition excludes qiyas between two non-existent entities (like a person insane and a child both lacking reason) is refuted by stating that terms 'asl' and 'far' can apply to non-existent. Other definitions of qiyas are considered: (1) transfer of ruling from root to branch — rejected because the ruling remains in the root; (2) manifestation of a similar ruling by a similar cause — preferred because qiyas reveals, does not create. The author then proves that qiyas is a valid proof (hujja) both by transmission (naql) and reason ('aql). Three objections are raised: (a) Quran is sufficient; (b) hadith: Children of Israel went astray by qiyas; (c) uncertainty of cause. The refutations: (a) qiyas reveals what is in the Quran; (b) their qiyas was obstinate, ours is for manifesting rulings; (c) uncertainty does not prevent action, only prevents certainty. The Urdu commentary summarizes and clarifies the Arabic.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): In language: estimation; in sacred law: equating the branch to the root in ruling and cause.
الأصل (al-asl): The root case from which a ruling is taken; it must have a textual ruling.
الفرع (al-far'): The new case for which the ruling is sought via qiyas.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause or attribute that is common between asl and far' and upon which the ruling is based.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, qiyas in sacred law is:
A) The transfer of a ruling from one case to another
B) The estimation of the branch to the root in ruling and cause
C) The establishment of a new ruling without textual basis
D) The preference of one proof over another

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid proof that manifests the ruling already present in the primary sources by equating a new case to an original case through a shared cause.
