Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Definition of Qiyas
Definition of Qiyas and its nuances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred Hanafi definition of qiyas, explain why 'ibana' and 'mithl' are used, and evaluate the applicability of qiyas to non-existent cases.

Core Idea
Qiyas clarifies a like ruling by a like cause; it manifests, not creates.

The Hanafi school defines qiyas with precision to distinguish it from mere transfer of rulings. This definition is chosen for its linguistic closeness and to address potential objections, such as whether qiyas applies to non-existent entities. Understanding this definition is foundational to grasping how analogy functions as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred definition
Locate the definition that the author presents as correct: 'إبانة مثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علته في الآخر'. Note the key terms: إبانة, مثل, حكم, علة.
The author rejects 'نقل الحكم' (transfer of ruling) because the original ruling remains with the asl.
2
Analyze the choice of 'إبانة'
Understand why the author uses 'إبانة' (clarification) over 'إثبات' (establishment). The text states: لأن القياس مظهر لا مثبت – qiyas reveals, not confirms.
This reflects the Hanafi stance that qiyas does not create new rulings but uncovers implicit ones.
3
Understand the addition of 'مثل'
The word 'مثل' (like) is added because what is transferred is a like of the ruling, not the identical ruling. This preserves the ruling's attachment to the asl.
The ruling of the asl remains; only a similar ruling applies to the far.
4
Evaluate the objection regarding non-existent cases
Consider the objection that qiyas cannot apply to two non-existent entities (e.g., insane and minor). The author refutes by asserting that 'asl' and 'far' can be applied to non-existent in legal reasoning.
This is a distinct Hanafi position; some schools require existence of asl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّمَا فُسرَ بِهَذَا التَّفْسِيرُ لأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى اللُّغَةِ بِقِلَّةِ التَّغَيرِ وَمَا يَتَوَهُمُ أَنَّهُ لا يَسْمَلُ الْقِيَاسَ بَيْنَ المَعْدُوْمَيْنِ كَقِيَاسِ عِدِيمِ الْعَقْلِ بِسَبَبِ الْجَنُونِ عَلَى عَدِيمِ الْعَقْلِ بِسَبَبِ الصِّغَرِ لأَنَّهُ لا يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ الْفَرْعُ وَالأَصْلُ فَبَاطِلَ لانا لأَنَّا لا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهُ لا يُطْلَقُ الأَصْلُ وَالْفَرْعُ عَلى المَعْدُومِ وَقِيْلَ هُوَ تَعْدِيَةُ الْحُكْمِ مِنَ الأَصْلِ إِلَى الْفَرْعِ وَهُوَ بَاطِلُ لأَنْ حُكْمَ الأَصْلِ قَائِمٌ بِهِ لا يُعْدَى مِنْهُ وَإِنَّمَا يُعْدَى مِثْلَهُ وَإِذَا قِيْلَ هُوَ إِبَانَةٌ مِثْلَ حُكْمِ أَحَدِ الْمَذْكُورَيْنِ بِمِثْلِ عِلْتِهِ فِي الْآخَرِ فَاخْتِيْرَ لَفْظُ الإيَانَةِ لاَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ مُظْهِرُ لا مُثْبِتْ وَزِيدَ لَفْظُ الْمِثْلِ لأَنَّ الْمُعْدَى هُوَ مِثْلُ الْحُكْمِ لا عَيْنُ الْحُكْمِ وَإِنَّهُ حُجَّةٌ نَقْلاً وَعَقْلاً وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ هَذَا لَأَنْ بَعْضَ النَّاسِ يُنْكِرُ كُونَ الْقِيَاسِ حُجَّةً لأَنَّ الله تَعَالَى قَالَ وَنَزَّلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ تِبْيَانًا لِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى الْقَيَاسِ وَلَأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ قَالَ لَمْ يَزَلْ أَمَرَ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ مُسْتَقِيمًا حَتى كَثُرَتْ فِيْهِمْ أَوْلَادُ السَّبَايَا فَقَاسُوا مَالَمْ يَكُنْ بِمَا قَدْ كَانَ فَضَلُّوا وَأَصْلُوا وَلاَنَّ فَى أَصْلِه شَبْهَةٌ إِذْ لا يُعْلَمُ أَنْ هَذَا هُوَ عِلَّةٌ لِلْحُكْمِ وَالْجَوَابُ عَن الأَول أَنَّ الْقَيَاسَ كَاشِفْ عَمَّا فِي الْكِتَابِ وَلا يُكُونُ مُبَايِنًا لَهُ وَعَنِ الثَّانِي أَنْ قِيَاسَ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيْلَ لَمْ يَكُنْ إِلا لِلتَّعَتُّ وَالعِنَادِ وَقَيَاسُنَا لِإظْهَارِ الْحُكْمِ وَعَنِ الثَّالِثِ أَنَّ شُبْهَةَ الْعِلَّةِ فِي الْقَيَاسِ لاَ تُنَافِى الْعَمَلَ وَإِنَّمَا تُنَافِى الْعِلْمَ وَذَلِكَ جَائِزَ أَمَّا النَّقْلُ فَقَوْله تَعَالى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الأَبْصَارِ لأَن الاِعْتِبَارَ رَدُّ الشَّيءِ إِلَى نَظِيْرِهِ فَكَانَة قَالَ قِيْسُوا الشَّيْءُ عَلى نَظِيْرِهِ وَهُوَ شَامِلٌ لِكُلِّ قِيَاسِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ قِيَاسَ الْمَثَلَاتِ عَلى الْمَثَلَاتِ أَوْ قِيَاسَ الْفُرُوعِ الشَّرْعِيَةِ عَلَى الأَصُولِ فَيَكُونُ إِثْبَات حَجَيَةِ الْقِيَاسِ بِه ثَابِتا بِالنَّصِّ وَحَدِيثُ مُعَاذٍ مَعْرُوفٌ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبيَّ صلّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِيْنَ بَعَثَ مُعَاذًا إِلَى الْيَمَنِ قَالَ لَهُ بِمَ تَقْضِي يَا مُعَاذُ فَقَالَ بِكِتَابِ اللهِ قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ قَالَ بِسُنَّةِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ قَالَ أَجْتَهِدُ رَأْيِي فَقَالَ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي وَفْقَ رَسُولَ رَسُوْلِهِ بِمَا يَرْضَى بِهِ رَسُولُهُ فَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْقِيَاسُ حُجَّةً لأَنكَرَهُ وَلَمَا حَمِدَ عَلَيْهِ وَلا يُقَالُ إِنَّهُ يُنَاقِضُ قَوْلَ اللَّهِ وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ مَبْحَثُ الْقِيَاسِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ فَكَيْفَ يُقَالُ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ فَىٰ كِتَابِ اللهِ لأَنَّا نَقُولُ إِنَّ عَدَمَ الْوِجْدَانِ لا تَقْتَضَى عَدَمَ كَوْنِهِ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَأَمَّا الْمَعْقُولُ فَهُوَ أن الاعتبار وَاجِبٌ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أَوْلِى الأَبْصَارِ وَهُوَ وَارِدُ فِي قُضِيَةٍ عُقُوبَاتِ الْكُفَّارِ كَمَا سَيَأْتِي فَمَعْنَاهُ وَهُوَ التَّأَمُلُ فِيمَا أَصَابَ مَنْ قَبْلَنَا مِنَ الْمَثَلَاتِ إِى الْعُقُوبَاتِ بِالْقَتْلِ وَالْجَلاَءِ بِأَسْبَابِ نُقِلَتْ عَنْهُمْ مِنَ الْعَدَاوَةِ وَتَكْذِيبِ الرَّسُولِ لِنَكُفَّ عَنْهَا احْتِرَازًا عَنْ مِثْلِهَا مِنَ الْجَزَاءِ.
And it is only interpreted with this interpretation because it is closer to the language with little change. And what is mistakenly thought that it does not include qiyas between two non-existents, like qiyas of one devoid of intellect due to insanity upon one devoid of intellect due to minority, because the terms 'far'' and 'asl' are not applied to them, [that] is invalid, because we do not accept that 'asl' and 'far'' are not applied to the non-existent. And it was said: it is the transfer of the ruling from the asl to the far', and that is invalid because the ruling of the asl is established in it and is not transferred from it; only its like is transferred. And when it is said: it is a clarification of a like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned [things] by a like of its 'illa in the other, then the word 'ibana (clarification) is chosen because qiyas is a manifester, not a confirmer, and the word 'mithl' (like) is added because what is transferred is a like of the ruling, not the ruling itself. And that it is a proof by transmission and reason. And he only said this because some people deny that qiyas is a proof because Allah said 'And We have sent down to you the Book as a clarification for everything' so there is no need for qiyas; and because the Prophet said: 'The affair of the Children of Israel remained upright until many children of captives appeared among them, so they analogized what was not [yet] by what was, and they went astray and led astray'; and because in its foundation there is ambiguity since it is not known that this is indeed the 'illa for the ruling. And the answer to the first is that qiyas is a revealer of what is in the Book and is not separate from it; and to the second, that the qiyas of the Children of Israel was only out of transgression and obstinacy, while our qiyas is for the manifestation of the ruling; and to the third, that the ambiguity of the 'illa in qiyas does not preclude action, it only precludes knowledge, and that is permissible. As for transmission: His statement 'So take heed, O you of insight' because 'i'tibar is the referral of a thing to its like, so it is as if He said: measure a thing by its like, and it includes every qiyas, whether it is qiyas of punishments upon punishments or qiyas of legal branches upon principles, so the proof of qiyas being established by it is established by the text. And the hadith of Mu'adh is well-known: it is narrated that the Prophet when he sent Mu'adh to Yemen said: 'By what will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will strive my opinion.' He said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of His Messenger to what pleases His Messenger.' For if qiyas were not a proof, he would have disapproved and would not have praised him. And it cannot be said that it contradicts Allah's statement 'And We have not omitted anything from the Book' because everything is discussed in the Quran through qiyas; how then can it be said 'if you do not find in the Book of Allah'? Because we say that non-finding does not necessitate its non-existence in the Book. As for the rational: indeed 'i'tibar is obligatory by His statement 'So take heed, O you of insight' and it is revealed concerning the punishment of the disbelievers as will come; so its meaning is contemplation of what befell those before us of punishments, i.e., chastisements by killing and exile due to causes transmitted from them of enmity and denial of the Messenger, so that we may refrain from them as a precaution against their like of recompense.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the definition and evidentiary status (hujjiyya) of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining why the chosen definition of qiyas is preferred: it stays closer to the linguistic meaning with minimal alteration. A potential objection is raised that this definition excludes qiyas between two non-existent entities, such as comparing an insane person (devoid of intellect due to insanity) with a minor (devoid of intellect due to youth), since neither would be called 'asl' or 'far'. The author refutes this, stating that the terms 'asl' and 'far' can be applied to non-existent cases in legal reasoning. Next, an alternative definition—'transfer of the ruling from the asl to the far'—is rejected because the ruling of the asl stays with it; only a similar ruling is extended. The accepted definition is: 'clarification (إبانة) of a like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned items by a like of its effective cause (علّة) in the other.' The wording is carefully chosen: 'إبانة' (clarification) because qiyas reveals a ruling, not creates it; 'مثل' (like) because what is transferred is similar to the original ruling, not the ruling itself. The passage then affirms that qiyas is a proof (حجة) both by textual transmission (نقل) and reason (عقل). Some opponents reject qiyas, arguing: (1) the Quran is a complete clarification, eliminating the need for qiyas; (2) a hadith says the Children of Israel went astray when they used analogy; (3) the 'illa (cause) is uncertain, making qiyas speculative. The author responds: (1) qiyas only uncovers what is already implicit in the Quran; (2) the Children of Israel's analogy was rebellious, while ours seeks truth; (3) uncertainty in the 'illa affects certainty but does not bar practical action. Then, textual proofs are provided: the Quranic verse 'فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ' (Take heed, O you of insight) is interpreted as a command to measure one thing by its like, encompassing all types of qiyas including legal derivations. The famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is cited: when the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) sent him to Yemen, Mu'adh stated he would judge by the Quran, then the Sunnah, then his own ijtihad (qiyas). The Prophet praised this, which would not have happened if qiyas were invalid. An objection that this contradicts 'وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ' (We have not omitted anything from the Book) is rebutted: not finding a ruling does not mean it is absent in the Quran; qiyas extracts it. Finally, the rational proof is that 'i'tibar (taking heed) is obligatory based on the same verse, which originally pertained to punishments but analogically applies to all legal rulings. The passage thus firmly establishes qiyas as a legitimate and necessary source of law in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): اصطلاحاً: إبانة مثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علته في الآخر (clarification of a like ruling of one of two things by a like of its effective cause in the other)
الإبانة (al-ibāna): الإظهار والإيضاح (manifestation and clarification); specifically, qiyas manifests a ruling, not creates it.
المثل (al-mithl): المساوي في الحكم لا نفس الحكم (the equal in ruling, not the ruling itself)
الأصل (al-aṣl): المقيس عليه (the base case from which analogy is drawn)
الفرع (al-far‘): المقيس (the new case to be analogized)
العلة (al-‘illa): الوصف المناسب الذي يترتب عليه الحكم (the appropriate attribute upon which the ruling is based)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author prefer the word 'إبانة' (clarification) over 'إثبات' (establishment) in the definition of qiyas?
A) Because qiyas is weaker than textual evidence.
B) Because qiyas only reveals a ruling already implicit in the sources.
C) Because 'إبانة' is a more eloquent Arabic term.
D) Because the Prophet used it in the hadith of Mu'adh.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas in Hanafi usul is a clarifier of a like ruling by a like cause, revealing implicit rulings without creating new ones.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Establishing Qiyas as a Proof (Hujja)
Proofs for Qiyas and refutation of objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main objections against qiyas, state the Hanafi responses, and cite the primary textual proofs (Quran and Sunnah) for its validity.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a valid proof by Quran, Sunnah, and reason; its uncertainty does not bar action.

Despite its importance, qiyas has been challenged by some groups. The Hanafi school defends it strongly, addressing objections from textual completeness, historical misuse, and epistemological uncertainty. Understanding these proofs is essential for any student of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
List the three objections against qiyas
Identify the three arguments opponents use: (1) Quran is complete, so no need for qiyas; (2) hadith that Children of Israel erred by analogy; (3) uncertainty of the 'illa.
These objections are presented in the text after 'وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ هَذَا لَأَنْ بَعْضَ النَّاسِ يُنْكِرُ'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to each objection
For each objection, note the rebuttal: (1) qiyas reveals what is in the Quran; (2) their analogy was rebellious, ours is truthful; (3) uncertainty does not preclude action.
The author stresses that qiyas is a kashif (revealer), not separate from the Book.
3
Identify the Quranic proof for qiyas
Locate the verse 'فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ' (Take heed, O you of insight). Understand that 'i'tibar means referring a thing to its like, thus commanding qiyas.
The verse is general, covering all analogies (punishments and legal branches).
4
Examine the hadith of Mu'adh as a Sunnah proof
The Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's method (Quran, Sunnah, then ijtihad) establishes qiyas as a valid source. The Prophet praised him, which would not happen if qiyas were invalid.
Also rebut the objection that it contradicts 'وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ' – not finding does not mean absent; qiyas extracts it.
5
Understand the rational (aql) proof
The verse 'فَاعْتَبِرُوا' is also a rational command to contemplate past punishments to avoid similar fates. This analogical reasoning is obligatory.
The rational proof is rooted in the same Quranic command, showing consistency.

وَإِنَّمَا فُسرَ بِهَذَا التَّفْسِيرُ لأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى اللُّغَةِ بِقِلَّةِ التَّغَيرِ وَمَا يَتَوَهُمُ أَنَّهُ لا يَسْمَلُ الْقِيَاسَ بَيْنَ المَعْدُوْمَيْنِ كَقِيَاسِ عِدِيمِ الْعَقْلِ بِسَبَبِ الْجَنُونِ عَلَى عَدِيمِ الْعَقْلِ بِسَبَبِ الصِّغَرِ لأَنَّهُ لا يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ الْفَرْعُ وَالأَصْلُ فَبَاطِلَ لانا لأَنَّا لا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهُ لا يُطْلَقُ الأَصْلُ وَالْفَرْعُ عَلى المَعْدُومِ وَقِيْلَ هُوَ تَعْدِيَةُ الْحُكْمِ مِنَ الأَصْلِ إِلَى الْفَرْعِ وَهُوَ بَاطِلُ لأَنْ حُكْمَ الأَصْلِ قَائِمٌ بِهِ لا يُعْدَى مِنْهُ وَإِنَّمَا يُعْدَى مِثْلَهُ وَإِذَا قِيْلَ هُوَ إِبَانَةٌ مِثْلَ حُكْمِ أَحَدِ الْمَذْكُورَيْنِ بِمِثْلِ عِلْتِهِ فِي الْآخَرِ فَاخْتِيْرَ لَفْظُ الإيَانَةِ لاَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ مُظْهِرُ لا مُثْبِتْ وَزِيدَ لَفْظُ الْمِثْلِ لأَنَّ الْمُعْدَى هُوَ مِثْلُ الْحُكْمِ لا عَيْنُ الْحُكْمِ وَإِنَّهُ حُجَّةٌ نَقْلاً وَعَقْلاً وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ هَذَا لَأَنْ بَعْضَ النَّاسِ يُنْكِرُ كُونَ الْقِيَاسِ حُجَّةً لأَنَّ الله تَعَالَى قَالَ وَنَزَّلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ تِبْيَانًا لِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى الْقَيَاسِ وَلَأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ قَالَ لَمْ يَزَلْ أَمَرَ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ مُسْتَقِيمًا حَتى كَثُرَتْ فِيْهِمْ أَوْلَادُ السَّبَايَا فَقَاسُوا مَالَمْ يَكُنْ بِمَا قَدْ كَانَ فَضَلُّوا وَأَصْلُوا وَلاَنَّ فَى أَصْلِه شَبْهَةٌ إِذْ لا يُعْلَمُ أَنْ هَذَا هُوَ عِلَّةٌ لِلْحُكْمِ وَالْجَوَابُ عَن الأَول أَنَّ الْقَيَاسَ كَاشِفْ عَمَّا فِي الْكِتَابِ وَلا يُكُونُ مُبَايِنًا لَهُ وَعَنِ الثَّانِي أَنْ قِيَاسَ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيْلَ لَمْ يَكُنْ إِلا لِلتَّعَتُّ وَالعِنَادِ وَقَيَاسُنَا لِإظْهَارِ الْحُكْمِ وَعَنِ الثَّالِثِ أَنَّ شُبْهَةَ الْعِلَّةِ فِي الْقَيَاسِ لاَ تُنَافِى الْعَمَلَ وَإِنَّمَا تُنَافِى الْعِلْمَ وَذَلِكَ جَائِزَ أَمَّا النَّقْلُ فَقَوْله تَعَالى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الأَبْصَارِ لأَن الاِعْتِبَارَ رَدُّ الشَّيءِ إِلَى نَظِيْرِهِ فَكَانَة قَالَ قِيْسُوا الشَّيْءُ عَلى نَظِيْرِهِ وَهُوَ شَامِلٌ لِكُلِّ قِيَاسِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ قِيَاسَ الْمَثَلَاتِ عَلى الْمَثَلَاتِ أَوْ قِيَاسَ الْفُرُوعِ الشَّرْعِيَةِ عَلَى الأَصُولِ فَيَكُونُ إِثْبَات حَجَيَةِ الْقِيَاسِ بِه ثَابِتا بِالنَّصِّ وَحَدِيثُ مُعَاذٍ مَعْرُوفٌ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبيَّ صلّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِيْنَ بَعَثَ مُعَاذًا إِلَى الْيَمَنِ قَالَ لَهُ بِمَ تَقْضِي يَا مُعَاذُ فَقَالَ بِكِتَابِ اللهِ قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ قَالَ بِسُنَّةِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ قَالَ أَجْتَهِدُ رَأْيِي فَقَالَ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي وَفْقَ رَسُولَ رَسُوْلِهِ بِمَا يَرْضَى بِهِ رَسُولُهُ فَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْقِيَاسُ حُجَّةً لأَنكَرَهُ وَلَمَا حَمِدَ عَلَيْهِ وَلا يُقَالُ إِنَّهُ يُنَاقِضُ قَوْلَ اللَّهِ وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ مَبْحَثُ الْقِيَاسِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ فَكَيْفَ يُقَالُ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ فَىٰ كِتَابِ اللهِ لأَنَّا نَقُولُ إِنَّ عَدَمَ الْوِجْدَانِ لا تَقْتَضَى عَدَمَ كَوْنِهِ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَأَمَّا الْمَعْقُولُ فَهُوَ أن الاعتبار وَاجِبٌ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أَوْلِى الأَبْصَارِ وَهُوَ وَارِدُ فِي قُضِيَةٍ عُقُوبَاتِ الْكُفَّارِ كَمَا سَيَأْتِي فَمَعْنَاهُ وَهُوَ التَّأَمُلُ فِيمَا أَصَابَ مَنْ قَبْلَنَا مِنَ الْمَثَلَاتِ إِى الْعُقُوبَاتِ بِالْقَتْلِ وَالْجَلاَءِ بِأَسْبَابِ نُقِلَتْ عَنْهُمْ مِنَ الْعَدَاوَةِ وَتَكْذِيبِ الرَّسُولِ لِنَكُفَّ عَنْهَا احْتِرَازًا عَنْ مِثْلِهَا مِنَ الْجَزَاءِ.
And it is only interpreted with this interpretation because it is closer to the language with little change. And what is mistakenly thought that it does not include qiyas between two non-existents, like qiyas of one devoid of intellect due to insanity upon one devoid of intellect due to minority, because the terms 'far'' and 'asl' are not applied to them, [that] is invalid, because we do not accept that 'asl' and 'far'' are not applied to the non-existent. And it was said: it is the transfer of the ruling from the asl to the far', and that is invalid because the ruling of the asl is established in it and is not transferred from it; only its like is transferred. And when it is said: it is a clarification of a like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned [things] by a like of its 'illa in the other, then the word 'ibana (clarification) is chosen because qiyas is a manifester, not a confirmer, and the word 'mithl' (like) is added because what is transferred is a like of the ruling, not the ruling itself. And that it is a proof by transmission and reason. And he only said this because some people deny that qiyas is a proof because Allah said 'And We have sent down to you the Book as a clarification for everything' so there is no need for qiyas; and because the Prophet said: 'The affair of the Children of Israel remained upright until many children of captives appeared among them, so they analogized what was not [yet] by what was, and they went astray and led astray'; and because in its foundation there is ambiguity since it is not known that this is indeed the 'illa for the ruling. And the answer to the first is that qiyas is a revealer of what is in the Book and is not separate from it; and to the second, that the qiyas of the Children of Israel was only out of transgression and obstinacy, while our qiyas is for the manifestation of the ruling; and to the third, that the ambiguity of the 'illa in qiyas does not preclude action, it only precludes knowledge, and that is permissible. As for transmission: His statement 'So take heed, O you of insight' because 'i'tibar is the referral of a thing to its like, so it is as if He said: measure a thing by its like, and it includes every qiyas, whether it is qiyas of punishments upon punishments or qiyas of legal branches upon principles, so the proof of qiyas being established by it is established by the text. And the hadith of Mu'adh is well-known: it is narrated that the Prophet when he sent Mu'adh to Yemen said: 'By what will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will strive my opinion.' He said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of His Messenger to what pleases His Messenger.' For if qiyas were not a proof, he would have disapproved and would not have praised him. And it cannot be said that it contradicts Allah's statement 'And We have not omitted anything from the Book' because everything is discussed in the Quran through qiyas; how then can it be said 'if you do not find in the Book of Allah'? Because we say that non-finding does not necessitate its non-existence in the Book. As for the rational: indeed 'i'tibar is obligatory by His statement 'So take heed, O you of insight' and it is revealed concerning the punishment of the disbelievers as will come; so its meaning is contemplation of what befell those before us of punishments, i.e., chastisements by killing and exile due to causes transmitted from them of enmity and denial of the Messenger, so that we may refrain from them as a precaution against their like of recompense.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the definition and evidentiary status (hujjiyya) of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining why the chosen definition of qiyas is preferred: it stays closer to the linguistic meaning with minimal alteration. A potential objection is raised that this definition excludes qiyas between two non-existent entities, such as comparing an insane person (devoid of intellect due to insanity) with a minor (devoid of intellect due to youth), since neither would be called 'asl' or 'far'. The author refutes this, stating that the terms 'asl' and 'far' can be applied to non-existent cases in legal reasoning. Next, an alternative definition—'transfer of the ruling from the asl to the far'—is rejected because the ruling of the asl stays with it; only a similar ruling is extended. The accepted definition is: 'clarification (إبانة) of a like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned items by a like of its effective cause (علّة) in the other.' The wording is carefully chosen: 'إبانة' (clarification) because qiyas reveals a ruling, not creates it; 'مثل' (like) because what is transferred is similar to the original ruling, not the ruling itself. The passage then affirms that qiyas is a proof (حجة) both by textual transmission (نقل) and reason (عقل). Some opponents reject qiyas, arguing: (1) the Quran is a complete clarification, eliminating the need for qiyas; (2) a hadith says the Children of Israel went astray when they used analogy; (3) the 'illa (cause) is uncertain, making qiyas speculative. The author responds: (1) qiyas only uncovers what is already implicit in the Quran; (2) the Children of Israel's analogy was rebellious, while ours seeks truth; (3) uncertainty in the 'illa affects certainty but does not bar practical action. Then, textual proofs are provided: the Quranic verse 'فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ' (Take heed, O you of insight) is interpreted as a command to measure one thing by its like, encompassing all types of qiyas including legal derivations. The famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is cited: when the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) sent him to Yemen, Mu'adh stated he would judge by the Quran, then the Sunnah, then his own ijtihad (qiyas). The Prophet praised this, which would not have happened if qiyas were invalid. An objection that this contradicts 'وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ' (We have not omitted anything from the Book) is rebutted: not finding a ruling does not mean it is absent in the Quran; qiyas extracts it. Finally, the rational proof is that 'i'tibar (taking heed) is obligatory based on the same verse, which originally pertained to punishments but analogically applies to all legal rulings. The passage thus firmly establishes qiyas as a legitimate and necessary source of law in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): اصطلاحاً: إبانة مثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علته في الآخر (clarification of a like ruling of one of two things by a like of its effective cause in the other)
الإبانة (al-ibāna): الإظهار والإيضاح (manifestation and clarification); specifically, qiyas manifests a ruling, not creates it.
المثل (al-mithl): المساوي في الحكم لا نفس الحكم (the equal in ruling, not the ruling itself)
الأصل (al-aṣl): المقيس عليه (the base case from which analogy is drawn)
الفرع (al-far‘): المقيس (the new case to be analogized)
العلة (al-‘illa): الوصف المناسب الذي يترتب عليه الحكم (the appropriate attribute upon which the ruling is based)
الحجية (al-hujjiyya): كون الشيء حجة يجب العمل به (the status of being a proof that must be acted upon)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof for qiyas from the Quran according to the Hanafi school?
A) 'يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَوْفُوا بِالْعُقُودِ'
B) 'فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ'
C) 'وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ'
D) 'أَطِيعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا الرَّسُولَ'

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid and necessary proof in Hanafi usul, supported by Quran, Sunnah, and reason, despite objections about completeness, historical misuse, and uncertainty.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Proof of Qiyas in Hanafi Usul
Defines qiyas and proves its authority via naqli and aqli proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas in Hanafi usul, distinguish it from a transfer of ruling, and identify the transmitted and rational proofs for its authority.

Core Idea
Qiyas manifests an existing ruling in a new case; it does not create a new ruling.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwaar introduces the Hanafi definition of qiyas (analogy) and establishes its binding authority as a source of law. You will learn why qiyas is not a transfer of the ruling itself but a manifestation of its like, and how the Quran and Sunnah provide both textual and rational evidence for its obligatory use. The lesson also addresses the objection that the Quran contains everything, showing that non-finding does not mean non-existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correct definition and its key components
Extract the Hanafi definition: qiyas is manifesting the ruling of the original in the branch when the cause is found. Note the rejection of 'transfer' and the inclusion of 'mithl' (like) and 'izhar' (manifestation).
The definition distinguishes qiyas from creating a new ruling.
2
Analyze the transmitted proofs (naqli)
Study the Quranic verse (59:2) and the hadith of Mu'adh. Understand how i'tibar means referring to a similar thing, and how the Prophet's approval proves qiyas is a proof.
The verse is general, covering all qiyas; the hadith shows practical application.
3
Examine the rational proof (aqli)
The text argues that i'tibar is obligatory to learn from past nations, and legal qiyas follows the same reasoning pattern: cause to ruling.
This is an analogy arguing for the validity of analogy itself.
4
Address the objection from Quran 6:38
Understand the objection that the Quran contains everything so qiyas is unnecessary, and the Hanafi response: non-finding does not equal non-existence; the Quran contains general principles that require qiyas.
This is a common challenge to qiyas.
5
Apply the definition and proofs to a sample case
Consider the case of deriving prohibition of hashish from khamr. Apply the definition: original (khamr), ruling (haram), cause (intoxication), and manifest that ruling in the branch (hashish) due to shared cause.
This is from the thamarah al-khilaf mentioned in the dispute map.

قیاس کی ایک تعریف یہ بھی کی گئی ہے کہ قیاس اصل سے فرع میں حکم کو منتقل کرنے کو کہتے ہیں یہ تعریف اطل ہے اس وجہ سے کہ اصل کا حکم اصل ہی کے ساتھ قائم ہوتا ہے اس سے متعدی نہیں ہوتا متعدی اس حکم کا مثل ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے قیاس کی تعریف کی گئی ہے کہ اصل ملت کی مانند فرع میں غلت پائے جانے کی صورت میں فرع میں اصل کے حکم کے ظاہر کرنے کا نام قیاس ہے اس لئے قیاس کی تعریف میں لفظ ابانت اختیار کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ قیاس مظہر حکم ہے مثبت حکم نہیں ہے اول لفظ مثل کا اضافہ اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ متعدی (جس ظلم کو ظاہر کیا گیا ہے) وہ علم کا مل ہوتا ہے عین حکم نہیں ہوا وانه حجة نقلاً وعقلاً اور وہ شرعی حجت ہے نعلی اور عقلی دلیلوں سے مصنف نے قیاس کے حجت ہونے کو بصراحات ذکر فرمایا کیونکہ بعض لوگ قیاس کو حجت نہیں مانتے بلکہ انکار کرتے ہیں اس وجہ سے کہ اللہ تعالی نے ارشاد فرمایا (1) وَنَزَلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الكِتابَ تِبْيَانًا لِكُن شتی (ہم نے آپ پر ایسی کتاب نازل فرمائی جس میں ہر چنے کا بیان ہے ) لہلہاتیاس کی حاجت نہیں ہے (۲) اسی طرح جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا لَمْ تَزَلَ أَمَرَ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ مستقيما الخ بنی اسرائیل اس زمانہ تک حق پر قائم رہے الله أما النقلُ فَقَوْله تَعَالى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الأَبْصَارِ لأَن الاِعْتِبَارَ رَدُّ الشيء إلى نَظِيْرِهِ فَكَانَة قَالَ قِيْسَوا الشيءُ عَلى نَظِيْرِهِ وَهُوَ شَامِلٌ لَكُلِّ قَيَاسِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ قيَاسَ الْمَثَلاتِ عَلى المَثَلاتِ أَوْ قَيَاسِ الْفُرُوعِ الشَّرْعِيَةِ عَلَى الأَصُولِ فَيَكُونُ اِثْبَات حَجَيَةِ الْقَيَاسِ بِه ثَابِتا بالنُص وَحَدِيثُ مُعَادٍ مَعْرُوفٌ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنْ النَّبي صلّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِيْنَ بَعَثَ مَعَاذَا إِلَى الْيَمَنِ قَالَ لَهُ بِمَ تَقْضِي يَا مُعَادُ فَقَالَ بِكِتَابِ الله قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ قَالَ يَستَنْةِ رَسول الله صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ مَالَ اجْتَهِدُ يَرَانِى فَقَالَ الْحَمْدُ للهِ الَّذِي وَفْقَ رَسول رَسُوْلِهِ بِمَا يَرْضى به رَسُولُهُ فَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنِ القَيَاسُ حُجَّةٌ لأَنكَرَهُ وَلَمَا حَمِدَ عَلَيْهِ وَلا يُقَالُ إِنَّهُ يُنَاقِصُ قَوْلَ اللَّهِ وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَكُلِّ شَيْءٍ مَبْحَثُ الْقِيَاسِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ فَكَيْفَ يُقَالُ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدْ فَىٰ كِتَابِ اللهِ لأَنَّا نَقُولُ إِنْ عَدَمَ الْوِجْدَانِ لا تَقْتَضَى عَدَمَ كَوْنِهِ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَأَمَّا الْمَعْقُولُ فَهُوَ إن الاعتبار وَاجِبٌ  ِلقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أَوْلِى الأَبْصَارِ وَهُوَ وَارِدُ فِي قُضِيَةٍ عُقُوبَاتِ الْكُفَّارِ كَمَا سَيَاتِي فَمَعْنَاهُ وَهُوَ التَّامَلُ فِيمَا أَصَابَ مَنْ قَبْلَنَا مِنَ الْمَثَلَاتِ إِى العقوبات بالقَتْلِ وَالجَلاَءِ بِأَسْبَابِ نُقِلَتْ عَنْهُمْ مِنَ الْعَدَاوَةِ وَتِكْذِيبِ الرَّسُولِ لنَكُفْ عَنْهَا احْتَرَارُ عَنْ مِثْلِهَا مِنَ الجَزاء. ترجمه تشریح أما النقل الج بہر حال نقلی دلائل (قیاس کے حجت ہونے پر یہ ہیں ) فقوله تعالی فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الانصار (1) اللہ تعالی کا قول ہے سو عبرت پکڑ والے بصیرت والد) اعتبار سے معنی شئی کو اس کی نظیر کی طرف لوٹانا گو یا حق تعالی نے فرمایا کہ شئی کو اس کی نظیر پر قیاس کرو۔ یہ تمام قیاسات کو شامل ہے خواہ عذاب کو امم سابقہ کے عذاب پر قیاس کیا جائے یا فروع شرعیہ کا قیاس اصول شرع پر ا کیا جائے لہذا قیاس کے حجت ہونے کا ثبوت نص سے مل گیا لہذا قیاس کا محبت ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ اور نہ حکم کا عبث ہونا لازم آمریکا ) حدیث معاذ مشہور (۲) تم اس کے حجت ہونے پر حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث مشہورہ وہ یہ ہے کہ جس وقت جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت معاذ کو (یمن کا گورنر بنا کر) یمن بھیجا تو دریافت فرمایا اور اگر اس میں بھی نہ پایا تب تو حضرت معاذ نے جواب دیا تو پھر اپنی رائے سے اجتہاد کروں گا تو آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا الحمد للہ کہ اللہ تعالی نے اپنے رسول کے قاصد کو اس چیز کی توفیق عطا فرمائی جس پر دور اضی ہے اور اس کا رسول بھی راضی ہے لہذا اگر قیاس حجت نہ ہوتا تو اس موقعہ پر آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ و سلم البتہ انکار فرمادیتے اور حضرت معاذ کے اس جواب اجتہد برائی پر الحمد للہ نہ فرماتے اس پر یہ اعتراض نہ وار د کیا جائے کہ یہ حدیث کتاب اللہ کی اس آیت وَمَا قَرْطَنَا فِي الكِتاب من شبی کے معارض ہے (ہم نے قرآن میں کوئی چیز نہیں چھوڑی) سب بیان کر دی ہے اور ہر شے قرآن مجید میں موجود ہے پس یہ کیو کر کہا گیا کہ فإن لم تجد فِي كِتَابِ اللهِ تَعَالیٰ کیونکہ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ پانے کا مطلب یہ نہیں ہے کہ قرآن میں موجود نہیں ہے کیونکہ عدم وجدان عدم وجود کو مستلزم نہیں) و المعقول فهذا الع اور بہر حال قیاس کے حجت ہونے کی عقلی دلیل (۱) یہ ہے کہ اعتبار واجب ہے اللہ تعالی کے اس قول کی بنا پر کہ فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الأبْصاویر آیت کفار کی سزاؤں اور عذاب کے بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے جیسا کہ منقریب تفصیل آجائے گی لہذا اختبار کے معنی تامل کے ہیں ان چیزوں میں جو ہم سے پچھلی امتوں کو غلط اب و بچے کسی کو قتل کیا گیا کسی کو جلاوطن کیا گیا وغیرہ بِاسْتبَاب نُقِلَتْ عَنْهُ جن کے. اسباب ان سے معقول ہیں کہ انہوں نے اللہ کے رسول سے دشمنی کی اور ان کی تکذیب کا ارتکاب کیا لنکف عَنْهَا اختر از اتا کہ ہم ان سے باز رہیں ان کی جیسی جزاؤں سے بچنے کے لئے۔ فَيَصِيرُ حَاصِلُ الْمَعْنى قِبْوَايَا أَوْلِي الأَبْصَارِ أحوَالَكُمْ بِأحوال هذه الكفار وَتَامَّلُوْا بِأنْكُمْ إِن تَقْصِدُ وَالعِدَاوَةِ الرَّسُولِ وَتَكْذِيبِهِ تُبْتَلُوا بِالْجَلاءِ والقَتْلِ كَمَا أبْتُلِى أُولَئِكَ الْكُفَّارُ بِهِ وَهَذَا هُوَ الثابت بِعِبَارِةِ النَّص وَالْقَيَاس الشرعي نظير هذا العاملِ فَكَما أن الْعَبَارَةَ عِنْةٌ وَالْعَقُوبَةُ حُكَمْ فَيَتَعَدَى مِنَ الْكَفَّارِ الْمَعْيُودِينِ إلى حال كُل أولى الأبْصَارِ فَكَذَالِكَ الْعِلْةُ الشرعية علةٌ وَالحُرْمَةُ حُكْمٌ فَيَتَعَدى
One definition of qiyas is that it is the transfer of a ruling from the original to the branch. This definition is incorrect because the original's ruling stands with the original itself; it does not transfer. What transfers is the like of that ruling. Therefore qiyas is defined as: manifesting the ruling of the original in the branch when the cause is found in the branch similar to the original. Hence the word 'izhar' (manifestation) is chosen in the definition because qiyas is a manifester of the ruling, not a positor of the ruling. The addition of the word 'mithl' (like) is because what transfers is the like of the ruling, not the ruling itself. And it is a proof by transmission and reason. The author explicitly mentioned that qiyas is a proof because some people do not accept qiyas and reject it. They say Allah said: 'And We have sent down to you the Book as clarification for all things' so there is no need for qiyas. Also the Prophet said: 'The children of Israel remained upright until...' As for the transmitted proof: His statement 'So take heed, O people of insight' because 'i'tibar' means referring a thing to its like. It is as if He said: 'Measure a thing by its like.' And this includes all qiyas, whether it is measuring punishments to punishments or measuring legal branches to principles. So proving the authority of qiyas by it is proven by the text. And the hadith of Mu'adh is well-known: that when the Prophet sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he said: 'By what will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will exert my opinion.' So he said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of His Messenger to what pleases His Messenger.' If qiyas were not a proof, he would have rejected it and not praised him for it. And it cannot be said that this contradicts Allah's statement 'We have not neglected in the Book anything' because we say: non-finding does not necessitate non-existence in the Book. As for the rational proof: i'tibar is obligatory by His statement 'So take heed, O people of insight' which is revealed concerning the punishments of the disbelievers, as will come. Its meaning is reflection on what afflicted those before us of punishments, i.e., penalties of killing and exile due to causes transmitted from them: enmity and denial of the Messenger, so that we refrain from them, guarding against similar recompense. So the outcome of the meaning is: 'Compare, O people of insight, your states to the states of these disbelievers, and reflect that if you intend enmity to the Messenger and denial of him, you will be afflicted with exile and killing as those disbelievers were afflicted.' This is what is established by the wording of the text. And legal qiyas is analogous to this reasoning: just as the punishment is a ruling that transfers from the specified disbelievers to the state of all people of insight, similarly a legal cause is a cause and prohibition is a ruling, so it transfers.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh. The author first rejects an incorrect definition of qiyas as 'transferring the ruling from the original to the branch' because the ruling itself does not transfer; only its like does. The correct definition is that qiyas is the manifestation of the original's ruling in the branch when the effective cause ('illah) is found. Qiyas is a manifester (muzhir) of the ruling, not a creator. The word 'mithl' (like) is added because what is transferred is similar to the ruling, not the ruling itself. The passage then proves that qiyas is a valid legal proof (hujja) using both transmitted (naqli) and rational (aqli) evidence. The transmitted proofs are: Quranic verse 'So take heed, O people of insight' (59:2) which commands i'tibar, meaning referring a thing to its like, thus establishing qiyas. The second proof is the well-known hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when he was sent to Yemen. The Prophet approved Mu'adh's method of using personal reasoning (ijtihad) when no text is found, which is qiyas. An objection is raised that this contradicts the verse 'We have not neglected in the Book anything' (6:38), but the author refutes it by stating that not finding a ruling does not mean it is not in the Book; the Book contains general principles. The rational proof is that i'tibar (reflection) is obligatory to learn from past nations' punishments, and legal qiyas follows the same pattern: just as the punishment for disbelievers is transferred to others due to the same cause (enmity and denial), similarly legal rulings transfer from original to branch due to shared cause.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Manifesting the ruling of the original in the branch due to the presence of a shared effective cause
الاعتبار (al-i'tibar): Referring a thing to its like, which is the basis of qiyas
الحجة (al-hujja): A proof or evidence that establishes a legal ruling definitively or probably

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi definition of qiyas include the word 'mithl' (like)?
A) Because qiyas transfers the exact ruling, not its like
B) Because what transfers is the like of the ruling, not the ruling itself
C) Because qiyas creates a new ruling similar to the original
D) Because the cause must be identical in original and branch

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a manifester (muzhir) of an existing ruling, not a creator, and its authority is proven by Quran, Sunnah, and rational necessity.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Proofs for the Authority of Qiyas (Analogical Reasoning)
Presents Qur'anic, hadith, and rational proofs for qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary textual and rational proofs for the authority of qiyas in Hanafi usul, and apply the istinbat chain to derive the ruling that qiyas is hujja.

Core Idea
Qiyas is proven by the Quran's command to use 'i'tibar', the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's reasoning, and rational inference from linguistic analogy.

In this lesson, we explore how Hanafi usul establishes the authority of qiyas as a source of Shari'a. The author presents both naqli (Quran and Hadith) and aqli (rational) proofs, demonstrating that analogical reasoning is deeply rooted in Islamic legal methodology. By understanding these proofs, you will see why the Hanafi school considers qiyas a fundamental tool for deriving rulings on new cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary Quranic evidence
Locate the verse 'Fa'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (Quran 59:2). Analyze the linguistic meaning of 'i'tibar' and how it implies qiyas.
The word 'i'tibar' means to cross over from one thing to its like.
2
Examine the hadith of Mu'adh
Find the hadith where the Prophet (saw) approves Mu'adh's use of ijtihad when no explicit text exists. Understand why this approval extends to qiyas.
The Prophet (saw) did not object, indicating qiyas is valid.
3
Trace the rational proof from the verse
See how the verse's command to reflect on punishments leads to an analogy between past nations and present believers. This establishes qiyas through 'dalalat al-nass' (indication of the text).
The author distinguishes between 'isharat al-nass' and 'dalalat al-nass'.
4
Analyze the linguistic analogy
Consider the example of the word 'lion' used metaphorically for a courageous man. This shows that analogy (qiyas) is inherent in human language and reasoning.
This reinforces the rational basis for qiyas.
5
Synthesize the evidence
Combine the textual and rational proofs to conclude that qiyas is a valid and authoritative source (hujja) in Hanafi usul.
The istinbat chain from the verse solidifies the ruling.

رہے تو تم بھی جلا وطن یا قتل کی سزائوں میں جتلا کئے جاؤ گے۔ جس طرح یہ کفار اس میں مبتلا کئے گئے تھے قیاس کا اتنا حصہ تو عبارت النص سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اور قیاس شرعی اس کی نظیر ہے ہیں جس طرح عداوت علت اور سزا اس کا حکم ہے جو کفار سابقین تمام ان لوگوں کی طرف منتقل کیا جائے گا جن لوگوں میں یہ علت پائی جائے گی ٹھیک اسی طرح عالیہ شرعیہ علت ہے مثلاً سکر (نشہ ہونا) علت ہے قمر کی حرمت کے لئے (حرمت حکم ہے البتہ متعین ہے حکم متعین کی طرح متعدی ہو گا۔ اس وقت قیاس کے حجت ہونے کی دلیل عقل سے ثابت ہو گی۔ حاصل کلام یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی کا قول فاعتبروا یا اولی الابصار اگر اپنے عموم پر جاری ہو کہ اپنی نظیر کی طرف لوٹائی جائے گی۔ اگر چہ آیت کا درود خاص کر عقوبات کے بارے میں ہے تو قیاس کے حجت ہونے کی تعلمی دلیل یہی آیات بن جائیں گی۔ یعنی اشارۃ النص سے حجیت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ عبادہ اس سے نہیں اگر چہ عقوبات میں شامل کرنے کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے کیونکہ آیت عقوبات کے موقع پر نازل ہوئی تھی۔ تو قیاس کے حجت ہونے کا ثبوت آیت سے عقلاً ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی دلالتہ النص سے ثابت ہو جائے گا نہ کہ قیاس سے ورنہ دور لازم آ جائے گا۔ مبحث القياس وكذالك التأمل في حقائق اللغة المبح (۲) اسی طرح الفاظ کے لغوی معانی پر غور کر سکے بطور استعارہ دوسرے معانی کے لئے ان کا استعمال شائع وذائع ہے قیاس کے حجت ہونے کی دوسری عقلی دلیل کا بیان ہے اور صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ خلا لفظ اسد کی حقیقت پر غور کیا جائے گا اور وہ وہیکل معلوم ہے غایت درجہ
Now, the textual proofs for the authority of qiyas are: His saying, the Exalted: 'So take heed, O people of insight.' The meaning of i'tibar is to return a thing to its similar. So the Exalted commanded to measure a thing by its similar. This includes all qiyas, whether punishment is measured against punishments of past nations or subsidiary legal rulings are measured against original legal principles. Thus the proof of qiyas being authoritative is obtained from the text, so its authority is established. And the famous hadith of Mu'adh. Its proof is that when the Prophet sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he asked him, and if he does not find [in the Book] then what? He replied: I will exercise my own judgment (ijtihad). The Prophet said: Praise be to Allah who guided the messenger of His Messenger to that which pleases Him and His Messenger. So if qiyas were not authoritative, the Prophet would have objected. The objection that this hadith contradicts the verse 'We have not left anything in the Book' is answered by saying that 'not finding' does not entail non-existence. As for the rational proof: i'tibar is obligatory based on the verse. The verse was revealed concerning punishments of disbelievers. So i'tibar means to reflect on the conditions of past nations who were punished for enmity. The result: 'O people of insight, compare your conditions to those of these disbelievers and reflect that if you persist in enmity and denial, you will be afflicted with exile and killing.' This is what is established by the text's wording. Legal qiyas is similar: just as enmity is the cause and punishment the effect, it extends from those specific disbelievers to all who share the cause. Similarly, a Shari'a cause is a cause and prohibition is a ruling, so it extends from the analogand to the analogate. Thus the authority of qiyas is then by rational proof. The conclusion: if the verse 'So take heed' is taken generally as returning every thing to its similar, even though it was revealed specifically about punishments, then the authority of qiyas is proven by transmission (naqlan) i.e., by implication of the text, not its wording. If it is restricted to reflection on punishments due to its context, then the authority of qiyas is proven rationally (aqlan) i.e., by indication of the text, not by qiyas itself, otherwise circularity would result. Similarly, reflection on the realities of language for metaphorical use is another explanation of rational inference: e.g., reflect on the reality of 'lion'—a known structure of extreme ferocity and courage—then this word is borrowed for a courageous man due to shared courage. So the meaning becomes: 'O people of insight, compare your conditions to those of past disbelievers...' This part is established by the text's wording. Legal qiyas is its counterpart. Just as enmity is a cause and punishment a ruling extending from those specified disbelievers to all people of insight, similarly a Shari'a cause is a cause and a ruling like prohibition extends from the analogand to the analogate. Then the authority of qiyas is proven rationally. The summary: if the verse is taken generally, its authority is by implication; if specifically, by rational indication. Similarly, reflection on linguistic realities for metaphor is common, and this is another rational proof: e.g., consider the reality of 'lion' as a known form of extreme ferocity and courage, then this word is borrowed for a courageous man due to shared courage.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage discusses the proofs for the authority of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author presents three types of proofs: textual (naqli) from the Quran and hadith, and rational (aqli). The primary textual proof is the Quranic verse 'fa'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (So take heed, O people of insight), where 'i'tibar' is interpreted as a command to perform qiyas—drawing an analogy between a known case and a new one. The author notes that this verse is general, covering both historical lessons and legal analogy. The second textual proof is the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when the Prophet sent him to Yemen. When asked how he would judge, Mu'adh replied that if he did not find a ruling in the Quran or Sunnah, he would exert his own reasoning (ijtihad). The Prophet praised Allah for guiding Mu'adh to what pleases Him and His Messenger. The author argues that had qiyas not been valid, the Prophet would have objected. An objection is raised that this hadith seems to contradict the verse 'We have not left anything in the Book' (Quran 6:38), but the author responds that 'not finding' does not mean the ruling is absent from the Quran; it could be derived implicitly. The rational proof is then elaborated: the verse commands reflection (tamul) on the punishments of past disbelievers. This reflection involves drawing an analogy: if one commits similar sins (enmity and denial of the Messenger), one will receive similar punishments. This is qiyas in action. However, the author distinguishes between the literal wording of the verse (which only speaks about punishment) and the underlying principle (illa). If we take the verse in its general sense (returning everything to its like), then the authority of qiyas is proven by textual implication (isharat al-nass). If we restrict it to punishments due to context, then the authority is proven rationally (by 'dalalat al-nass'—the indication of the text) without committing circular reasoning. The author also gives a linguistic example: the metaphorical use of 'lion' for a courageous man is based on the common attribute of courage, which is itself a form of qiyas. Thus, the rational basis for qiyas is ingrained in human language and reasoning.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): To return a thing to its like; to draw an analogy between a known case (asl) and a new case (far') based on a shared underlying cause (illa).
اعتبار (i'tibar): Linguistically, to pass from one thing to another; here, it means to consider and draw an analogy, i.e., qiyas.
حجية (hujjiyya): The quality of being a valid proof or authority in Islamic law.
اشارة النص (isharat al-nass): An implicit indication of the text that points to a ruling beyond its literal wording.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): The indication of the text that leads to a ruling through rational inference, not literal wording.
تأمل (ta'mul): Reflection or deep consideration, especially on past events to derive lessons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the significance of the phrase 'isharat al-nass' in proving the authority of qiyas from the verse 'Fa'tabiru'?
A) It means the verse literally commands qiyas on all matters.
B) It indicates that qiyas is implied in the general command to 'return everything to its like'.
C) It proves that qiyas is only valid for punishments.
D) It shows that the verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is an authoritative source in Hanafi usul, proven by the Quranic command to use i'tibar, the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's ijtihad, and the rational necessity of analogy in language and law.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Rational Proof of Qiyas: Linguistic Analogy and the Riba Hadith
Explains rational proof via linguistic analogy and the hadith on riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two rational proofs for the authority of qiyas (linguistic analogy and consensus) and derive how the riba hadith establishes the definition of qiyas as radd al-shay' ila nazirihi.

Core Idea
Qiyas is proven rationally by linguistic analogy and consensus, not by qiyas itself—avoiding circularity.

This passage presents the second rational proof for the authority of qiyas: the analogy of linguistic metaphor (isti'ara). Just as a word like 'asad' (lion) is used for a brave man due to shared bravery, a ruling is transferred from one case to another based on a shared 'illa. The author then clarifies that the actual proof of qiyas's authority is not qiyas itself but consensus (ijma), which provides rational evidence without circularity. Finally, the famous riba hadith is analyzed to demonstrate that qiyas is defined as 'returning a thing to its counterpart' (radd al-shay' ila nazirihi).

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic analogy (isti'ara) as a rational basis for qiyas
Reflect on how the word 'asad' (lion) is metaphorically used for a brave man because they share the attribute of bravery. This natural reasoning is analogous to qiyas shar'i: transferring a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa). This shows that qiyas is ingrained in human reasoning.
The analogy is not the proof itself but illustrates the rationality of qiyas.
2
Recognize that the authority of qiyas is proven by consensus (ijma), not by qiyas
The author asserts that the proof (hujjiyya) of qiyas is established rationally by the implication of ijma (dalalat al-ijma), specifically the consensus of the Companions on using qiyas. This avoids circular reasoning (dawr) that would occur if qiyas were proven by qiyas itself.
Ijma here serves as a rational proof, not a transmitted one; it is 'aqlan bi dalalat al-ijma.
3
Analyze the riba hadith to extract the definition of qiyas
The hadith 'Wheat for wheat, barley for barley... like for like, hand to hand, and excess is riba' establishes the principle of equality (mumathala) in exchanges. The author interprets this as the basis for qiyas: returning a thing to its counterpart (radd al-shay' ila nazirihi). The requirement of equality in quantity (kayl or wazn) indicates that rulings are transferred based on similarity.
The hadith is used to define qiyas, not to prove its authority.
4
Examine the grammatical analysis of the hadith to understand the conditional obligation
The command (amr) in the hadith can be read in the nominative (raf') as a nominal statement or accusative (nasb) as an imperative. The author prefers the imperative reading but clarifies that the obligation (wujub) is not on the sale itself (which is mubah) but on the condition of equality (mumathala). Thus the meaning is: 'Sell with equality' or 'Selling is obligatory only when equality is observed.'
This shows how Hanafi usul handles amr when the act's permissibility is known.

وَأَرَادَ بِالْفَضلِ فِي قَوْله وَالْفَضلُ رِبّوا الْفَضْلُ عَلَى الْقَدْرِ دُونَ نَفْسِ الْفَضْلِ حَتَّى يَجُودُ بَيْعَ حَفْنَةٍ بَحَفْنَتَيْنِ وَهُكذا إلى أنْ يَبْلُغَ يُصنف صا. او القیاس نظیرہ اور Section on Qiyas. Likewise, reflection (ta'mul) in the realities of language... (2) Similarly, one can reflect on the lexical meanings of words; using them metaphorically for other meanings is widespread. This is an explanation of the second rational proof for the authority of qiyas, and its form is: for example, one reflects on the reality of the word 'asad' (lion), and it is the known form, extreme in ferocity and utmost bravery. Then this word is used metaphorically for a brave man because of the commonality in bravery with the real lion, since bravery is shared between them. Therefore, the brave man is called 'asad' because of the attribute of bravery. And qiyas is its counterpart, i.e., qiyas shar'i is the counterpart of each of the consideration (ta'mul) in punishments for abstaining from their causes, and the reflection (ta'mul) in the realities of language for metaphorically using them. So the proof of the authority of qiyas is rational, by the implication of consensus (ijma), not by qiyas itself, to avoid circularity. And its clarification is that the clarification of qiyas in its being a return of a thing to its counterpart is established in his saying: 'Wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, gold for gold, silver for silver, like for like, hand to hand, and excess is riba.' And it is also narrated: 'measure for measure and weight for weight' instead of 'like for like'. The word 'al-hintatu' is narrated in the nominative (raf'), meaning the sale of wheat for wheat like for like, and it is also narrated in the accusative (nasb), meaning 'sell wheat for wheat' and wheat is measured by its kind. His saying 'like for like' is a condition (hal) for what preceded, as if it was said: 'Sell wheat for wheat while they are equal.' And conditions (ahwal) are stipulations (shurut), and the command (amr) is for obligation (ijab), and selling is permissible (mubah). So the command turns to the condition which is a stipulation, thus the meaning becomes: obligation of sale with the condition of equality and similarity, not the obligation of the sale itself. And by 'like' (mithl) he meant quantity (qadr), i.e., measured items in measured things and weight in weighed things, as indicated in another hadith: 'measure for measure' (kaylan bi kayl). And by 'excess' (fadl) in his saying 'and the excess is riba', he meant excess over the quantity, not the excess itself, so that selling a handful for two handfuls is allowed, and so on until it reaches... He said: 'Qiyas is its counterpart' meaning qiyas shar'i is exactly the counterpart of that reflection (ta'mul) that was commanded in the punishments of previous nations, so that people abstain from adopting their causes. And reflection on the reality of language was done to derive other meanings. Thus the proof of the authority of qiyas is established rationally by the implication of consensus (ijma), not by qiyas itself, to avoid circularity. And its detail: the detail of qiyas as returning a thing to its counterpart is established by the hadith that follows: the hadith is: His saying (peace be upon him): 'Sell...'
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on proving the authority (hujjiyya) of qiyas. It first presents a second rational proof: the analogy of linguistic usage (isti'ara). Just as a word like 'asad' is used metaphorically for a brave man due to shared bravery, qiyas shar'i transfers a ruling from one case to another based on a shared cause (illa). This shows that qiyas is a natural human reasoning process. Then the author asserts that the actual proof for qiyas is not qiyas itself but rather consensus (ijma) — specifically, the consensus of the Companions on using qiyas, which provides rational evidence (aqlan) without circularity. The text then introduces a hadith (the famous riba hadith) as evidence for the definition of qiyas as 'returning a thing to its counterpart' (radd al-shay' ila nazirihi). The hadith enumerates six commodities and requires equality in exchange. The author provides a detailed grammatical analysis: the hadith can be read with the nominative case (indicating a nominal clause) or the accusative (indicating an imperative). The preferred interpretation is that the command to sell is not obligatory but conditional — the obligation is to sell with equality (mumathala), not to sell per se. This establishes the principle of equivalence which is the essence of qiyas. The author also clarifies that 'like' means quantity (qadr) in measured or weighed items, and 'excess' refers to excess over the quantity, which is riba. Finally, the text concludes that the proof of qiyas's authority is rational via consensus (ijma), not via qiyas itself, to avoid circular reasoning (dawr). The hadith is used to demonstrate that the definition of qiyas is the return of a thing to its counterpart.

Key Terms
استعارة (isti'ara): Linguistic metaphor; using a word for a meaning other than its original due to a shared attribute.
رد الشيء إلى نظيره (radd al-shay' ila nazirihi): Returning a thing to its counterpart; the definition of qiyas.
مماثلة (mumathala): Equality or similarity; the condition in riba transactions that forms the basis of qiyas.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars; here used as the source of proof for qiyas (by implication).
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law; transferring a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is defined as returning a thing to its counterpart, and its authority is proven rationally by linguistic analogy and the implication of consensus, not by qiyas itself.

Proof of Qiyas from the Hadith of Riba
Textual analysis of the riba hadith as proof for qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the hadith of riba serves as proof for qiyas by identifying the grammatical and logical structure that yields the illa (cause) of genus and amount.

Core Idea
The hadith of riba does not command selling; it commands equality — establishing the illa for qiyas.

The authority of qiyas (legal analogy) is a foundational principle of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Its proof does not come from qiyas itself (to avoid circularity) but from rational evidence including ijma. The hadith of riba provides a scriptural anchor by showing how a ruling (prohibition of excess) is linked to a specific cause (genus and amount), which can then be extended to other cases. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and logical analysis of that hadith as presented in our source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its surface command
Read the hadith: 'Sell wheat for wheat... like for like, hand to hand; excess is riba.' Note the imperative form 'sell' and the condition 'like for like'. The text analyzes whether the command applies to the act of selling or to the condition.
2
Parse the grammatical structure
The commentary explains that 'like for like' is an adverb of state (hal). The word 'al-hintah' is read in both nominative and accusative, showing the phrase can be a generic statement or a direct command. The hal functions as a condition.
Hanafi principle: 'al-ahwal shurut' (states are conditions).
3
Apply the usul principle: command is for obligation, but attached to a condition
Since selling is already permissible (mubah), the command cannot be for the sale itself. Instead, it obligates the condition embedded in the hal. Therefore, the obligation is to sell with equality, not to actually sell.
Al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but when attached to a condition, it obligates the condition.
4
Extract the illa (cause) from the obligation of equality
The obligation of equality in amount between the six commodities implies that they are similar. Similarity requires both form (amount) and meaning (genus). Hence, the effective cause for the ruling of riba is genus and amount (al-jins wa al-qadr).
This illa becomes the basis for qiyas: any two items sharing genus and amount fall under the same ruling.
5
Conclude: the hadith proves qiyas by providing a scriptural precedent for cause-based extension
The hadith itself does not prove qiyas directly (that would be circular); rather, ijma and rational reflection confirm that the existence of a common illa justifies analogical reasoning. The hadith offers the foundational pattern.
The text states: 'the proof of the authority of qiyas is rational by the indication of consensus, not by qiyas.'

التَّسْوِيَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْقَدْرِ ثُمَّ الْحُرْمَةُ بِنَاءً عَلَى فَواتِ حُكْمِ الأمْرِ يَعْنِي حَيْثُمَا فَاتَتِ التَّسْوِيَةُ تَثْبُتُ الحُزمَةُ هَذَا حُكْمُ النَّص وَالدَّاعِى إِلَيْهِ فِى العِلْةُ البَاعِثَةُ عَلَى وُجُوبِ التَّسنرِيَةِ الْقَدْرُ وَالْجِنْسُ لأَنَّ إِيجَابُ التُنوِيَةِ فِي الْقَدْرِ بَيْنَ هَذِهِ الْأُمَوْرِ يَقْتَضَى أَنْ تَكُوْنِ أَمْثَالاً مُتَسَاوِيَةٌ وَلَنْ تَكُونَ كَذَالِكَ إِلَّا بِالْقَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ لأَنَّ الْمُمَاثَلَةَ تَقُوْمُ بِالصُّورَةِ وَالْمَعْنَى وَذَلِكَ بِالْقَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ
And qiyas is its like, meaning: legal qiyas is the like of each of the consideration in punishments to avoid their causes, and reflection on the realities of language and metaphor for them. So the proof of the authority of qiyas is rational by the indication of consensus, not by qiyas, to avoid circularity. Its explanation: that the explanation of qiyas in that it is returning something to its like is established in his saying: 'Wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, gold for gold, silver for silver, like for like, hand to hand, and excess is riba.' And it is narrated 'measure for measure and weight for weight' instead of 'like for like'. And his saying 'al-hintah' is narrated in the nominative, meaning selling wheat for wheat like for like, and narrated in the accusative meaning 'Sell wheat for wheat'. And wheat is measured by its genus. And his saying 'like for like' is an adverb of state for what preceded, as if it was said: 'Sell wheat for wheat' while they are equal. And adverbial states are conditions, and the command is for obligation, but selling is permissible, so the command is directed to the state which is a condition. So the meaning is: obligation of sale with the condition of equality and similitude, not obligation of the sale itself. And by 'like' he meant the amount: measurement in measured items and weight in weighed items, as evidence of what is mentioned in another hadith: 'measure for measure and weight for weight'. And by 'excess' in his saying 'excess is riba' he meant excess over the amount, not excess in itself, such that selling one handful for two handfuls is permissible, and likewise until it reaches a certain amount. Then the ruling of the text is: obligation of equality between them in amount, then prohibition based on the failure of the command's effect, meaning wherever equality is absent, prohibition is established. This is the ruling of the text. And the cause prompting it, the motive for the obligation of equality, is amount and genus. Because obligating equality in amount between these things requires that they be similar equals, and they will not be so except by amount and genus, because similarity consists of form and meaning, and that is by amount and genus.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the hadith of riba (usury) as proof for qiyas (legal analogy). The author explains that qiyas is not proven by circular reasoning but by consensus. The hadith commands selling six commodities like for like, hand to hand, and prohibits excess. The author analyzes the grammatical forms: 'al-hintah' in nominative implies a general statement, while accusative implies a command. The phrase 'like for like' is an adverbial state, making equality a condition. Since selling is inherently permissible, the command is for the condition, not the sale itself. Thus the obligation is to sell with equality, not to sell. The cause (illa) for the ruling is amount and genus, as similarity requires both. This establishes qiyas: if two items share the cause (amount and genus), the ruling of riba applies. The commentary also clarifies that small excesses (e.g., one handful for two) are not riba because the excess is not measurable by standard measures.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Legal analogy: returning a new case to a similar established ruling due to shared cause (illa).
الربا (al-riba): Usury or prohibited excess in exchange of certain commodities when unequal in amount or not hand-to-hand.
المماثلة (al-mumathala): Equality in amount and genus required for valid exchange of ribawi items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the primary proof for the authority of qiyas (legal analogy)?
A) The hadith of riba itself through its implication of equality
B) Rational proof based on consensus (ijma)
C) A direct Quranic verse
D) The precedent of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The hadith of riba establishes the illa (genus and amount) that forms the basis for qiyas, but the authority of qiyas itself is proven by ijma.
