Prerequisites and First Condition of Qiyas
Explaining the three essential matters for qiyas and its first condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three prerequisite matters for qiyas and apply the first condition to evaluate the validity of an analogical argument.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires evidence that a text is currently ma'lul and that the 'illah is distinct — assumption is not enough.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar clarifies a common misunderstanding about qiyas: it is not enough that a text has an 'illah in principle. For qiyas to be a valid proof, three independent matters must be established. The passage then introduces the first formal condition of qiyas: the original case analogized from must not have its ruling reserved exclusively for itself by another text. Understanding these prerequisites safeguards your own analogical reasoning and helps refute weak analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prerequisite matters for qiyas
Read the passage and extract the three matters that must be present for qiyas to be a hujjah. Focus on the phrases after 'الاول' and 'الثاني' and 'الثالث'.
The first matter is a general principle; the second and third require independent evidence.
2
Examine the hadith example for identifying the 'illah
The passage cites the hadith 'al-hanata bil-hanata'. Notice how it is used to illustrate the third matter: evidence that distinguishes the 'illah (equality in value and type) from other potential causes.
This is a classic example of how a text can indicate its 'illah explicitly.
3
Understand the first condition of qiyas
The passage states: the asl (original case) must not have its ruling restricted exclusively to itself by another text. Consider the example of Khuzayma, whose testimony was specially sanctioned. Why can't we analogize from such a case?
If the ruling is exclusive to a specific case, then its 'illah is not generalizable.
4
Apply the condition to a hypothetical
Suppose a text says: 'Permission for the traveler to combine prayers is specific to the traveler.' Could we analogize from this ruling to a sick person? Use the first condition to decide.
If the text explicitly restricts the ruling to a specific category, qiyas is invalid.
5
Prepare to construct a full qiyas
This lesson sets the groundwork. In subsequent lessons, you will learn the formal rukn, hukm, and methods of repelling opponent's qiyas. For now, memorize the three matters and the first condition.
They are the gatekeepers of valid analogical reasoning in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو
نور الانوار به جلد سوم
اور نصوص کے لئے علت کا ہونا نہیں اصل ہے یہ کہ اصل میں ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے وہم یہ کیا گیا ہے کہ کیا ضروری ہے کہ نص معلول بھی ہو (یعنی نص میں سے علت کا استنباط کیا جا سکتا ہوں تاکہ اس کو فرغ کی جانب متعدی کیا جاسکے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ تمام اصول میں خواہ وہ کتاب ہو یا سنت یا اجماع سب میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ کسی نہ کسی علت کے ساتھ مقبول ہوتے ہیں۔
اور وہی طیف فرع میں پائی جاتی ہے الا انه الله قیاس کے لئے صرف اصلی تقاضہ پر بھروسہ کرنا کانی نہیں ہے۔ بل لابد في ذالك من دلاله بلکہ یہ ضروری ہے کہ علت کی شناخت کی بھی کوئی دلیل ہو یعنی ایسی دلیل جو یہ بتائے کہ علمت نہیں ہے دوسری نہیں جیسا کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قول الحنطة بالحنطة
کو بمقابلہ حفطہ لانے اور سلام بمثل کہنے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے اس میں قدر و جنس کا ایک ہو تا علت ہے۔ وَلَا بُدْ قَبْلَ ذَالِكَ مِن قِيَامِ الدُّلَيْلِ عَلَى أَنْهُ لِلْحَالِ شاهِدٌ أَيْ عَلَى أَنْ هَذَا النَّصِ فِى الْحَالِ مَعْلُول مَعَ قَطْعِ النُّطْرِ عَنْ كَوْنِ الأصولِ فِي الأَصْلِ مَعْلُولَة فَقَولة لِلْحَالِ وَقَوْلة شاهدٌ كُنّى به عَنْ كَوْنِهِ مَعْلُولاً لأنه إذا كَانَ مَعْلُوْلاً بَعِلَّةٍ جَامِعَةٍ كَانَ شاهِدًا عَلى حُكم الفَرْعِ وَالْحَاصِلُ أنْ هنَا ثَلْتَهُ أُمَيْرٍ الْأَوْلَ أَنَّ الأَصل فَى كُلِّ نَصِ أنْ يَكُونَ مَعْلُوْلاً وَالثانى أن لابُدُ مِنْ دَلَيْلٍ مُسْتَقِل يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ هذا النَّمِ فِى الْحَالِ مَعْلُوْلَ بَقَطْعِ النظرِ عَنْ ذَالِكَ الأَصْلِ وَالثَّالِثُ أَنْ لَا يُدْ من دَلَيْلٍ يُمَيِّرُ الْعِلَّةٍ مِنْ غَيْرِهَا وَيُبَيِّنُ أَنْ هَذَا هُوَ الْعِلْةُ دُونَ مَا عَدَاهُ فَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَت هَذِهِ الثَّلْثَةُ فَلاَ بُدْ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْقَيَاسُ حُجةٌ ثُمَّ لِلْقَيَاسِ تَفْسِيرٌ لَغَةٌ وَشَرِيْعَةً كَمَا ذَكَرَنَا وَشَرْطُ وَرُكُنُ وَحُكُمْ وَدَفَع فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ بَيَانِ هَذِهِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ لأَجْلِ مُحَافَظَةِ قَيَاسِهِ وَدَفْعُ قَيَاسِ خَصَبَهُ فَشَرْطُهُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ الأَصلُ مخصوصا يُحْكَمِهِ بِنَ آخَرَ الظَّاهِرُ أنَّ الأصلَ هُوَ الْمَقِيْسُ عَلَيْهِ وَالْبَاءِ فِي حُكْمِهِ دَاخِل عَلَى الْمَقْصُورِ وَالْمَعْنِى أَنْ لا يَكُونَ الْمَقِيْس عَلَيْهِ كَخْزَيْمَةَ مَثلاً مَقْصُورًا عَلَيْهِ حُكْمُهُ بَنَ آخَرَ اذْ لَوْ كَانَ حُكْمُهُ مَقْصُورًا عَلَيْهِ بَالنَّصَّ فَكَيْفَ يُقَاسَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ وَلَا يُجوِّرُ أَنْ يُرَادَ بَالأَصْلِ النَّمِ الدَّالُ عَلَى حُكْمِ الْمَيْسِ عَلَيْهِ ويَكُونَ البَاهُ بِمَعْنِى مَعَ ادْيَكُونُ الْمَعنى جِيْنَيْدٍ أَنْ لا يَكُونَ النَّص الدال على حكم المقيْس عَلَيْهِ مَخصُوصًا مَعَ حُكْمِه بِنَ آخَرَ وَلاشك أن النص الآخر هو النص الدال على حكم المَقِيْس عَلَيْهِ.
نور الانوار جلد سوم
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو وَلَا بُدَّ قَبْلَ ذلك الخ اور یہ کی ضروری ہے کہ شناخت علت سے پہلے فی الحال وجود علت پر
ترجمہ و تشریح ہوئی دلیل قائم ہو یعنی اس بات پر دلیل ہونا چا ہیے کہ یہ نص فی الحال معلول ہے (یعنی جس نص سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے اس میں فی الحال علت موجود ہے اس سے قطع نظر کہ اصل میں اصول (یعنی نصوص ) علت کے ساتھ معلول ہے یا نہیں۔ پس ماتن کا قول "لیالی" کے معنی فی الحال" کے ہیں (یعنی استنباط کرنے کے وقت علیت کے موجود ہونے کی دلیل) اور مائن کا قول "شاہد سے کفایہ معلول ہونے کا کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ جب نص کسی ایسی علت کے ساتھ معلول ہو گی جو اصل اور فرع میں مشترک اور جامع ہے تو وہ نص حکم فرع کے لئے گواہ اور شاہدہ بن جائے گی۔ الحاصل:- حاصل اس بیان کا یہ ہے کہ قیاس کو حجت بناتے وقت ان تینوں باتوں کو مد نظر رکھنا چاہئے۔ (۱) ہر نص میں اصل یہ ہے کہ معلول ہو یعنی کسی علت کی معلول ہو۔ (۲) ایسی دلیل کا ہونا ضروری ہے جو اس بات کی نشاندہی کرے کہ یہ نص فی الحال اس علت کے ساتھ معلول ہے اس سے قطع نظر کہ اصل میں یہ معلول تھی۔ (۳) تیسری بات یہ بھی ہے کہ علمت کو غیر علت سے ممتاز کرنے والی دلیل بھی موجود ہوتا چاہئے جو اس بات کو بتائے کہ یہی علت ہے دوسری کوئی علت نہیں ہے جب یہ مذکورہ مینوں امور جمع ہوں گے تو ضروری ہے کہ قیاس حجت ہو۔
ثم للقياس تفسير لغة پھر قیاس کے لئے لغوی و شرعی معنی ہیں جیسا کہ ہم نے پہلے بیان کیا اور کچھ شرطیں اور ارکان و احکام اور وجوہ مدافعت بھی ہیں لہذا ان چاروں امور کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے تاکہ اپنا قیاس غلطی اور کو تاہی سے محفوظ رہے اور مخالف کے قیاس کو دفع کرنا ممکن ہو سکے۔ فشرطه أن لا يكون الأصل المخ شرائط قیاس (۱) قیاس کی پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل کا حکم خود اصل کے لئے مخصوص ہونا دوسری نعی سے ثابت نہ ہو مصنف کی عبارت میں اصل سے مراد مقیس علیہ ہے اور لفظ بخشیہ میں حرف بار مقصود ( مخصوص) پر داخل ہے مخصوص علیہ پر داخل نہیں۔ وَالْمَعْفى ألا يَكُونُ الخ متن کی عبارت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا مقیس علیہ ایسا نہ ہو کہ حکم مقیس مقصود اور منحصر ہو۔ دوسری نص کی روشنی میں مثلاً حضرت خزیمه فكيف يقاس عليه غيره تو پھر مقیس علیہ پر اس کے غیر کو کیونکر قیاس کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
علیہ
ولا يجوز ان يراد بالاصل اور متن میں مذکور لفظ اصل سے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ نص مراد لی جائے جو مقیس علیہ کے حکم پر دال ہے اور لفظ " بحکمہ " میں باہ کو " مع " کے معنی میں لیا جائے کیونکہ اس وقت معنی یہ ہو جائیں گے کہ البنص الدال على حكم المقيس علیہ وہ نص جو مقیس علیہ کے حکم پر دال ہے وہ مقیس علیہ کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے دوسری نص کی وجہ سے اور اس میں شک نہیں کہ وہ نص آخر وہ نص ہے جو مقیس علیہ کے حکم پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔
Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu commentary, volume 3 of Nur al-Anwar. And the texts do not have an 'illah; the principle is that this is an answer to an objection: it was imagined that it is necessary that the text be ma'lul (i.e., that the 'illah can be extracted from the text so that it can be extended to the branch). The meaning is that all principles, whether the Book, Sunnah, or Ijma', have the principle that they are accepted with some 'illah. And that ['illah] is found in the branch. However, for qiyas, it is not sufficient to rely only on the original requirement. Rather, there must be evidence for it, i.e., evidence that specifies the 'illah and not something else, like the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Wheat for wheat'... it becomes known that equality in value and type is the 'illah. And before that, it is necessary to establish evidence that [the text] is a witness for the present case, i.e., that this text is currently ma'lul, disregarding whether the principles are originally ma'lula. His saying 'for the present' and 'witness' are metaphors for being ma'lul, because if it is ma'lul with a comprehensive 'illah, it becomes a witness for the ruling of the branch. The conclusion is that there are three matters: first, the principle in every text is that it is ma'lul; second, there must be independent evidence that this text is currently ma'lul, disregarding that principle; third, there must be evidence that distinguishes the 'illah from others and clarifies that this is the 'illah and not something else. When these three are gathered, then qiyas must be a proof. Then qiyas has a linguistic and Shari'i interpretation as we mentioned, and conditions, pillars, ruling, and refutation. So it is necessary to explain these four to preserve one's own qiyas and repel the qiyas of an opponent. Its condition is that the asl (original) should not be specified in its ruling by another text. Apparently, the asl is that upon which measurement is made, and the 'ba' in 'hukmihi' enters upon the restricted. The meaning is that the measured-upon should not be such that its ruling is restricted to it by another text, like Khuzayma for example; if its ruling is restricted to it by text, then how can something else be measured upon it? And it is not permissible that by 'asl' is meant the text indicating the ruling of the measured-upon, and that the 'ba' is taken in the sense of 'with', because then the meaning would be that the text indicating the ruling of the measured-upon is not specified with its ruling by another text, and there is no doubt that that other text is the text indicating the ruling of the measured-upon.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, expounds on the prerequisites for qiyas (analogical reasoning) to be valid as a proof (hujjah) in Hanafi usul. The author begins by addressing the misconception that every text (nass) must inherently possess an 'illah (effective cause) for qiyas to proceed. He clarifies that while it is true that all primary sources (usul) — the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' — are generally based on some 'illah, it is not enough to merely assume this. For qiyas to be valid, three specific matters must be established: (1) that the text is, in principle, ma'lul (has an 'illah), (2) that there is independent evidence (dalil mustaqill) proving that this particular text is currently ma'lul, regardless of the general principle, and (3) that there is evidence distinguishing the exact 'illah from other potential causes. He illustrates this with the hadith 'al-hanata bi al-hanata' (wheat for wheat) from the riba regulations, where the 'illah of equality in value and type is identified. Only when these three conditions are satisfied does qiyas become a valid proof. He then transitions to the formal components of qiyas: its definition, conditions, pillar, ruling, and the means of refuting opponent's analogies. Specifically, he details the first condition: the asl (original case upon which analogy is based) must not have its ruling restricted exclusively to itself by another text. He clarifies that the word 'asl' here means the case being analogized from (maqis 'alayh), not the text itself. If a ruling is exclusive to a specific case by explicit text (e.g., the special status of Khuzayma's testimony), then analogy from that case is invalid. He also precludes an alternative interpretation that suggests the condition is about the text being unrestricted, confirming the Hanafi position that the asl's ruling must be generalizable.

Key Terms
علت ('illah): The effective cause or ratio legis that grounds a ruling and allows analogical extension.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared 'illah.
اصل (asl): The original case or text upon which analogy is based.
معلول (ma'lul): A text or ruling that has an 'illah; i.e., it is grounded in an effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT among the three matters necessary for qiyas to be a proof (hujjah)?
A) That every text is in principle ma'lul.
B) That there is independent evidence that the specific text is currently ma'lul.
C) That the 'illah is the sole reason for the ruling without any other cause.
D) That there is evidence distinguishing the 'illah from other potential causes.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is only a valid proof when three matters are met: the text is ma'lul in principle, evidence confirms it for this case, and the exact 'illah is distinguished — plus the first condition that the asl's ruling is not exclusive.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Necessity of Evidence for 'Illah in Qiyas
Explains the need for proof that a text has an active cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the requirement of proving the current existence of an 'illah in a text before performing qiyas and explain why such evidence is necessary.

Core Idea
Before analogizing, you must prove the text currently has a legal cause.

This passage clarifies a foundational prerequisite for qiyas: the original text (nass) must be shown to have a legally effective cause ('illah) at the time of deduction. The author distinguishes between the text's original causation and its current state, emphasizing that evidence for the latter is mandatory. Without such proof, analogical reasoning lacks a valid basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement
State that evidence is needed to prove the text is currently 'ma'lul' (has an active 'illah).
The passage uses 'ليالي' to mean 'currently'.
2
Understand 'ma'lul'
Recognize that a 'ma'lul' text is one whose ruling is linked to a specific, identifiable cause.
This is a key concept for qiyas.
3
Distinguish original vs. current causation
Note that the requirement focuses on the present existence of the 'illah, not whether the text was originally caused.
This prevents automatic assumption of causation.
4
Recognize the text as 'shahid'
Understand that when a text's 'illah is shared between asl and far', the text serves as a witness for the branch's ruling.
The commentator elaborates on this role.
5
Apply the rule
In evaluating a qiyas argument, always check if the original text has been proven to currently possess the claimed 'illah.
This is a critical step in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بُدَّ قَبْلَ ذلك الخ اور یہ کی ضروری ہے کہ شناخت علت سے پہلے فی الحال وجود علت پر ترجمہ و تشریح ہوئی دلیل قائم ہو یعنی اس بات پر دلیل ہونا چا ہیے کہ یہ نص فی الحال معلول ہے (یعنی جس نص سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے اس میں فی الحال علت موجود ہے اس سے قطع نظر کہ اصل میں اصول (یعنی نصوص ) علت کے ساتھ معلول ہے یا نہیں۔ پس ماتن کا قول "لیالی " کے معنی فی الحال“ کے ہیں (یعنی استنباط کرنے کے وقت علیت کے موجود ہونے کی دلیل) اور مائن کا قول "شاہد سے کفایہ معلول ہونے کا کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ جب نص کسی ایسی علت کے ساتھ معلول ہو گی جو اصل اور فرع میں مشترک اور جامع ہے تو وہ نص حکم فرع کے لئے گواہ اور شاہدہ بن جائے گی۔
And it is necessary before that... and it is necessary that before recognizing the cause, there is evidence for the current existence of the cause, i.e., it is necessary to have proof for the fact that this text is currently caused (meaning the text from which one derives [the ruling] currently has the cause present, regardless of whether originally the principles (nusus) are caused with a cause or not). So the author's statement 'لیالی' means 'currently' (i.e., evidence for the existence of causation at the time of deduction), and the commentator's statement 'شاہد' is deemed sufficient for being caused because when a text is caused with a cause that is common and comprehensive between the original and branch, that text becomes a witness for the ruling of the branch.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage explains a preliminary requirement for employing qiyas: one must have evidence that the original text (nass) is currently 'ma'lul'—i.e., it has an 'illah (legal cause) attached to it at the time of deduction. This is separate from the question of whether the text was originally caused. The author uses the term 'ليالي' to emphasize contemporaneity. The commentator adds that the text itself serves as a witness (shahid) when its cause is shared between the asl and far'. In short, before any analogical reasoning, the existence of the 'illah must be proven.

Key Terms
علت ('illah): The legal cause that links a ruling to its textual basis.
معلول (ma'lul): A text that is connected to an 'illah and thus serves as the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must be established before using a text as the basis for qiyas?
A) That the text is from the Quran.
B) That the text currently has an 'illah.
C) That the ruling is universally agreed upon.
D) That the text is from the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas requires prior proof that the text's ruling is currently caused by a specific 'illah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The First Two Conditions of Qiyas: Exclusivity and Conformity to Qiyas
Explains two conditions that prevent using a ruling as asl for qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that disqualify an asl from being used in qiyas, apply them to the examples of Khuzayma's testimony and forgetful fasting, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i on the latter.

Core Idea
An asl cannot be used for qiyas if its ruling is exclusive to it (makhsous) or if the ruling itself contradicts qiyas.

Qiyas requires a valid original case (asl). This lesson presents two critical conditions that render an asl invalid for analogy: when the ruling is proven by another text to be exclusive to that case (makhsous), and when the ruling itself contradicts the general principles of qiyas. The story of Khuzayma's testimony and the rule on forgetful eating during fast illustrate these conditions. Understanding these prevents unwarranted analogical extension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The text states that the ruling of the asl must not be shown by another text to be exclusive to it. This is the first condition of qiyas. Locate the sentence that expresses this (beginning 'فشرطه أن لا يكون الأصل...').
The phrase 'مخصوص بحكمه' means specific in its ruling.
2
Analyze the Khuzayma example
Read the hadith and the explanation. Why is Khuzayma's testimony exclusive? The Prophet said 'Whoever Khuzayma testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' This ruling is given as an honor and cannot be analogized to others, even the Rightly Guided Caliphs.
The exclusivity is proven by the explicit text (nas).
3
Identify the second condition
The second condition is that the asl must not itself be contrary to qiyas. Find the example of forgetful fasting. Qiyas would require the fast to be nullified by eating, but the hadith explicitly maintains it. Thus it contradicts qiyas and cannot be used as an asl.
A ruling that is an exception to qiyas cannot serve as a basis for further qiyas.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The text notes that Shafi'i analogizes the mistaken and coerced to the forgetful, considering the cause to be lack of intent. The Hanafi response: the forgetful case is an exception, so it cannot be extended. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, fast of mistaken/coerced is nullified; in Shafi'i it is valid.
This difference stems from whether the forgetful case is considered makhsous.
5
Apply the conditions to a new scenario
Consider the special permission for the Prophet to marry more than four wives. Is this ruling exclusive? Use the first condition: it is proven by Quranic text to be specific to the Prophet, so it cannot be used as an asl for qiyas for others.
This reinforces the understanding of exclusivity (makhsous).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فشرطه أن لا يكون الأصل المخ شرائط قیاس (۱) قیاس کی پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل کا حکم خود اصل کے لئے مخصوص ہونا دوسری نعی سے ثابت نہ ہو مصنف کی عبارت میں اصل سے مراد مقیس علیہ ہے اور لفظ بخشیہ میں حرف بار مقصود ( مخصوص) پر داخل ہے مخصوص علیہ پر داخل نہیں۔ وَالْمَعْفى ألا يَكُونُ الخ متن کی عبارت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا مقیس علیہ ایسا نہ ہو کہ حکم مقیس مقصود اور منحصر ہو۔ دوسری نص کی روشنی میں مثلاً حضرت خزیمه فكيف يقاس عليه غيره تو پھر مقیس علیہ پر اس کے غیر کو کیونکر قیاس کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ علیہ ولا يجوز ان يراد بالاصل اور متن میں مذکور لفظ اصل سے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ نص مراد لی جائے جو مقیس علیہ کے حکم پر دال ہے اور لفظ " بحکمہ " میں باہ کو " مع " کے معنی میں لیا جائے کیونکہ اس وقت معنی یہ ہو جائیں گے کہ البنص الدال على حكم المقيس علیہ وہ نص جو مقیس علیہ کے حکم پر دال ہے وہ مقیس علیہ کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے دوسری نص کی وجہ سے اور اس میں شک نہیں کہ وہ نص آخر وہ نص ہے جو مقیس علیہ کے حکم پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ كَشَهَادَةِ خَزَيْمَةَ وَحْدَةً فَإنَّهُ مَخصُوص بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ شَهِدَ لَهُ خَزَيْمَةُ فَهُوَ حَسَنبُهُ وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَن يُقَاسَ عَلَيْهِ مَنْ هُوَ أَعْلَى حَالاً مِنْهُ كَالْمُلْفَاءِ الرَّاشِدِيْنَ إِذْ تَبْطَلُ حِينَئِذٍ كَرَامَةُ اختصاصيه بهذا الحُكْمِ وَقِصْتُه مَاروىَ أَنَّ النَّبِيِّ صلى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ اسْتَرَى نَاقَةٌ مِنْ أَعْرَابِي وَأَوْفَاهُ الثَّمَنَ فَانْكَرَ الأَعْرَابِي اسْتِيْفَاءَهُ وقَالَ هَلم شهيدا فَقَالَ مَنْ يَشْهَدَلِي وَلَمْ يَحْضُرُ نِي أَحَدٌ فَقَالَ خَزَيْمَةُ أَنَا هَلُمَّ أَشْهَدُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنَّكَ أَنفِيَتْ الأَعْرَابِي ثَمَنَ النَّاقَةِ فَقَالَ كَيْفَ تَشْهَدُ لِي وَلَمْ تُحْضَرْ نِي فَقَالَ يَارَسُوْلَ اللهِ إِنَّا نُصَدِّقُكَ فِيْمَا تَاتِيْنَا بِهِ مِنْ خَيْرٍ السَّمَاءِ أَفَلاً نُصَدِّقُكَ فِيْمَا تُخْبِرُ بِهِ مِنْ أَدَاءِ ثَمَنِ النَّاقَةِ فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ شَهِدَ لَهُ خزيمَةٌ فَهُوَ حَسبُه فَجُعِلْتُ شَهَادَتُه كَشَهَادَةٍ رَجُلَيْنِ كَرَامَةً وَتَقْضِيْلاً عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مَعَ أَن النُّصوص أوْجَبَتْ إِسْتِرَاطُ لِعَدَدِ فِي حَقِّ الْعَامَّةِ فَلَايُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ وَأنْ لايَكُونَ مَعْدُولاً به عَنِ الْقَيَاسِ أنْ لاَ يَكُونُ الْأَصْلُ مُخَالِفًا لِلْقَيَاسِ إذْ لَوَكَانَ هُوَ بِنَفْسِهِ مُخَالِفًا لِلْقَيْاسِ فَكَيْف يُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ كَبَقَاءِ الصَّوْمِ مَعَ الأكل والشرب نَاسِيًا فَإِنَّهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِلْقَيَاسِ إِذِ الْقَيَاسُ يَقْتَضِئُ فَسَيَادَ الصُّوْمِ به وَإِنَّمَا أبْقَيْنَاهُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لِلذى أكل نَاسيًا ثُمَّ عَلَى صَوْمِكَ فَإِنَّمَا أَطْعَمَكَ اللهُ وَسَقَاكَ اللهُ فَلا يُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ الْخَاطِئ وَالْمُكْرَهُ كَمَا قَاسَهُمَا الشَّافَعِي.
So its condition is that the asl... conditions of qiyas: (1) The first condition of qiyas is that the ruling of the asl is specific to the asl itself, not established by another text. In the author's expression, 'asl' means the object of analogy (maqis alayh), and the letter 'ba' in the word 'bikhushiya' [؟] enters upon the intended (makhsus) not upon the object of specification. And the intended meaning is that the object of analogy (maqis alayh) should not be such that the ruling is intended and restricted to it in the light of another text. For example, Hadrat Khuzayma, how can others be analogized to him? And it is not permissible that by 'asl' mentioned in the text is meant the text that indicates the ruling of the object of analogy, and the 'ba' in 'bihukmihi' is taken in the sense of 'with', because then the meaning would become: 'The text that indicates the ruling of the object of analogy is not specific to it due to another text', and there is no doubt that that other text is the one that indicates the ruling of the object of analogy. Like the testimony of Khuzayma alone, for it is specific to him by the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever Khuzayma testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' And it is not appropriate to analogize to him one who is in a higher state, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, because then the special honor of being singled out with this ruling would be nullified. The story is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) bought a camel from a Bedouin and paid him the full price. The Bedouin denied receiving it and said, 'Bring a witness.' The Prophet said, 'Who will testify for me?' And no one was present. Then Khuzayma said, 'I will testify, O Messenger of Allah, that you have paid the Bedouin the price of the camel.' The Prophet said, 'How can you testify for me when you were not present?' He said, 'O Messenger of Allah, we believe you regarding what you bring from the heaven, so should we not believe you regarding what you inform about the payment of the camel's price?' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Whoever Khuzayma testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' So his testimony was made like the testimony of two men as an honor and distinction over others, even though the texts require the condition of number for the public. So no one else may be analogized to him. And [the second condition] is that the asl should not be contrary to qiyas itself; for if it itself contradicts qiyas, how can others be analogized to it? Like the continuation of fasting despite eating and drinking forgetfully, for it contradicts qiyas because qiyas would require the nullification of the fast thereby; we only maintain it due to his statement (peace be upon him) to the one who ate forgetfully: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed and gave you drink.' So the mistaken and the coerced cannot be analogized to it, as Shafi'i analogized them.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage details the first two conditions for the validity of qiyas. The first condition is that the ruling of the original (asl) must not be proven by another text to be exclusive to that original. If a ruling is uniquely assigned to a specific case (like the acceptance of Khuzayma's solitary testimony), then that case cannot be used as an analogical basis for others, even if those others are superior in rank. The story of Khuzayma illustrates this: the Prophet's special declaration made his testimony equivalent to two witnesses, and this honor is specific to him. The second condition is that the original must not itself be contrary to qiyas. An example is the ruling that fasting remains valid despite forgetful eating and drinking. Qiyas would suggest the fast breaks, but the hadith explicitly maintains its validity. Hence, this exceptional ruling cannot be extended by analogy to the mistaken or coerced person, unlike the Shafi'i view which does extend it. The passage emphasizes that each condition prevents unwarranted analogical extension.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): The source case in qiyas (maqis alayh) whose ruling is used as the basis for analogy.
مخصوص (makhsous): A ruling that is specifically assigned to a particular entity and not generalizable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't the acceptance of Khuzayma's solitary testimony be analogized to other Companions?
A) Because Khuzayma was a close companion.
B) Because the ruling is proven by a separate text to be exclusive to him.
C) Because other Companions are of higher status.
D) Because qiyas cannot be used in matters of testimony.

Key Takeaway
An asl must not have its ruling made exclusive by another text, nor be itself contrary to qiyas, otherwise analogy from it is invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for Valid Qiyas: Exception of Khuzaymah and the Need for a Non-Exceptional Asl
Commentary on conditions for qiyas with examples from Khuzaymah and fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi condition that the original ruling (asl) in qiyas must not be an exception to the general rule, using the cases of Khuzaymah and forgetful fasting.

Core Idea
A qiyas cannot be based on an original ruling that is itself an exception — that would break the chain of analogy.

This passage from a commentary on Nur al-Anwar explains the strict conditions for valid qiyas in Hanafi usul. The author uses two powerful examples: the testimony of Khuzaymah, which is a special karamah not generalizable, and the ruling that forgetful eating does not invalidate fasting, which is an exception to the general principle. Both illustrate the key rule: if the original ruling (asl) contradicts qiyas (i.e., is an exception), it cannot be used as a basis for analogy. We will break down the conditions and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding extending the fasting concession to cases of mistake and coercion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Khuzaymah exception
Recognize that the single testimony of Khuzaymah was accepted due to a specific hadith making it a karamah. This ruling is an exception to the general rule requiring two witnesses.
The story illustrates that the ruling is particular to Khuzaymah and cannot be analogized even to higher-ranking Companions.
2
Understand the condition 'asl must not be contrary to qiyas'
The author states that if the original ruling itself is an exception to the general principle (contrary to qiyas), it cannot serve as a basis for analogy. The fasting example demonstrates this.
General qiyas would invalidate the fast due to eating/drinking, but the hadith makes an exception for forgetfulness.
3
Analyze the fasting analogy dispute
Contrast the Hanafi position (exception stays limited to forgetfulness) with the Shafi'i position (analogized to mistaken and coerced). Note the thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi fiqh, mistaken/coerced fast invalid; in Shafi'i, valid.
The Hanafi response is that the original ruling is an exception, so it cannot be used as an asl.
4
Summarize the four sub-conditions
The second main condition (textual ruling extended identically to a parallel branch) actually comprises four sub-conditions: shar'i ruling, identical extension, branch must be parallel, no text in branch.
These are derived from the single condition stated by the author.
5
Apply the logic to a contemporary example
Consider whether a new case can be analogized: e.g., if a specific concession is given to a particular person, it cannot be extended to others by qiyas.
This reinforces the principle that exceptions are not generalizable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَشَهَادَةِ خَزَيْمَةَ وَحْدَةً فَإِنَّهُ مَخْصُوصٌ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ شَهِدَ لَهُ خَزَيْمَةُ فَهُوَ حَسْبُهُ وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُقَاسَ عَلَيْهِ مَنْ هُوَ أَعْلَى حَالًا مِنْهُ كَالْخُلَفَاءِ الرَّاشِدِينَ إِذْ تَبْطُلُ حِينَئِذٍ كَرَامَةُ اخْتِصَاصِهِ بِهَذَا الْحُكْمِ وَقِصَّتُهُ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ اشْتَرَى نَاقَةً مِنْ أَعْرَابِيٍّ وَأَوْفَاهُ الثَّمَنَ فَأَنْكَرَ الْأَعْرَابِيُّ اسْتِيفَاءَهُ وَقَالَ هَلُمَّ شَهِيدًا فَقَالَ مَنْ يَشْهَدُ لِي وَلَمْ يَحْضُرْنِي أَحَدٌ فَقَالَ خَزَيْمَةُ أَنَا هَلُمَّ أَشْهَدُ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ إِنَّكَ أَوْفَيْتَ الْأَعْرَابِيَّ ثَمَنَ النَّاقَةِ فَقَالَ كَيْفَ تَشْهَدُ لِي وَلَمْ تُحْضَرْ فَقَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ إِنَّا نُصَدِّقُكَ فِيمَا تَأْتِينَا بِهِ مِنْ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ أَفَلَا نُصَدِّقُكَ فِيمَا تُخْبِرُ بِهِ مِنْ أَدَاءِ ثَمَنِ النَّاقَةِ فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ شَهِدَ لَهُ خَزيمَةُ فَهُوَ حَسْبُهُ فَجُعِلَتْ شَهَادَتُهُ كَشَهَادَةِ رَجُلَيْنِ كَرَامَةً وَتَفْضِيلًا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مَعَ أَنَّ النُّصُوصَ أَوْجَبَتِ اشْتِرَاطَ الْعَدَدِ فِي حَقِّ الْعَامَّةِ فَلَا يُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ وَأَنْ لَا يَكُونَ مَعْدُولًا بِهِ عَنِ الْقِيَاسِ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ الْأَصْلُ مُخَالِفًا لِلْقِيَاسِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ هُوَ بِنَفْسِهِ مُخَالِفًا لِلْقِيَاسِ فَكَيْفَ يُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ كَبَقَاءِ الصَّوْمِ مَعَ الْأَكْلِ وَالشُّرْبِ نَاسِيًا فَإِنَّهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِلْقِيَاسِ إِذِ الْقِيَاسُ يَقْتَضِي فَسَادَ الصَّوْمِ بِهِ وَإِنَّمَا أَبْقَيْنَاهُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِلَّذِي أَكَلَ نَاسِيًا أَتِمَّ صَوْمَكَ فَإِنَّمَا أَطْعَمَكَ اللهُ وَسَقَاكَ فَلَا يُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ الْخَاطِئُ وَالْمُكْرَهُ كَمَا قَاسَهُمَا الشَّافِعِيُّ. وَأَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ الثَّابِتُ بِالنَّصِّ بِعَيْنِهِ إِلَىٰ فَرْعٍ هُوَ نَظِيرُهُ وَلَا نَصَّ فِيهِ هَذَا الشَّرْطُ وَإِنْ كَانَ وَاحِدًا لَكِنَّهُ يَتَضَمَّنُ شُرُوطًا أَرْبَعَةً أَحَدُهَا كَوْنُ الْحُكْمِ شَرْعِيًّا لَا عَقْلِيًّا وَالثَّانِي تَعْدِيَتُهُ بِعَيْنِهِ بِلَا تَغْيِيرٍ وَالثَّالِثُ كَوْنُ الْفَرْعِ نَظِيرًا لِلْأَصْلِ لَا أَدْوَنَ مِنْهُ وَالرَّابِعُ عَدَمُ وُجُودِ النَّصِّ فِي الْفَرْعِ وَقَدْ فَرَّعَ الْمُصَنِّفُ عَلَى كُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ تَفْرِيعًا عَلَى مَا سَيَأْتِي وَهَذَا هُوَ رَأْيُ جُمْهُورِ الْأُصُولِيِّينَ اقْتِدَاءً بِفِكْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَقَدِ ابْتَدَعَ بَعْضُ الشَّارِحِينَ فَقَالَ إِنَّهُ يَتَضَمَّنُ سِتَّ شُرُوطٍ الْأَرْبَعَةُ مِنْهَا هِيَ الْمَذْكُورَةُ وَهَذَانِ الِاثْنَانِ التَّعَدِّيَةُ وَكَوْنُ الْحُكْمِ الشَّرْعِيِّ ثَابِتًا بِالنَّصِّ وَهَذَا وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا يَسْتَقِيمُ لَكِنْ لَيْسَتْ لَهُ ثَمَرَةٌ صَحِيحَةٌ فَلَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لِإِثْبَاتِ اسْمِ الزِّنَا لِلِّوَاطَةِ لَيْسَ بِحُكْمٍ شَرْعِيٍّ
Like the testimony of Khuzaymah alone, for it is specified by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever Khuzaymah testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' And it is not appropriate to analogize to him one who is higher in rank than him, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, because then the special miracle of his being singled out for this ruling would be nullified. Its story is what was narrated: The Prophet (peace be upon him) bought a she-camel from a Bedouin and paid him the price in full. The Bedouin denied receiving it and said, 'Bring me a witness.' The Prophet said, 'Who will testify for me, when no one was present with me?' Khuzaymah said, 'I am here, I testify, O Messenger of Allah, that you paid the Bedouin the price of the she-camel.' He said, 'How can you testify for me when you were not present?' He said, 'O Messenger of Allah, we believe you in what you bring us from the news of the heaven; shall we not believe you in what you inform us regarding the payment of the price of the she-camel?' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Whoever Khuzaymah testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' So his testimony was made like the testimony of two men, as a miracle and distinction over others, despite the texts making the condition of number obligatory for the general public. Thus, no one else can be analogized to him. And that it should not be deviated from analogy: that the original should not be contrary to analogy. For if it itself is contrary to analogy, how can something else be analogized to it? Like the validity of fasting with eating and drinking forgetfully. For it is contrary to analogy, since analogy requires the invalidation of fasting by it. We only upheld it due to his saying (peace be upon him) to the one who ate forgetfully: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' So the mistaken and the coerced cannot be analogized to him, as al-Shafi'i analogized them. And that the legal ruling established by a specific text should be extended to a branch that is its parallel and has no text. This condition, although one, actually comprises four conditions: first, that the ruling be legal (shar'i) not rational; second, that it be extended identically without change; third, that the branch be a parallel to the original, not lower; fourth, that there be no text regarding the branch. The author has derived branches for each of these four as will come. This is the view of the majority of usul scholars, following the intellect of Islam. Some commentators innovated, saying it comprises six conditions: the four mentioned and these two: transitivity and that the legal ruling is established by text. This, although plausible, has no sound fruit. So the reasoning to prove the name of zina for liwat is not sound, as it is not a legal ruling.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for valid qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi usul, expanding on the text of Nur al-Anwar. The author first addresses an exception: the case of Khuzaymah ibn Thabit, whose single testimony was accepted by the Prophet ﷺ as sufficient, making it equivalent to the testimony of two men. This was a special karamah (miracle) for Khuzaymah, and therefore it cannot be analogized to other people, even if they are higher in rank like the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The full story is narrated to illustrate that this ruling is specific to Khuzaymah and not generalizable. The author then moves to a general condition for qiyas: the original ruling (asl) must not itself be contrary to qiyas. That is, if the ruling in the original case was established as an exception to the general rule (e.g., based on a specific text or as a concession), you cannot use that exception as a basis for analogy to other cases. The example given is fasting while forgetfully eating or drinking: the fasting remains valid despite eating/drinking, which contradicts the general principle that eating/drinking invalidates fasting. This ruling was based on a specific hadith. Therefore, you cannot analogize to it the cases of someone who intentionally makes a mistake (khati') or is forced to eat (mukrah), as Imam al-Shafi'i did. The author then explains a second condition: the ruling must be extended identically from a textually established ruling to a branch case that is exactly parallel and has no explicit text. This single condition actually contains four sub-conditions: (1) the ruling must be a shar'i (legal) ruling, not a rational one; (2) it must be extended identically without any change; (3) the branch (far') must be exactly parallel to the original, not inferior; (4) there must be no existing text (Quran/Hadith) on the branch case. The author notes that the commentator of the matn has detailed derivations for each. A later innovator claimed these two additional conditions (transitivity and textual establishment) make six, but the author rejects this as unfruitful, giving the example that applying the name 'zina' to liwat (sodomy) is not a valid legal ruling to analogize from.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a shar'i ruling from an original case (asl) to a branch case (far') due to shared effective cause ('illa).
أصل (asl): The original case with an established shar'i ruling from text or consensus.
فرع (far'): The new case to which the ruling is extended by analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the case of Khuzaymah's single testimony not be used as a basis for analogy to other Companions?
A) Khuzaymah was a high-ranking Companion, so his case is general.
B) The ruling was a special karamah (miracle) for Khuzaymah, specified by a hadith, and general texts require two witnesses.
C) The text establishing Khuzaymah's testimony is weak.
D) Other Companions did not need such a ruling.

Key Takeaway
A qiyas cannot be based on an original ruling that is itself an exception to the general rule, as that would nullify the specificity of the exception.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Four Conditions of Valid Qiyas and the Linguistic Analogy Dispute
Explaining four conditions for qiyas validity with a linguistic analogy dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for valid qiyas according to Hanafi usul and evaluate the dispute about whether liwat can be called zina via qiyas.

Core Idea
Valid qiyas requires a shar'i ruling transferred identically to an equal branch with no text—not linguistic name extension.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar presents the conditions for valid qiyas as articulated by Fakhr al-Islam and the majority of Hanafi usul scholars. It then applies the first condition—that the ruling must be shar'i—to a classic dispute: can the act of liwat be called 'zina' through qiyas? The analysis distinguishes between transferring a legal ruling (which is permissible via shared 'illa) and transferring a linguistic name (which is not valid qiyas). Understanding this distinction is key to applying qiyas correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the one condition that contains four
The passage states that the single condition 'the ruling is transferred identically to a counterpart without text' actually includes four sub-conditions. Recognise that this is a compact expression of multiple requirements.
The author follows Fakhr al-Islam's formulation.
2
List the four sub-conditions
Extract each: (1) the ruling must be shar'i (legal, not linguistic), (2) transferred identically without change, (3) the branch is a counterpart not inferior, (4) no existing text on the branch.
Some commentators added two more, but the author dismisses them as without benefit.
3
Understand the dispute on linguistic qiyas
Al-Shafi'i and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that liwat shares the definition of zina ('forbidden emission in a forbidden place') and thus should be called zina. Recognise this as an attempt to extend the name, not just the ruling.
The passage calls this 'qiyas fi al-lugha' (linguistic analogy).
4
Distinguish between name and ruling
The Hanafi position holds that giving the name is a matter of language, not a shar'i ruling. The ruling of zina (e.g., hadd) may apply due to shared 'illa, but the name itself cannot be transferred by qiyas.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the name affects punishment classification.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
If liwat is called zina, the hadd for zina applies; if not, the punishment may be ta'zir. The author sides with not transferring the name, as it yields no legal benefit.
The wine (khamr) analogy is cited: Shafi'is extend the name to all intoxicants, Hanafis restrict it to grape wine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ الثَّابِتُ بِالنَّصِّ بِعَيْنِهِ إِلَىٰ فَرْعٍ هُوَ نَظِيرُهُ وَلَا نَصَّ فِيهِ. هَذَا الشَّرْطُ وَإِنْ كَانَ وَاحِدًا تَسْبَعَةٌ لَكِنَّهُ يَتَضَمَنُ شُرُوطًا أَرْبَعَةٌ: أَحَدُهَا كَوْنُ الْحُكْمِ شَرْعِيًا لَا لُغَوِيًا، وَالثَّانِي تَعْدِيَتُهُ بِعَيْنِهِ بِلَا تَغْيِيرٍ، وَالثَّالِثُ كَوْنُ الْفَرْعِ نَظِيرًا لِلْأَصْلِ لَا أَدْوَنَ مِنْهُ، وَالرَّابِعُ عَدَمُ وُجُودِ النَّصِّ فِي الْفَرْعِ. وَقَدْ فَرَّعَ الْمُصَنِّفُ عَلَى كُلٍّ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ تَفْرِيعًا عَلَى مَا سَيَأْتِي. وَهَذَا هُوَ رَأْيُ جُمْهُورِ الْأُصُولِيِّينَ اقْتِدَاءً بِفَخْرِ الإِسْلَامِ. وَقَدِ ابْتَدَعَ بَعْضُ الشَّارِحِينَ فَقَالَ: إِنَّهَا تَتَضَمَنُ سِتَّةَ شُرُوطٍ: الْأَرْبَعَةُ مِنْهَا هِيَ الْمَذْكُورَةُ، وَهَذَانِ: التَّعْدِيَةُ، وَكَوْنُ الْحُكْمِ الشَّرْعِيِّ ثَابِتًا بِالنَّصِّ لَا بِالْفَرْعِ لِشَيْءٍ آخَرَ. وَهَذَا وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا يَسْتَقِيمُ لَكِنْ لَيْسَتْ لَهُ ثَمْرَةٌ صَحِيحَةٌ. فَلَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لِإِثْبَاتِ اسْمِ الزِّنَا لِلِّوَاطَةِ لَيْسَ بِحُكْمٍ شَرْعِيٍّ. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى أَوَّلِ الشَّرْطِ وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْحُكْمِ شَرْعِيًا. فَإِنَّ الشَّافِعِيَّ يَقُولُ: الزِّنَا سَفْحُ مَاءٍ مُحَرَّمٍ فِي مَحَلٍّ مُشْتَهًى مُحَرَّمٍ، وَهَذَا الْمَعْنَى مَوْجُودٌ فِي اللِّوَاطَةِ بَلْ هِيَ فَوْقَهُ فِي الْحُرْمَةِ وَالشَّهْوَةِ وَتَضْيِيعِ الْمَاءِ، فَيَجْرِي عَلَيْهَا اسْمُ الزِّنَا وَحُكْمُهُ. وَإِلَيْهِ ذَهَبَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ، وَهَذَا يُسَمَّى قِيَاسًا فِي اللُّغَةِ. وَلَكِنْ فَرْقٌ بَيْنَ أَنْ يُعْطَى لِلِّوَاطَةِ اسْمُ الزِّنَا وَبَيْنَ أَنْ يَجْرِي عَلَيْهَا حُكْمُهُ فَقَطْ لِأَجْلِ اشْتِرَاكِ الْعِلَّةِ. فَإِنَّ الْأَوَّلَ قِيَاسٌ فِي اللُّغَةِ دُونَ الثَّانِي. وَالْمُجَوِّزُونَ لَهُ هُمْ أَكْثَرُ أَصْحَابِ الشَّافِعِيِّ، فَإِنَّهُمْ يُعْطُونَ اسْمَ الْخَمْرِ لِكُلِّ مَا يُحَامِرُ الْعَقْلَ.
And that the legal ruling established by the text is transferred identically to a branch that is its counterpart and for which there is no text. This condition, though one, actually includes four conditions: first, the ruling is legal not linguistic; second, it is transferred identically without change; third, the branch is a counterpart of the original not inferior; fourth, there is no text concerning the branch. The author has derived subdivisions from each of these four as will come. This is the view of the majority of usul scholars following Fakhr al-Islam. Some commentators innovated, saying it includes six conditions: the four mentioned and these two: the transfer and the legal ruling being established by text not by something else. This is correct but yields no proper result. Therefore, the reasoning to establish the name of zina for liwat is not a valid legal ruling. A subdivision on the first condition: that the ruling is legal. For al-Shafi'i says: zina is the prohibited emission of fluid in a prohibited lustful place, and this meaning exists in liwat, indeed it is greater in prohibition, lust, and waste of fluid, so the name and ruling of zina apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad inclined to this, and this is called qiyas in language. But there is a difference between giving the name of zina to liwat and applying only its ruling due to shared cause. The first is linguistic qiyas, not the second. Those who permit it are most of al-Shafi'i's followers, for they give the name of wine to anything that intoxicates the mind.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains the conditions for valid qiyas. The author states one condition that actually contains four sub-conditions. First, the ruling being transferred must be a shar'i (legal) ruling, not a linguistic one. Second, the ruling is transferred identically without any change (ta'diya bi 'aynihi). Third, the branch (far') must be exactly similar to the original (asl), not inferior. Fourth, there must be no existing text (nas) concerning the branch. The author notes that the majority of usul scholars, following Fakhr al-Islam, adopt these four. Some commentators add two more: the act of transfer itself, and that the ruling is established by text, but these yield no practical benefit. The passage then applies the first condition to the dispute about whether the act of liwat (sodomy) can be called zina for the purpose of legal rulings. Al-Shafi'i defines zina as forbidden sexual emission in a forbidden place of desire, and argues that liwat fits this definition even more, so it should be called zina and receive the same ruling. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani agreed with this linguistic analogy. However, the author (Ashraf) distinguishes between giving the name (isim) and applying the ruling (hukm). Giving the name is linguistic qiyas, which is not valid for deriving a shar'i ruling. The ruling of zina (e.g., hadd) might still apply due to shared cause ('illa), but the name itself is not transferred. The author implies that the correct Hanafi position is that liwat does not share the same name as zina, and thus the hadd for zina may not apply identically—a detailed fiqh difference. The example of wine (khamr) is also cited: al-Shafi'i's followers give the name of wine to any intoxicant, while Hanafis maintain that khamr is specifically grape wine.

Key Terms
حكم شرعي (hukm shar'i): A ruling from Islamic law, not merely linguistic or rational
قياس في اللغة (qiyas fi al-lugha): Analogy based on linguistic meaning, not legal cause
علة (illa): The effective cause that justifies the ruling in both original and branch

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it incorrect to call liwat 'zina' via qiyas?
A) Because the definition of zina does not apply to liwat.
B) Because giving the name is a linguistic analogy, not a valid shar'i qiyas.
C) Because Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagreed with it.
D) Because there is a text that explicitly forbids calling liwat zina.

Key Takeaway
The four conditions of valid qiyas ensure its validity; linguistic analogy does not transfer legal names.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
First Condition of Qiyas: Shar'i Ruling and Rejection of Linguistic Analogy
Dispute on linguistic qiyas with Hanafi refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between linguistic analogy (qiyas fi al-lugha) and legal analogy (qiyas shar'i), and explain why the Hanafi school rejects linguistic analogy for deriving legal rulings.

Core Idea
Linguistic analogy extends names, not legal rulings — only a common legal 'illa transfers the hukm.

The first condition for a valid qiyas is that the ruling in the original case (asl) must be a shar'i (legal) ruling. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that zina (fornication) and liwat (sodomy) share the same meaning, so the name and ruling of zina apply to liwat. This reasoning is called qiyas fi al-lugha (linguistic analogy). The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes between assigning a name (linguistic) and applying a ruling (legal). A famous anecdote involving a bottle and rocket illustrates the absurdity of linguistic analogy. In this lesson, you will explore this dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
State the first condition for qiyas: the ruling in the asl must be shar'i (legal). This is necessary because qiyas transfers a legal ruling, not a linguistic one.
The condition is 'كون الحكم شرعيا' (the ruling is shar'i).
2
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
Examine how al-Shafi'i defines zina as 'safh ma' haram fi mahall mubah' and claims the same meaning exists in liwat, so the name and ruling transfer.
This is a linguistic analogy (qiyas fi al-lugha).
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between naming (ta'smiya) and ruling (hukm). Linguistic analogy gives the name but does not necessarily give the ruling.
The ruling transfers only if there is a common legal 'illa not just a linguistic meaning.
4
Evaluate the anecdote
Consider the Hanafi anecdote about the bottle (qarura) and rocket (jirjir) as a reductio ad absurdum of linguistic analogy.
If linguistic definitions were used for legal rulings, absurdities would follow.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: In the Shafi'i school, liwat is treated as zina with the same hadd punishment; in the Hanafi school, liwat is a separate offense with ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
This difference arises from rejecting linguistic analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى أَوَّلِ الشَّرْطِ وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْحُكْمِ شَرْعِيًا فَإِنَّ الشَّافِعِي يَقُولُ الزَّنَا سَفْحُ مَاءٍ مُحَرَّمٍ فِي مَحَلٍّ مُسْتَبَاحٍ مُحَرَّمٍ وَهَذَا الْمَعْنَى مَوْجُودٌ فِي الْمُوَاطَأَةِ بَلْ هِيَ فَوْقَ فِي الْحُرْمَةِ وَالشَّهْوَةِ وَتَضْيِيعِ الْمَاءِ فَيَجْرِي عَلَيْهَا اسْمُ الزَّنَا وَحُكْمُهُ وَإِلَيْهِ ذَهَبَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَهَذَا يُسَمَّى قِيَاسًا دُونَ الثَّانِي وَالْمُجَوِّزُونَ لَهُ هُمْ أَكْثَرُ أَصْحَابِ الشَّافِعِي فَإِنَّهُمْ يُعْطُونَ اسْمَ الْخَمْرِ لِكُلِّ مَا يُحَامِرُ الْعَقْلَ وَأَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الثَّانِي أَنَّهُ لَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لِصِحَّةِ ظِهَارِ الذِّمِّي كَمَا عَلَّلَهُ الشَّافِعِي فَيَقُولُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُّ طَلَاقُهُ فَيَصِحُّ ظِهَارُهُ كَالْمُسْلِمِ لَمْ يُوجَدِ الشَّرْطُ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ تَعْدِيَةُ الْحُكْمِ بِعَيْنِهِ لِكَوْنِ هَذَا التَّعْلِيلِ تَغْيِيرًا لِلْحُرْمَةِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الْمُسْلِمُ إِلَى إِطْلَاقِهَا فِي الْفَرْعِ عَنِ الْغَايَةِ لَأَنَّ ظِهَارَ الْمُسْلِمِ يَنْتَهِي بِالْكَفَّارَةِ وَظِهَارُ الذِّمِّي يَكُونُ مُؤَبَّدًا إِذْ لَيْسَ هُوَ أَهْلًا لِلْكَفَّارَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ وَقِيلَ هُوَ أَهْلُ التَّحْرِيرِ وَلَكِنْ لَيْسَ أَهْلًا لِلتَّمْرِيرِ الَّذِي يَحْلِفُ الصَّوْمُ وَلَا. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الثَّالِثِ وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْفَرْعِ الْفِعْلِ أَوْلَى وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنَّ عُذْرَهُمَا دُونَ عُذْرِهِ فَإِنَّ النِّسْيَانَ يَقَعُ بِلَا اخْتِيَارٍ وَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ إِلَى صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ وَفَعَلُ الْخَاطِئِ وَالْمُكْرَهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ فَإِنَّ الْخَاطِئَ يَذْكُرُ الصَّوْمَ وَلَكِنَّهُ يَقْصِرُ فِي الِاحْتِيَاطِ فِي الْمَضْمَضَةِ حَتَّى دَخَلَ الْمَاءُ فِي حَلْقِهِ. وَقَدْ قَالَ لَهُمْ وَاحِدٌ مِنَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ لِمَ تُسَمَّى الْقَارُورَةُ قَارُورَةً فَقَالُوا لِأَنَّهُ يَتَقَرَّرُ فِيهِ الْمَاءُ فَقَالَ إِنَّ بَطْنَكَ أَيْضًا يَتَقَرَّرُ فِيهِ الْمَاءُ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُسَمَّى قَارُورَةً ثُمَّ قَالَ لَهُمْ لِمَ يُسَمَّى الْجِرْجِيرُ جِرْجِيرًا فَقَالُوا إِنَّهُ يَتَجَرْجَرُ أَيْ يَتَحَرَّكُ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ فَقَالَ إِنَّ لِحْيَتَكَ أَيْضًا يَتَحَرَّكُ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُسَمَّى جِرْجِيرًا فَتَحَيَّرَ وَسَكَتَ.
A subdivision on the first condition: that the ruling is shar'i. For al-Shafi'i says: Zina is the discharge of forbidden fluid into a forbidden place that is permissible for desire, and this meaning is found in liwat, rather liwat is superior in prohibition, desire, and waste of fluid, so the name and ruling of zina apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad went to this. This is called qiyas in language. But there is a difference between giving liwat the name of zina and merely applying its ruling due to shared cause. The first is qiyas in language, unlike the second; those who permit it are most Shafi'is, for they give the name of khamr to everything that covers the intellect, and the ruling transfers. Subdivision on the second condition: that the reasoning is not sound for the validity of dhimmi zihar as al-Shafi'i reasoned: his divorce is valid, so his zihar is valid like a Muslim. The second condition is not found: transferring the ruling itself, because this reasoning changes the limited prohibition by expiation in the original (the Muslim) to absolute prohibition in the branch without termination, for the Muslim's zihar ends with expiation, while the dhimmi's zihar is permanent since he is not qualified for expiation which is between worship and punishment; it is said he is qualified for freeing a slave but not for fasting which involves oath. Subdivision on the third condition: that the branch is similar to the original. Al-Shafi'i says: Since the forgetful person is excused despite being deliberate in the act itself, then the mistaken and coerced, who are not deliberate in the act itself, are more entitled to be excused. We say: Their excuse is less than his excuse, for forgetfulness occurs involuntarily and is attributed to the right-holder, while the mistaken and coerced act without the right-holder. The mistaken person remembers the fast but is negligent in precaution during rinsing until water enters his throat. And a Hanafi said to them: Why is a bottle called a bottle? They said: Because water settles in it. He said: Your stomach also settles water, so it should be called a bottle. Then he said to them: Why is rocket called rocket? They said: It moves about on the ground. He said: Your beard also moves, so it should be called rocket. They were perplexed and remained silent.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author discusses the first condition: the ruling in the original case (asl) must be a shar'i (legal) ruling, not linguistic. Al-Shafi'i argues that zina (fornication) is defined as forbidden fluid in a forbidden place, and this meaning exists in liwat (sodomy), even more so, so the name and ruling of zina apply. This is called qiyas fi al-lugha (linguistic analogy). The Hanafi response distinguishes between assigning the name (which is linguistic) and applying the ruling (which is legal). The Shafi'is permit linguistic analogy, as they extend the name of khamr (wine) to any intoxicant. The author then addresses the second condition: the ruling must be transferred exactly as is. A Shafi'i argument that dhimmi zihar is valid by analogy to Muslim zihar is rejected because the ruling changes: Muslim zihar ends with expiation, dhimmi zihar is permanent since he cannot perform expiation. The third condition: the branch must be exactly similar to the original. Shafi'i argues that the forgetful person is excused despite being deliberate, so the mistaken and coerced should be more excused. Hanafis respond that the forgetful person's act is involuntary, while the mistaken person acted with negligence, so their excuse is less. The passage ends with a famous Hanafi anecdote refuting linguistic qiyas: a Hanafi challenges Shafi'is that if they define 'qarura' (bottle) by water settling, then a stomach should also be called a bottle; similarly, 'jirjir' (rocket) is defined as moving on the ground, so a beard should be called rocket, baffling them. This shows the absurdity of linguistic analogy for legal rulings.

Key Terms
قياس في اللغة (qiyas fi al-lugha): Analogy based on linguistic meaning and name extension, not on legal 'illa
تعدية الحكم (ta'diyat al-hukm): Transferring the ruling from asl to far' with exact same effect
الزنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and woman

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the Shafi'i qiyas on liwat (sodomy) from zina (fornication) invalid?
A) Because liwat is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because the ruling (hadd) is not transferred exactly; liwat has a different punishment.
C) Because the Shafi'i reasoning is based on linguistic analogy (qiyas fi al-lugha), which Hanafis reject.
D) Because Abu Hanifa differed from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a shar'i 'illa for qiyas; linguistic analogy (qiyas fi al-lugha) is rejected because it confuses naming with legal consequence.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
7 min
Second Condition of Qiyas: Exact Transfer of the Ruling (Ta'diyat al-Hukm)
Dispute on dhimmi zihar and the condition of exact transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of exact transfer (ta'diyat al-hukm) and evaluate why the Shafi'i analogy for dhimmi zihar fails according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
If the ruling changes in the branch, qiyas is invalid — ta'diyat al-hukm requires identical effect.

The second condition for valid qiyas is that the ruling must be transferred exactly from the original (asl) to the branch (far'), without any change. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that since a Muslim's zihar (a form of divorce-like declaration) is valid and ends with expiation, a dhimmi's (non-Muslim citizen's) zihar should also be valid by analogy. The Hanafi response shows that this analogy fails because the ruling changes: a Muslim's zihar is temporary (ends with expiation) while a dhimmi's zihar would be permanent because a dhimmi cannot perform the required expiation. This violates ta'diyat al-hukm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second condition
State the second condition: ta'diyat al-hukm bi 'aynihi — the ruling must be transferred exactly as it is in the original.
The ruling must apply identically in both cases.
2
Examine the Shafi'i analogy
Al-Shafi'i reasons: a dhimmi's divorce is valid, so his zihar should also be valid, by analogy to a Muslim.
This is a qiyas based on the common fact that both are valid acts of divorce/zihar.
3
Identify the Hanafi objection
The Hanafi objection: the ruling changes. In the Muslim case, zihar ends with expiation (kaffarah). In the dhimmi case, the dhimmi cannot perform expiation because it is a form of worship/punishment for which he is not qualified. So the zihar becomes permanent, which is a different ruling.
Thus, the ruling is not transferred exactly; the qiyas is invalid.
4
Consider the alternative view
Some argue the dhimmi can free a slave (as expiation) but cannot fast (which requires an oath). The text notes this debate but upholds the invalidity of the analogy.
The key point is that the ruling changes: from temporary to permanent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الْمُوَاطَأَةِ بَلْ هِيَ فَوْقَ فِي الْحُرْمَةِ وَالشَّهْوَةِ وَتَضْيِيعِ الْمَاءِ فَيَجْرِي عَلَيْهَا اسْمُ الزَّنَا وَحُكْمُهُ وَإِلَيْهِ ذَهَبَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَهَذَا يُسَمَّى قِيَاسًا فِي اللُّغَةِ وَلَكِنَّ فَرْقٌ بَيْنَ إِنْ يُعْطَى لِلْوَاطَةِ اسْمُ الزَّنَا وَبَيْنَ أَنْ يَجْرِيَ عَلَيْهَا حُكْمُهُ فَقَطْ لِأَجْلِ اشْتِرَاكِ الْعِلَّةِ فَإِنَّ الْأَوَّلَ قِيَاسٌ فِي اللُّغَةِ دُونَ الثَّانِي وَالْمُجَوِّزُونَ لَهُ هُمْ أَكْثَرُ أَصْحَابِ الشَّافِعِي فَإِنَّهُمْ يُعْطُونَ اسْمَ الْخَمْرِ لِكُلِّ مَا يُحَامِرُ الْعَقْلَ وَأَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الثَّانِي أَنَّهُ لَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لِصِحَّةِ ظِهَارِ الذِّمِّي كَمَا عَلَّلَهُ الشَّافِعِي فَيَقُولُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُّ طَلَاقُهُ فَيَصِحُّ ظِهَارُهُ كَالْمُسْلِمِ لَمْ يُوجَدِ الشَّرْطُ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ تَعْدِيَةُ الْحُكْمِ بِعَيْنِهِ لِكَوْنِ هَذَا التَّعْلِيلِ تَغْيِيرًا لِلْحُرْمَةِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الْمُسْلِمُ إِلَى إِطْلَاقِهَا فِي الْفَرْعِ عَنِ الْغَايَةِ لَأَنَّ ظِهَارَ الْمُسْلِمِ يَنْتَهِي بِالْكَفَّارَةِ وَظِهَارُ الذِّمِّي يَكُونُ مُؤَبَّدًا إِذْ لَيْسَ هُوَ أَهْلًا لِلْكَفَّارَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ وَقِيلَ هُوَ أَهْلُ التَّحْرِيرِ وَلَكِنْ لَيْسَ أَهْلًا لِلتَّمْرِيرِ الَّذِي يَحْلِفُ الصَّوْمُ وَلَا. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الثَّالِثِ وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْفَرْعِ نَظِيرَ الْأَصْلِ فَإِنَّ الشَّافِعِي يَقُولُ لَمَّا عُذِرَ النَّاسِي مَعَ كَوْنِهِ عَامِدًا فِي نَفْسِ الْفِعْلِ فَلَأَنْ يُعْذَرَ الْخَاطِئُ وَالْمُكْرَهُ وَهُمَا لَيْسَا بِعَامِدَيْنِ فِي نَفْسِ الْفِعْلِ أَوْلَى وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنَّ عُذْرَهُمَا دُونَ عُذْرِهِ فَإِنَّ النِّسْيَانَ يَقَعُ بِلَا اخْتِيَارٍ وَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ إِلَى صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ وَفَعَلُ الْخَاطِئِ وَالْمُكْرَهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ فَإِنَّ الْخَاطِئَ يَذْكُرُ الصَّوْمَ وَلَكِنَّهُ يَقْصِرُ فِي الِاحْتِيَاطِ فِي الْمَضْمَضَةِ حَتَّى دَخَلَ الْمَاءُ فِي حَلْقِهِ. وَقَدْ قَالَ لَهُمْ وَاحِدٌ مِنَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ لِمَ تُسَمَّى الْقَارُورَةُ قَارُورَةً فَقَالُوا لِأَنَّهُ يَتَقَرَّرُ فِيهِ الْمَاءُ فَقَالَ إِنَّ بَطْنَكَ أَيْضًا يَتَقَرَّرُ فِيهِ الْمَاءُ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُسَمَّى قَارُورَةً ثُمَّ قَالَ لَهُمْ لِمَ يُسَمَّى الْجِرْجِيرُ جِرْجِيرًا فَقَالُوا إِنَّهُ يَتَجَرْجَرُ أَيْ يَتَحَرَّكُ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ فَقَالَ إِنَّ لِحْيَتَكَ أَيْضًا يَتَحَرَّكُ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُسَمَّى جِرْجِيرًا فَتَحَيَّرَ وَسَكَتَ.
A subdivision on the first condition: that the ruling is shar'i. For al-Shafi'i says: Zina is the discharge of forbidden fluid into a forbidden place that is permissible for desire, and this meaning is found in liwat, rather liwat is superior in prohibition, desire, and waste of fluid, so the name and ruling of zina apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad went to this. This is called qiyas in language. But there is a difference between giving liwat the name of zina and merely applying its ruling due to shared cause. The first is qiyas in language, unlike the second; those who permit it are most Shafi'is, for they give the name of khamr to everything that covers the intellect, and the ruling transfers. The second condition is not found: transferring the ruling itself, because this reasoning changes the limited prohibition by expiation in the original (the Muslim) to absolute prohibition in the branch without termination, for the Muslim's zihar ends with expiation, while the dhimmi's zihar is permanent since he is not qualified for expiation which is between worship and punishment; it is said he is qualified for freeing a slave but not for fasting which involves oath. Subdivision on the third condition: that the branch is similar to the original. Al-Shafi'i says: Since the forgetful person is excused despite being deliberate in the act itself, then the mistaken and coerced, who are not deliberate in the act itself, are more entitled to be excused. We say: Their excuse is less than his excuse, for forgetfulness occurs involuntarily and is attributed to the right-holder, while the mistaken and coerced act without the right-holder. They said: It moves about on the ground. He said: Your beard also moves, so it should be called rocket. They were perplexed and remained silent.

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author discusses the first condition: the ruling in the original case (asl) must be a shar'i (legal) ruling, not linguistic. Al-Shafi'i argues that zina (fornication) is defined as forbidden fluid in a forbidden place, and this meaning exists in liwat (sodomy), even more so, so the name and ruling of zina apply. This is called qiyas fi al-lugha (linguistic analogy). The Hanafi response distinguishes between assigning the name (which is linguistic) and applying the ruling (which is legal). The Shafi'is permit linguistic analogy, as they extend the name of khamr (wine) to any intoxicant. The author then addresses the second condition: the ruling must be transferred exactly as is. This shows the absurdity of linguistic analogy for legal rulings.

Key Terms
تعدية الحكم (ta'diyat al-hukm): Transferring the ruling from asl to far' with exact same effect
ظهار الذمي (zihar al-dhimmi): Zihar (declaration of unlawful conjugal relations) by a non-Muslim subject
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for certain violations, such as freeing a slave or fasting

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the Shafi'i qiyas on dhimmi zihar?
A) Because dhimmis are not allowed to perform zihar at all.
B) Because the ruling changes: Muslim zihar is temporary, dhimmi zihar would be permanent.
C) Because the Shafi'i 'illa is invalid from the start.
D) Because the dhimmi's divorce is not valid.

Key Takeaway
The condition of ta'diyat al-hukm ensures that qiyas only transfers rulings that apply identically; any change invalidates the analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
7 min
Third Condition of Qiyas: Branch Must Be Similar to the Original
Dispute on the similarity condition with example of forgetful vs mistaken/coerced

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on excusing the mistaken and coerced person in fasting, and articulate the Hanafi critique of the Shafi'i analogy.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness is involuntary and excused by the right-holder; negligence and coercion are not — the branch is not similar to the original.

The third condition for qiyas is that the branch (far') must be exactly similar (nazir) to the original (asl). Imam al-Shafi'i argued that since a forgetful person is excused in fasting despite being deliberate in the act (he deliberately ate but forgot he was fasting), then a mistaken person or a coerced person should be even more entitled to excuse, because they lack intention. The Hanafi response demonstrates that the cases are not similar: forgetfulness occurs involuntarily and the act is attributed to the right-holder (Allah), while the mistaken person's act is due to his own negligence, and the coerced person's act is attributed to the coercer. Thus, the excuse for the forgetful is greater, not less.

Guided Path
1
State the third condition
The branch must be exactly similar (nazir) to the original; if there is a significant difference, qiyas is invalid.
This condition ensures the 'illa applies equally.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
Al-Shafi'i says: since the forgetful person is excused despite being deliberate in the action (he intentionally put food in his mouth but forgot the fast), then the mistaken and coerced (who lack intention entirely) should be even more excused.
This is an argument from 'first priority' (awla).
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: forgetfulness is involuntary and attributed to the right-holder (Allah). The mistaken person, however, committed negligence (e.g., not being careful during rinsing). The coerced person's act is not wholly his own; it is attributed to the coercer. Therefore, the excuse in the case of forgetfulness is greater, not less.
The branch cases are not similar to the original; the 'illa (presence of excuse) is weaker in the branches.
4
Identify the difference
The key difference: forgetfulness is purely involuntary and the act is forgiven by the right-holder; the mistaken person's act involves neglect (taqsir), so he is blameworthy to some extent.
Thus, the forgetful person has a stronger excuse, making the Shafi'i 'priority' argument inverted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الْمُوَاطَأَةِ بَلْ هِيَ فَوْقَ فِي الْحُرْمَةِ وَالشَّهْوَةِ وَتَضْيِيعِ الْمَاءِ فَيَجْرِي عَلَيْهَا اسْمُ الزَّنَا وَحُكْمُهُ وَإِلَيْهِ ذَهَبَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَهَذَا يُسَمَّى قِيَاسًا دُونَ الثَّانِي وَالْمُجَوِّزُونَ لَهُ هُمْ أَكْثَرُ أَصْحَابِ الشَّافِعِي فَإِنَّهُمْ يُعْطُونَ اسْمَ الْخَمْرِ لِكُلِّ مَا يُحَامِرُ الْعَقْلَ وَأَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الثَّانِي أَنَّهُ لَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لِصِحَّةِ ظِهَارِ الذِّمِّي كَمَا عَلَّلَهُ الشَّافِعِي فَيَقُولُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُّ طَلَاقُهُ فَيَصِحُّ ظِهَارُهُ كَالْمُسْلِمِ لَمْ يُوجَدِ الشَّرْطُ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ تَعْدِيَةُ الْحُكْمِ بِعَيْنِهِ لِكَوْنِ هَذَا التَّعْلِيلِ تَغْيِيرًا لِلْحُرْمَةِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الْمُسْلِمُ إِلَى إِطْلَاقِهَا فِي الْفَرْعِ عَنِ الْغَايَةِ لَأَنَّ ظِهَارَ الْمُسْلِمِ يَنْتَهِي بِالْكَفَّارَةِ وَظِهَارُ الذِّمِّي يَكُونُ مُؤَبَّدًا إِذْ لَيْسَ هُوَ أَهْلًا لِلْكَفَّارَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ وَقِيلَ هُوَ أَهْلُ التَّحْرِيرِ وَلَكِنْ لَيْسَ أَهْلًا لِلتَّمْرِيرِ الَّذِي يَحْلِفُ الصَّوْمُ وَلَا. تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الثَّالِثِ وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْفَرْعِ نَظِيرَ الْأَصْلِ فَإِنَّ الشَّافِعِي يَقُولُ لَمَّا عُذِرَ النَّاسِي مَعَ كَوْنِهِ عَامِدًا فِي نَفْسِ الْفِعْلِ فَلَأَنْ يُعْذَرَ الْخَاطِئُ وَالْمُكْرَهُ وَهُمَا لَيْسَا بِعَامِدَيْنِ فِي نَفْسِ الْفِعْلِ أَوْلَى وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنَّ عُذْرَهُمَا دُونَ عُذْرِهِ فَإِنَّ النِّسْيَانَ يَقَعُ بِلَا اخْتِيَارٍ وَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ إِلَى صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ وَفَعَلُ الْخَاطِئِ وَالْمُكْرَهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ فَإِنَّ الْخَاطِئَ يَذْكُرُ الصَّوْمَ وَلَكِنَّهُ يَقْصِرُ فِي الِاحْتِيَاطِ فِي الْمَضْمَضَةِ حَتَّى دَخَلَ الْمَاءُ فِي حَلْقِهِ. وَقَدْ قَالَ لَهُمْ وَاحِدٌ مِنَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ لِمَ تُسَمَّى الْقَارُورَةُ قَارُورَةً فَقَالُوا لِأَنَّهُ يَتَقَرَّرُ فِيهِ الْمَاءُ فَقَالَ إِنَّ بَطْنَكَ أَيْضًا يَتَقَرَّرُ فِيهِ الْمَاءُ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُسَمَّى قَارُورَةً ثُمَّ قَالَ لَهُمْ لِمَ يُسَمَّى الْجِرْجِيرُ جِرْجِيرًا فَقَالُوا إِنَّهُ يَتَجَرْجَرُ أَيْ يَتَحَرَّكُ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ فَقَالَ إِنَّ لِحْيَتَكَ أَيْضًا يَتَحَرَّكُ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُسَمَّى جِرْجِيرًا فَتَحَيَّرَ وَسَكَتَ.
A subdivision on the first condition: that the ruling is shar'i. For al-Shafi'i says: Zina is the discharge of forbidden fluid into a forbidden place that is permissible for desire, and this meaning is found in liwat, rather liwat is superior in prohibition, desire, and waste of fluid, so the name and ruling of zina apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad went to this. This is called qiyas in language. But there is a difference between giving liwat the name of zina and merely applying its ruling due to shared cause. The first is qiyas in language, unlike the second; those who permit it are most Shafi'is, for they give the name of khamr to everything that covers the intellect, and the ruling transfers. Subdivision on the second condition: that the reasoning is not sound for the validity of dhimmi zihar as al-Shafi'i reasoned: his divorce is valid, so his zihar is valid like a Muslim. The second condition is not found: transferring the ruling itself, because this reasoning changes the limited prohibition by expiation in the original (the Muslim) to absolute prohibition in the branch without termination, for the Muslim's zihar ends with expiation, while the dhimmi's zihar is permanent since he is not qualified for expiation which is between worship and punishment; it is said he is qualified for freeing a slave but not for fasting which involves oath. Subdivision on the third condition: that the branch is similar to the original. Al-Shafi'i says: Since the forgetful person is excused despite being deliberate in the act itself, then the mistaken and coerced, who are not deliberate in the act itself, are more entitled to be excused. We say: Their excuse is less than his excuse, for forgetfulness occurs involuntarily and is attributed to the right-holder, while the mistaken and coerced act without the right-holder. The mistaken person remembers the fast but is negligent in precaution during rinsing until water enters his throat. And a Hanafi said to them: Why is a bottle called a bottle? They said: Because water settles in it. He said: Your stomach also settles water, so it should be called a bottle. Then he said to them: Why is rocket called rocket? They said: It moves about on the ground. He said: Your beard also moves, so it should be called rocket. They were perplexed and remained silent.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author discusses the first condition: the ruling in the original case (asl) must be a shar'i (legal) ruling, not linguistic. Al-Shafi'i argues that zina (fornication) is defined as forbidden fluid in a forbidden place, and this meaning exists in liwat (sodomy), even more so, so the name and ruling of zina apply. This is called qiyas fi al-lugha (linguistic analogy). The Hanafi response distinguishes between assigning the name (which is linguistic) and applying the ruling (which is legal). The Shafi'is permit linguistic analogy, as they extend the name of khamr (wine) to any intoxicant. The author then addresses the second condition: the ruling must be transferred exactly as is. A Shafi'i argument that dhimmi zihar is valid by analogy to Muslim zihar is rejected because the ruling changes: Muslim zihar ends with expiation, dhimmi zihar is permanent since he cannot perform expiation. The third condition: the branch must be exactly similar to the original. Shafi'i argues that the forgetful person is excused despite being deliberate, so the mistaken and coerced should be more excused. Hanafis respond that the forgetful person's act is involuntary, while the mistaken person acted with negligence, so their excuse is less. The passage ends with a famous Hanafi anecdote refuting linguistic qiyas: a Hanafi challenges Shafi'is that if they define 'qarura' (bottle) by water settling, then a stomach should also be called a bottle; similarly, 'jirjir' (rocket) is defined as moving on the ground, so a beard should be called rocket, baffling them. This shows the absurdity of linguistic analogy for legal rulings.

Key Terms
الناسي (al-nasi): The person who forgets, e.g., forgets he is fasting and eats
الخاطئ (al-khati'): The person who makes a mistake unintentionally, but with some negligence
المكره (al-mukrah): The person who is coerced or forced to act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the forgetful person more excused than the mistaken person in fasting?
A) Because the forgetful person did not intentionally break the fast.
B) Because forgetfulness is involuntary and the act is attributed to the right-holder, while the mistaken person acted negligently.
C) Because the forgetful person's fast is automatically accepted, while the mistaken person's requires qada.
D) Because the mistaken person intended to break the fast.

Key Takeaway
The branch must be exactly similar to the original in the 'illa; a superficial similarity (like lack of intention) is insufficient if the underlying cause differs.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
The Second Condition of Qiyas: Ta'diyat al-Hukm bi 'Aynihi – Refuting Shafi'i Qiyas for Dhihar of a Dhimmi
Refutation of qiyas for dhihar of a dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the second condition of qiyas (ta'diyat al-hukm bi 'aynihi) and apply it to evaluate the Shafi'i argument that dhihar of a dhimmi is valid by analogy to divorce.

Core Idea
A qiyas fails if the ruling in the branch differs in essence from the original, even if the cause appears similar.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i qiyas concerning the validity of dhihar (a pre-Islamic divorce practice) for a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen). The Hanafi scholars demonstrate that the second condition of qiyas—that the ruling must be transferred identically—is violated: the Muslim's dhihar ends with expiation, but a dhimmi cannot perform expiation, making the prohibition permanent. An anecdote about qiyas in language sets the stage, showing how superficial analogies can lead to absurdities.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i Qiyas Claim
The Shafi'i argue that since a dhimmi's divorce (talaq) is valid, his dhihar should also be valid by analogy to a Muslim's dhihar. The claimed illa (cause) is the validity of the divorce act.
2
Identify the Second Condition of Qiyas
The second condition (ta'diyat al-hukm bi 'aynihi) requires that the ruling in the branch be identical in essence to the ruling in the original. If the ruling changes qualitatively, qiyas is invalid.
Hanafi usul emphasizes strict identity of the hukm.
3
Analyze the Ruling Transformation
In the original (Muslim), dhihar creates a finite prohibition that ends with expiation (kaffarah). In the branch (dhimmi), the prohibition would be permanent because the dhimmi cannot perform kaffarah (which involves acts of worship like fasting). Thus the ruling is not identical—it changes from finite to infinite.
Even if a dhimmi can free a slave (one form of kaffarah), he cannot fast as a substitute, as fasting is an act of worship for which he is not eligible.
4
Consider the Language Qiyas Anecdote
The anecdote about qārūrah (bottle) and jarjīr (watercress) shows that reasoning solely from a superficial common meaning can lead to absurd conclusions, reinforcing the need for strict qiyas conditions.
The Shafi'i claimed knowledge of etymologies; the Hanafi showed their logic would imply the stomach is a bottle and the beard is watercress.
5
Conclude the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: dhihar of a dhimmi is not valid because the Shafi'i qiyas fails the second condition. The practical result is that a dhimmi cannot effect dhihar.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with clear usul grounds.

يُعْذَرَ الْخَاطِيُّ وَالْمُكْرَةِ وَهُمَا لَيْسَا بَعَامِدَيْنِ فِى نفْسٍ الْفِعْل أولى وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنْ عُذْرَهُمَا دُونَ عُذْرِهِ فَإِنَّ النَّسيَانَ يَقَعُ بلااختِيَارِ وَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ إِلَى نے ایسا کیا ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ذمی کی طلاق صحیح ہے۔ لہذا اس کا ظہار بھی مسلمان کی طرح درست ہو گا۔ ہمارے نزدیک یہ قیاس اس لئے درست نہیں کہ قیاس کی شرط ثالث کی دوسری شرطہ بعینہ اصل کے حکم کا تعد یہ کرتا ہے اور وہ یہاں نہیں پایا جاتا لكونه کیونکہ اس سے یعنی اس قیاس سے تعبیر لِلحُرْمَةِ المُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكُفَّارَةِ حرمت کا حکم جو اصل پر یعنی مسلمان کے حق میں کفارہ سے ختم ہو جاتا ہے فرع میں
