اہل نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کفارہ عبادہ اور مزاء دونوں کے در میان دائر ہے یہاں پر ایک شبہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ کا فراپنے غلام کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے اور کفارہ ظہار میں غلام کا آزاد کرنا بھی شامل ہے۔ تو بعض لوگوں نے اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا کہ ذمی غلام آزاد کرنے کا اہل ہے لیکن اس تحریر ( آزادی غلام کا اہل نہیں ہے جس کا قائم مقام صوم ہو۔ کیونکہ صوم عبادت ہے جس کا ذمی اہل میں ہے ) ولا لتعدية الحكم من الناسی (ج) اور بھول کر کھائی لینے والے پر قیاس کر کے مکروہ اور خاطی کے حق میں حکم کا منتقل کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کا عذر بھول کر کھانے والے کے عذر سے بہت ہی کم ہے یہ تیسری شرط کی تفریح ہے اور شرط یہ ہے کہ فرع اصل کی نظیر ہو کیونکہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب کہ بھول کر کھانے والے (ناسی) حالانکہ فعل آکل و شرب میں عام ہے عمد اکھا پی رہا ہے اور اس کا عذر مقبول ہے تو وہ شخص روزہ یاد ہوتے ہوئے بلا اختیار پانی حلق میں اتر گیا یا کسی نے زبردستی روزہ توڑنے پر مجبور کر دیا۔ ان کا عذر قابل قبول ہو جانا چاہیے کیونکہ وہ اپنے اختیار سے عمر اکھالی نہیں رہا۔ الہند اولی ہے کہ الکا عذر قبول کیا جائے ونحن نقول ہم جواب دیں گے کہ خاطی و مکرہ دونوں کا بندر ناسی سے کمتر ہے کیونکہ نسیان بغیر اختیار کے انسان پر طاری ہوتا ہے اور نسیان صاحب حق کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے کہ خالق و مالک نے بھول کر اس کے ذہن میں ڈالدیا ہے اور نکرہ اور خاطی کا فعل افطار صوم صاحب حق کی طرف ہے نہیں ہے کیونکہ خاطی کو روز میاد ہوتا ہے مگر مضمضہ (کی) کرنے میں جو احتیاط کرنا چاہیے اس میں کو تاہی کرنا ہے حتی کہ پانی اس سے حلق میں داخل ہو گیا۔ وَالْمُكْرَهُ أَكْرَمَةَ الإِنْسانُ وَالْجَاهُ إِلَيْهِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ عُدْرُ هُمَا كَعَدْرِ النَّاسِي فَيَفْسِدْ صَوْمُهُمَا وَقَدْ فَرَعْنَاهُمَا فِيْمَا سَبَقَ عَلَى كَوْن الأصل مُخَالِفًا للقياس ولا ضير
Some hold it impermissible, while the majority permit qiyas in language. A Hanafi once asked the Shafi'is: 'Why is the bottle called qārūrah?' They said: 'Because water settles in it.' He said: 'Your stomach also settles water, so it should be called qārūrah.' Then he asked: 'Why is the watercress called jarjīr?' They said: 'Because it moves on the surface.' He said: 'Your beard also moves, so it should be called jarjīr.' They were bewildered and silent. Regarding the validity of dhihar of a dhimmi: this is a branch on the second condition, that the reasoning for the validity of dhihar of a dhimmi is not sound as al-Shafi'i reasoned, saying: 'His divorce is valid, so his dhihar is valid like a Muslim.' The second condition—the transfer of the ruling in its essence—is absent, because this reasoning changes the finite prohibition (ended by expiation) in the original (the Muslim) into an infinite prohibition in the branch, for the Muslim's dhihar ends with expiation, while the dhimmi's dhihar becomes perpetual since he is not qualified for expiation, which revolves between worship and punishment. It is said he is qualified for emancipation but not for the fasting that is the substitute for emancipation, because fasting is an act of worship for which the dhimmi is not qualified. Similarly, the transfer of the ruling from the forgetful one (nāsī) to the mistaken (khāṭi') and coerced (mukrah) is not valid because their excuse is lesser than his. This is a branch on the third condition: that the branch be analogous to the original. Al-Shafi'i says: 'When the forgetful one is excused despite being intentional in the act itself, then it is more appropriate that the mistaken and coerced, who are not intentional in the act itself, be excused.' We say: Their excuse is lesser than his, because forgetfulness occurs without choice and is attributed to the Lord of the right, while the act of the mistaken and coerced is not from the Lord of the right. The mistaken one knows the fast but is negligent in gargling until water enters his throat, and the coerced one is compelled by a person. So their excuse is not like that of the forgetful one; thus their fast is broken. We have already derived this on the basis that the original is contrary to qiyas, and there is no harm.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i arguments for the validity of dhihar (a form of pre-Islamic divorce) from a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim protection) and for excusing the mistaken and coerced in breaking fast. It is part of a larger discussion on the conditions of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author first recounts an anecdote where a Hanafi scholar challenges Shafi'i knowledge of etymologies by showing that their claimed basis for qiyas in language leads to absurd conclusions: if a bottle is named qārūrah because water settles in it, then the stomach should also be called qārūrah; if watercress is named jarjīr because it moves on the ground, then the beard should also be called jarjīr. This undermines the Shafi'i claim that they can know the wad' (original coinage) of all names, which they use for qiyas. Then the author addresses the second condition of qiyas: that the ruling in the branch must be the same in essence as in the original. Shafi'i argues that since a dhimmi's divorce is valid, his dhihar should also be valid like a Muslim's. The Hanafi response is that this reasoning changes the nature of the ruling: a Muslim's dhihar is a finite prohibition that can be expiated, while a dhimmi's dhihar would become permanent because he is not eligible for expiation (kaffarah), which involves worship (e.g., fasting) that a dhimmi cannot perform. Even though a dhimmi can free a slave, he cannot perform the substitute (fasting) if he cannot free a slave. Thus the ruling in the branch is not identical, so qiyas fails. Next, regarding the third condition: the branch must be analogous to the original. Shafi'i argues that if the forgetful person (nāsī) is excused despite intentionally eating, then the mistaken (khāti') and coerced (mukrah) should be even more excusable. The Hanafi response: the forgetful person's act is not under his control and is attributed to Allah (the Owner of the right), while the mistaken person is negligent in takin precautions (e.g., in rinsing the mouth) and the coerced is forced by a human. Their excuses are much weaker, so they are not excused, and their fast is broken. This shows the Hanafi commitment to strict conditions for qiyas.

Key Terms
ظِهَار (dhihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back', which makes her forbidden until expiation is performed.
ذِمِّي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, subject to Islamic law in civil matters but not in worship.
كَفَّارَة (kaffarah): Expiation required for certain acts, such as dhihar; includes freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor.
تَعْدِيَةُ الْحُكْمِ بِعَيْنِهِ (ta'diyat al-hukm bi 'aynihi): The second condition of qiyas: the ruling must be transferred identically from the original to the branch without change.
قِيَاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi text argue that dhihar of a dhimmi is not valid by qiyas on divorce?
A) Because the dhimmi is not a Muslim.
B) Because the ruling would become permanent (without expiation) unlike the Muslim's dhihar which ends with expiation.
C) Because qiyas is not allowed in matters of divorce.
D) Because the original ruling is based on revelation, not analogy.

Key Takeaway
The second condition of qiyas requires the ruling in the branch to be identical in essence to the original; if it changes, qiyas is invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
The Third Condition of Qiyas: The Branch Must Be Analogous – Refuting Qiyas for the Mistaken and Coerced in Fasting
Refutation of qiyas for excusing the mistaken and coerced in fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the third condition of qiyas (that the branch must be analogous to the original) to evaluate whether the mistaken (khāṭi') and coerced (mukrah) in breaking fast should be treated like the forgetful (nāsī).

Core Idea
A qiyas fails if the branch differs in a legally relevant way from the original, even if they share a superficial similarity.

This lesson continues the Hanafi critique of Shafi'i qiyas, now focusing on the third condition: the branch must be a true analogy (nazīr) to the original in the specific aspect that makes the original ruling applicable. The Shafi'i argue that since the forgetful person (nāsī) is excused in fasting, the mistaken (khāṭi') and coerced (mukrah) should be excused a fortiori. The Hanafi refutation shows that their excuses are qualitatively different—one is negligent, the other is coerced by a human—while the forgetful is not at fault. Thus the branch is not analogous.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i Qiyas for Excusing the Mistaken and Coerced
The Shafi'i argue: the forgetful person (nāsī) who eats while fasting is excused (fast valid) because he did not intend to break the fast. Since the mistaken (khāṭi') and coerced (mukrah) also did not intend to break the fast, they should be excused by qiyas. This is an argument a fortiori (awlā).
2
Identify the Third Condition of Qiyas
The third condition requires that the branch (far') be truly analogous (nazīr) to the original (asl) in the relevant aspect. If there is a legally significant difference, qiyas fails.
Hanafi usul emphasizes that the analogy must hold in the specific characteristic that justifies the ruling.
3
Hanafi Differentiation: Nature of the Excuse
The Hanafi response distinguishes the three cases. The forgetful person's act is beyond his control and is attributed to Allah (the Owner of the right). The mistaken person is negligent: he knows the fast but fails to take proper precaution (e.g., gargling too deeply). The coerced is forced by a human. Their acts are still voluntary in a way that the forgetful's is not.
Thus the branch (khāṭi'/mukrah) is not analogous to the original (nāsī).
4
Practical Outcome (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
According to the Hanafi school, the fast of the mistaken and coerced is invalid (they must make it up), while the forgetful's fast remains valid. This is the practical consequence of the failed qiyas.
5
Relate to the Broader Usul Principle
This example illustrates the Hanafi commitment to strict conditions for qiyas. The third condition ensures that qiyas does not equate cases that are different in their legal cause (ʿilla). The Hanafi analysis scrutinizes the nature of the act and its attribution.
The forgetful is excused by textual proof (hadith), while the mistaken and coerced are not covered by that text.

یہ کرتا ہے اور وہ یہاں نہیں پایا جاتا لكونه کیونکہ اس سے یعنی اس قیاس سے تعبیر لِلحُرْمَةِ المُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكُفَّارَةِ حرمت کا حکم جو اصل پر یعنی مسلمان کے حق میں کفارہ سے ختم ہو جاتا ہے فرع میں اہل نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کفارہ عبادہ اور مزاء دونوں کے در میان دائر ہے یہاں پر ایک شبہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ کا فراپنے غلام کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے اور کفارہ ظہار میں غلام کا آزاد کرنا بھی شامل ہے۔ تو بعض لوگوں نے اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا کہ ذمی غلام آزاد کرنے کا اہل ہے لیکن اس تحریر ( آزادی غلام کا اہل نہیں ہے جس کا قائم مقام صوم ہو۔ کیونکہ صوم عبادت ہے جس کا ذمی اہل میں ہے ) ولا لتعدية الحكم من الناسی (ج) اور بھول کر کھائی لینے والے پر قیاس کر کے مکروہ اور خاطی کے حق میں حکم کا منتقل کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کا عذر بھول کر کھانے والے کے عذر سے بہت ہی کم ہے یہ تیسری شرط کی تفریح ہے اور شرط یہ ہے کہ فرع اصل کی نظیر ہو کیونکہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب کہ بھول کر کھانے والے (ناسی) حالانکہ فعل آکل و شرب میں عام ہے عمد اکھا پی رہا ہے اور اس کا عذر مقبول ہے تو وہ شخص روزہ یاد ہوتے ہوئے بلا اختیار پانی حلق میں اتر گیا یا کسی نے زبردستی روزہ توڑنے پر مجبور کر دیا۔ ان کا عذر قابل قبول ہو جانا چاہیے کیونکہ وہ اپنے اختیار سے عمر اکھالی نہیں رہا۔ الہند اولی ہے کہ الکا عذر قبول کیا جائے ونحن نقول ہم جواب دیں گے کہ خاطی و مکرہ دونوں کا بندر ناسی سے کمتر ہے کیونکہ نسیان بغیر اختیار کے انسان پر طاری ہوتا ہے اور نسیان صاحب حق کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے کہ خالق و مالک نے بھول کر اس کے ذہن میں ڈالدیا ہے اور نکرہ اور خاطی کا فعل افطار صوم صاحب حق کی طرف ہے نہیں ہے کیونکہ خاطی کو روز میاد ہوتا ہے مگر مضمضہ (کی) کرنے میں جو احتیاط کرنا چاہیے اس میں کو تاہی کرنا ہے حتی کہ پانی اس سے حلق میں داخل ہو گیا۔ وَالْمُكْرَهُ أَكْرَمَةَ الإِنْسانُ وَالْجَاهُ إِلَيْهِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ عُدْرُ هُمَا كَعَدْرِ النَّاسِي فَيَفْسِدْ صَوْمُهُمَا وَقَدْ فَرَعْنَاهُمَا فِيْمَا سَبَقَ عَلَى كَوْن الأصل مُخَالِفًا للقياس ولا ضير
Some hold it impermissible, while the majority permit qiyas in language. A Hanafi once asked the Shafi'is: 'Why is the bottle called qārūrah?' They said: 'Because water settles in it.' He said: 'Your stomach also settles water, so it should be called qārūrah.' Then he asked: 'Why is the watercress called jarjīr?' They said: 'Because it moves on the surface.' He said: 'Your beard also moves, so it should be called jarjīr.' They were bewildered and silent. Regarding the validity of dhihar of a dhimmi: this is a branch on the second condition, that the reasoning for the validity of dhihar of a dhimmi is not sound as al-Shafi'i reasoned, saying: 'His divorce is valid, so his dhihar is valid like a Muslim.' The second condition—the transfer of the ruling in its essence—is absent, because this reasoning changes the finite prohibition (ended by expiation) in the original (the Muslim) into an infinite prohibition in the branch, for the Muslim's dhihar ends with expiation, while the dhimmi's dhihar becomes perpetual since he is not qualified for expiation, which revolves between worship and punishment. It is said he is qualified for emancipation but not for the fasting that is the substitute for emancipation, because fasting is an act of worship for which the dhimmi is not qualified. Similarly, the transfer of the ruling from the forgetful one (nāsī) to the mistaken (khāṭi') and coerced (mukrah) is not valid because their excuse is lesser than his. This is a branch on the third condition: that the branch be analogous to the original. Al-Shafi'i says: 'When the forgetful one is excused despite being intentional in the act itself, then it is more appropriate that the mistaken and coerced, who are not intentional in the act itself, be excused.' We say: Their excuse is lesser than his, because forgetfulness occurs without choice and is attributed to the Lord of the right, while the act of the mistaken and coerced is not from the Lord of the right. The mistaken one knows the fast but is negligent in gargling until water enters his throat, and the coerced one is compelled by a person. So their excuse is not like that of the forgetful one; thus their fast is broken. We have already derived this on the basis that the original is contrary to qiyas, and there is no harm.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i arguments for the validity of dhihar (a form of pre-Islamic divorce) from a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim protection) and for excusing the mistaken and coerced in breaking fast. It is part of a larger discussion on the conditions of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author first recounts an anecdote where a Hanafi scholar challenges Shafi'i knowledge of etymologies by showing that their claimed basis for qiyas in language leads to absurd conclusions: if a bottle is named qārūrah because water settles in it, then the stomach should also be called qārūrah; if watercress is named jarjīr because it moves on the ground, then the beard should also be called jarjīr. This undermines the Shafi'i claim that they can know the wad' (original coinage) of all names, which they use for qiyas. Then the author addresses the second condition of qiyas: that the ruling in the branch must be the same in essence as in the original. Shafi'i argues that since a dhimmi's divorce is valid, his dhihar should also be valid like a Muslim's. The Hanafi response is that this reasoning changes the nature of the ruling: a Muslim's dhihar is a finite prohibition that can be expiated, while a dhimmi's dhihar would become permanent because he is not eligible for expiation (kaffarah), which involves worship (e.g., fasting) that a dhimmi cannot perform. Even though a dhimmi can free a slave, he cannot perform the substitute (fasting) if he cannot free a slave. Thus the ruling in the branch is not identical, so qiyas fails. Next, regarding the third condition: the branch must be analogous to the original. Shafi'i argues that if the forgetful person (nāsī) is excused despite intentionally eating, then the mistaken (khāti') and coerced (mukrah) should be even more excusable. The Hanafi response: the forgetful person's act is not under his control and is attributed to Allah (the Owner of the right), while the mistaken person is negligent in takin precautions (e.g., in rinsing the mouth) and the coerced is forced by a human. Their excuses are much weaker, so they are not excused, and their fast is broken. This shows the Hanafi commitment to strict conditions for qiyas.

Key Terms
نَاسِي (nāsī): A person who forgets he is fasting and eats or drinks inadvertently.
خَاطِئ (khāṭi'): A person who mistakenly breaks his fast, e.g., by swallowing water while gargling due to negligence.
مُكْرَه (mukrah): A person who is coerced into breaking his fast by another person.
قِيَاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, why is the mistaken person (khāṭi') not excused in fasting even though he did not deliberately break the fast?
A) Because his fast is already invalid due to negligence.
B) Because he is not excused by qiyas on the forgetful, as his excuse is weaker.
C) Because mistake is not mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because the Shafi'i qiyas is incorrect.

Key Takeaway
The third condition of qiyas requires that the branch be a true analogy (nazīr) to the original in the specific legal aspect; otherwise, the analogy is invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Second Condition of Qiyas: Zihar of a Dhimmi
Explains the second condition of qiyas with the example of zihar of a dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects the analogy (qiyas) of a dhimmi's zihar to a Muslim's, and identify the violation of the second condition of qiyas (exact transference of ruling).

Core Idea
Qiyas fails if the ruling changes in transfer — zihar of a dhimmi would create permanent prohibition, violating exact transference.

In this lesson, we explore a classic usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is concerning the validity of zihar (a form of divorce-like repudiation) performed by a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen). The disagreement hinges on the second condition of qiyas: that the ruling of the original case must transfer exactly to the new case without change. Understanding this condition helps you evaluate when analogical reasoning is sound and when it breaks down.

Guided Path
1
State the Second Condition of Qiyas
Recall that for qiyas to be valid, the ruling of the original (asl) must be transferred exactly to the branch (far') without any change in the ruling itself. This is called 'ta'diyat al-hukm bi 'aynihi.'
This condition distinguishes valid qiyas from flawed analogy.
2
Identify the Original and Branch in this Dispute
The original case is a Muslim's zihar, which results in a temporary prohibition ending with expiation (kaffarah). The branch is a dhimmi's zihar. The Shafi'i analogy tries to transfer the ruling from a Muslim's divorce (which is valid for dhimmi) to zihar.
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since a dhimmi's divorce is valid, so should his zihar be valid.
3
Analyze Hanafi Critique: Why the Ruling Changes
The Hanafis argue that the ruling cannot transfer exactly: for a Muslim, the prohibition ends with expiation (fasting, freeing a slave, etc.), but a dhimmi cannot perform expiation because parts of it (like fasting) are acts of worship he is not qualified for. Thus the prohibition becomes permanent in the branch, a change in the ruling.
The change (taghayyur al-hukm) violates the second condition, making qiyas invalid.
4
Address the Objection: Dhimmi Can Free a Slave
An objection: a dhimmi can free a slave, so why can't he expiate? The Hanafi response: the freeing that can be substituted by fasting is not valid for a dhimmi because fasting (a form of worship) is part of the expiation options. He could free a slave only if the full expiation were possible, but since he cannot fast, the freeing is not a valid substitute.
Thus the inability to perform any part of expiation renders the entire expiation impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا لِصِحَّةِ ظِهَارِ الذِّمِّيِّ (ب) اور ذمی کا ظہار صحیح ہونے کے لئے: طلاق پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے یہ دوسری شرط کی تفریح ہے یعنی مسلمان کی طرح کافر کی طلاق صحیح ہونے کی وجہ سے کافر کے ظہار کو بھی طلاق پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ امام شافعی نے ایسا کیا ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ذمی کی طلاق صحیح ہے۔ لہذا اس کا ظہار بھی مسلمان کی طرح درست ہو گا۔ ہمارے نزدیک یہ قیاس اس لئے درست نہیں کہ قیاس کی شرط ثالث کی دوسری شرطہ بعینہ اصل کے حکم کا تعدیہ کرتا ہے اور وہ یہاں نہیں پایا جاتا لكونه کیونکہ اس سے یعنی اس قیاس سے تغییر للحرمة المتناهیة بالكفارة حرمت کا حکم جو اصل پر یعنی مسلمان کے حق میں کفارہ سے ختم ہو جاتا ہے فرع میں اس کے اندر تبدیلی لازم آتی ہے کفارہ سے ختم نہ ہو کر ہمیشہ کے لئے حرمت ثابت ہو جائے کیونکہ مسلمان کا ظہار کفارہ پر ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ذمی کافر کا ظہار دائمی باقی رہتا ہے کیونکہ وہ کفارہ ادا کرنے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کفارہ عبادت اور جزاء دونوں کے درمیان دائر ہے یہاں پر ایک شبہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ کافر اپنے غلام کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے اور کفارہ ظہار میں غلام کا آزاد کرنا بھی شامل ہے۔ تو بعض لوگوں نے اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا کہ ذمی غلام آزاد کرنے کا اہل ہے لیکن اس تحریر (آزادی غلام کا اہل نہیں ہے جس کا قائم مقام صوم ہو۔ کیونکہ صوم عبادت ہے جس کا ذمی اہل نہیں ہے)
And for the validity of zihar of the dhimmi: it is not correct to analogize it to divorce. This is a branch of the second condition, meaning that just as the divorce of a disbeliever is valid like that of a Muslim, so too his zihar should be analogized to divorce. Imam Shafi'i did this, saying that the divorce of a dhimmi is valid, so his zihar is also valid like a Muslim's. According to us, this qiyas is not valid because the second condition of qiyas requires the exact transference of the ruling of the original, and that is not found here because this qiyas leads to a change in the ruling: the ruling of prohibition that ends with expiation in the original (for a Muslim) becomes in the branch a permanent prohibition without expiation, since the dhimmi cannot perform expiation because expiation involves both worship and recompense. An objection arises: a dhimmi can free his slave, and freeing a slave is part of zihar expiation. Some answered that a dhimmi is capable of freeing a slave, but not the type of freeing that is substituted by fasting, because fasting is worship that a dhimmi is not qualified for.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage discusses the second condition of qiyas, illustrated by the example of zihar of a dhimmi. The condition is that the ruling of the original must transfer exactly to the branch without change. Imam Shafi'i analogized the zihar of a dhimmi to divorce, arguing that since a dhimmi's divorce is valid, his zihar should also be valid. The Hanafi response is that this qiyas changes the ruling: for a Muslim, zihar results in a temporary prohibition that ends with expiation, but for a dhimmi, expiation is impossible (since it involves worship like fasting), so the prohibition would become permanent. This violates the condition of exact transference. The passage also addresses a potential objection that a dhimmi can free a slave (a form of expiation), but the Hanafi reply distinguishes that the type of freeing that can be substituted by fasting is not valid for a dhimmi, as fasting is pure worship.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce-like repudiation where a husband compares his wife to his mother, requiring expiation
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection with certain rights and obligations
تغییر الحكم (taghayyur al-hukm): Change in the ruling when transferring it from original to branch, invalidating qiyas
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the analogy of zihar of a dhimmi to a Muslim's zihar?
A) Because a dhimmi cannot own slaves
B) Because the ruling would become permanent without expiation, changing the original ruling
C) Because zihar is invalid for all non-Muslims
D) Because divorce of a dhimmi is invalid

Key Takeaway
The second condition of qiyas requires exact transference of the ruling; if the branch cannot fulfill a necessary condition of the original (like expiation), the ruling changes and qiyas is invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Third Condition of Qiyas: The Branch Must Be Analogous to the Original
Explains third condition of qiyas using nasi/khati/mukrah example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a proposed analogy (qiyas) satisfies the third condition that the branch (far') must be exactly analogous (nazir) to the original (asl), and apply this condition to the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on the fast of a mistaken/coerced person.

Core Idea
For qiyas to be valid, the branch must exactly match the original; different excuses break the analogy.

This lesson examines a classic usuli dispute: can we compare the case of a mistaken or coerced fasting person to that of a forgetful person? The answer hinges on the third condition of qiyas—that the branch must be analogous (nazir) to the original. Through this example, you will learn how Hanafi scholars apply this condition to reject a seemingly a fortiori argument from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third condition of qiyas
The condition is that the branch (far') must be exactly like the original (asl) in the effective cause ('illah). If there is a distinction, qiyas is invalid.
This is a key gatekeeping condition in Hanafi usul.
2
State the ruling on the forgetful fasting person (nasi)
The forgetful person who eats or drinks while fasting has a valid fast because forgetfulness is an excuse from Allah that overcomes him without choice.
This is established from hadith: 'Whoever forgets while fasting, let him complete his fast.'
3
Explain the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if a forgetful person who eats intentionally (in a general sense) is excused, then those who break fast involuntarily (mistaken) or under coercion have a stronger claim to leniency, so their fast should also be valid.
This is an a fortiori (awla) reasoning.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the excuse of the forgetful person is stronger because it is directly from Allah without any fault of his own. In contrast, the mistaken person is negligent (fails to be careful in rinsing), and the coerced person chooses to break the fast to save his life. Therefore, their excuses are not analogous.
The crucial distinction is the nature of the excuse: divine vs. human causation.
5
Conclude the dispute and note the principle
Since the branch (mistaken/coerced) is not analogous to the original (forgetful), the qiyas is invalid. This illustrates that qiyas must be based on exact similarity, and many rulings branch from different principles.
The Hanafi position is that their fast is invalid; the Shafi'i position is that it is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا لِتَعْدِيَةِ الْحُكْمِ مِنَ النَّاسِي (ج) اور بھول کر کھانے والے پر قیاس کر کے مکروہ اور خاطی کے حق میں حکم کا منتقل کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کا عذر بھول کر کھانے والے کے عذر سے بہت ہی کم ہے یہ تیسری شرط کی تفریح ہے اور شرط یہ ہے کہ فرع اصل کی نظیر ہو کیونکہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب کہ بھول کر کھانے والے (ناسی) حالانکہ فعل اکل و شرب میں عام ہے عمدا کھا پی رہا ہے اور اس کا عذر مقبول ہے تو وہ شخص روزہ یاد ہوتے ہوئے بلا اختیار پانی حلق میں اتر گیا یا کسی نے زبردستی روزہ توڑنے پر مجبور کر دیا۔ ان کا عذر قابل قبول ہو جانا چاہیے کیونکہ وہ اپنے اختیار سے عمدا نہیں کھا رہا۔ الہند اولی ہے کہ الک عذر قبول کیا جائے ونحن نقول ہم جواب دیں گے کہ خاطی و مکرہ دونوں کا عذر ناسی سے کمتر ہے کیونکہ نسیان بغیر اختیار کے انسان پر طاری ہوتا ہے اور نسیان صاحب حق کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے کہ خالق و مالک نے بھول کر اس کے ذہن میں ڈال دیا ہے اور مکرہ اور خاطی کا فعل افطار صوم صاحب حق کی طرف ہے نہیں ہے کیونکہ خاطی کو روزہ یاد ہوتا ہے مگر مضمضہ (کرنے) میں جو احتیاط کرنا چاہیے اس میں کوتاہی کرنا ہے حتی کہ پانی اس سے حلق میں داخل ہو گیا۔ وَالْمُكْرَهُ أَكْرَمَةَ الْإِنْسَانُ وَالْجَاهُ إِلَيْهِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ عُذْرُهُمَا كَعُذْرِ النَّاسِي فَيَفْسِدْ صَوْمُهُمَا وَقَدْ فَرَعْنَاهُمَا فِيْمَا سَبَقَ عَلَى كَوْن الْأَصْلِ مُخَالِفًا لِلْقِيَاسِ وَلَا ضَيْرَ فِيهِ فَإِنَّ أَكْثَرَ الْمَسَائِلِ يَتَفَرَّعُ عَلَى أَصُولٍ مُخْتَلِفَةٍ
And not for the transference of the ruling from the forgetful person: it is not correct to analogize from the forgetful person to the mistaken and the coerced. Because the excuse of both is much less than the excuse of the forgetful person. This is a branch of the third condition, and the condition is that the branch be analogous to the original. Because Imam Shafi'i says that when the forgetful person (nasi) eats and drinks intentionally (in a general sense) and his excuse is accepted, then the person who, while remembering his fast, water enters his throat involuntarily, or someone forces him to break his fast – his excuse should also be accepted, because he did not eat intentionally. At the end, it is more appropriate that such excuses be accepted. We say that the excuse of both the mistaken and coerced is less than that of the forgetful, because forgetfulness overcomes a person without his choice, and it is attributed to the owner of the right (Allah), who caused the forgetfulness. But the act of breaking the fast by the mistaken and coerced is not attributed to the owner of the right, because the mistaken person remembers his fast but fails to be careful in rinsing his mouth, leading to water entering his throat. And the coerced person is forced by a human, and he intends to break his fast to save his life. Therefore their excuse is not like that of the forgetful, and their fast is invalidated. We have already branched these two cases on the basis that the original is contrary to analogy, and there is no harm in that because most issues branch from different principles.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage explains the third condition of qiyas: the branch must be exactly analogous to the original. The example is the ruling on the fast of a forgetful person (nasi) compared to one who makes a mistake (khati') or is coerced (mukrah). Imam Shafi'i argues that if a person who forgets and eats intentionally is excused, then those who break their fast involuntarily or under coercion should be excused a fortiori. The Hanafi response is that the excuse of forgetfulness is stronger because it is directly from Allah and without choice, while the mistaken person has some negligence, and the coerced person chooses to break the fast to save his life. Hence, their fast is invalid. This shows that the condition of exact analogy is not met, so qiyas is invalid. The text also notes that many issues branch from different principles, and there is no harm in that.

Key Terms
ناسی (nasi): A person who forgets he is fasting and eats or drinks
خاطی (khati'): A person who makes a mistake while fasting, e.g., water enters throat due to lack of caution
مکرہ (mukrah): A person coerced to break his fast
شرط ثالث (shart thalith): Third condition of qiyas: the branch must be analogous to the original

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject analogizing the mistaken/coerced person to the forgetful person regarding the validity of the fast?
A) Because the mistaken person ate intentionally
B) Because the excuse of forgetfulness is stronger and directly from Allah, while the mistaken person has negligence and the coerced person chooses to break the fast
C) Because the fast of a forgetful person is invalid
D) Because qiyas is not allowed in rulings about fasting

Key Takeaway
The third condition of qiyas requires the branch to be exactly analogous; a stronger excuse in the original prevents analogy if the branch's excuse is weaker or different.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Fourth Condition of Qiyas: No Text in the Branch
Discusses fourth condition of qiyas with examples and an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourth condition of qiyas to determine when analogy is invalid due to an existing text in the branch.

Core Idea
If a text exists in the branch, qiyas is unnecessary unless the text agrees with qiyas.

This lesson unpacks the fourth condition of qiyas: the branch must not have its own specific text. When a text exists, analogy is not needed unless the text supports the same ruling. We explore the Hanafi critique of Shafi'i's qiyas on slave expiation and address a key objection about the riba hadith, distinguishing between specification (takhsis) and change of ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth condition
State the fourth condition in your own words: there must be no specific text in the branch. If a text exists, qiyas is not required, unless the text agrees with qiyas (then both can be cited).
This is a condition for the validity of qiyas in usul al-fiqh.
2
Examine the slave expiation example
Look at the example: expiation for killing requires a believing slave (text restricts), but for oath and zihar, the Quranic text says 'freeing a slave' without faith. Shafi'i analogized to killing, but Hanafis argue the text in the branch is sufficient, so qiyas is invalid.
3
Understand the fourth condition's nuance
When the branch text contradicts qiyas, qiyas is invalid. When it agrees, both can be used. The author of al-Hidayah often cites both naqli and aqli evidence to show consistency.
This reinforces that qiyas is not redundant but confirmatory.
4
Address the riba objection
An objection: Hanafis used qiyas to extend riba from food to other items, but this seems to change the original general prohibition (small and large amounts) to only large amounts. The response: this is takhsis (specification), not a change in ruling. The text's ruling remains valid, but its scope is limited.
Takhsis is not a violation of the fourth condition because the original ruling remains unchanged in its applied area.
5
Apply to new cases
Given a hypothetical branch with a text that agrees with qiyas, decide whether qiyas is valid. Or, given a branch text that contradicts qiyas, explain why qiyas is invalid.

Source Text

وَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ الْإِيمَانُ (د) اور كفارة يمين اور كفارہ ظہار میں جو غلام آزاد کيا جاتا ہے اس کے لئے ایمان کی شرط لگانا (كفارہ قتل پر قیاس کر کے) درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ فرع کے بارہ میں مستقل نص وارد ہے اس لئے لازم آتا ہے کہ فرع کے بارہ میں مستقل نص موجود ہے اور قیاس کی ضرورت نہیں۔ فِي رَقَبَةٍ كَفَارَةِ الْيَمِينِ وَالظُّهَارِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعْدِيَةٌ إِلَى مَا فِيْهِ نَصٌّ بِتَغْيِيْرِهِ تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الرَّابِعِ وَهُوَ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ النَّصُّ فِي الْفَرْعِ وَهَبْنَا النَّصُّ الْمُطْلَقُ عَنْ قَيْدِ الْإِيمَانِ مَوْجُوْدٌ فِي رَقَبَةِ كَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِينِ وَالظُّهَارِ فَلَا فِيْمَا يُخَالِفُ الْقِيَاسَ نَصُّ الْفَرْعِ وَأَمَّا فِيْمَا يُوَافِقُهُ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِأَنْ يَثْبُتَ الْحُكْمُ بِالْقِيَاسِ وَالنَّصِّ جَمِيعًا كَمَا هُوَ دَأْبُ صَاحِبِ الْهِدَايَةِ يَسْتَدِلُ لِكُلِّ حُكْمٍ بِالْمَعْقُولِ وَالْمَنْقُولِ تَنْبِيْهًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنِ النَّصُّ مَوْجُوْدًا لَثَبَتَ بِالْقِيَاسِ أَيْضًا وَالشَّرْطُ الرَّابِعُ أَنْ يَبْقَى حُكْمُ النَّصِّ بَعْدَ التَّعْلِيْلِ عَلَى مَا كَانَ قَبْلَهُ إِنَّمَا صَرَّحَ بِقَيْدِ الرَّابِعِ لِئِلَا يَتَوَهَّمَ أَنَّ الشَّرْطَ الثَّالِثَ لَمَّا تَضَمَّنَ شُرُوْطًا أَرْبَعَةً كَانَ هَذَا شَرْطًا سَابِعًا فَأَطْلَقَ الرَّابِعَ تَنْبِيْهًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ شَرْطٌ وَاحِدٌ وَمَعْنَى بَقَاءِ حُكْمِ النَّصِّ أَنْ يَتَغَيَّرَ عَمَّا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ سِوَى إِنَّهُ تَعَدَّى إِلَى الْفَرْعِ فَعَمَّ وَإِنَّمَا خَصَّصْنَا الْقَلِيْلَ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ لَا تَبِيعُوا الطَّعَامَ بِالطَّعَامِ إِلَّا سَوَاءً بِسَوَاءٍ جَوَابُ سُؤَالٍ مُقَدَّرٍ وَهُوَ إِنَّكُمْ قُلْتُمْ أَنْ لَا يَتَغَيَّرَ حُكْمُ الْأَصْلِ بَعْدَ التَّعْلِيْلِ وَفِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَبِيعُوا الطَّعَامَ بِالطَّعَامِ لَمَّا عَلَّلْتُمْ حُرْمَةَ الرِّبَا بِالْقَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ وَعَدَّيْتُمْ إِلَى غَيْرِ الطَّعَامِ فَقَدْ خَصَّصْتُمُ الْقَلِيْلَ مِنَ النَّصِّ الدَّالِّ عَلَى حُرْمَةِ الرِّبَا فِي الْقَلِيْلِ وَالْكَثِيرِ وَأَقْصَرْتُمْ حُرُمَةَ الرِّبَا عَلَى الْكَثِيرِ فَقَط
And faith is not stipulated: for the slave in the expiation of an oath and zihar, stipulating faith (by analogy to expiation for killing) is not correct because there is a specific text regarding the branch. This is a branch of the fourth condition: that there be no text in the branch. And here, the absolute text without the condition of faith exists in the slave of expiation for oath and zihar, so it should not be analogized to the slave of expiation for killing which is restricted by faith, as Imam Shafi'i did, because there is no need for qiyas when a text exists. This is when the text in the branch contradicts qiyas. But when the text agrees with qiyas, there is no harm in establishing the ruling by both qiyas and the text, as is the practice of the author of al-Hidayah, who presents both rational and transmitted evidence for every ruling, indicating that even if the text were not present, the ruling would still be established by qiyas. The fourth condition is that the ruling of the text remains after ta'lil as it was before. He explicitly mentioned the fourth condition to prevent the misunderstanding that (since the third condition includes four sub-conditions) this might be considered a seventh condition; so he called it the fourth to show it is a single condition. The meaning of 'preserving the text's ruling' is that it does not change except that it extends to the branch. And we only specify the small amount from the hadith 'Do not sell food for food except like for like' as an answer to a hypothetical objection: you said that the ruling of the original should not change after ta'lil, but in the hadith, when you made the illah for the prohibition of riba as quantity and genus and extended it to non-food items, you specified the small amount from the text that indicates prohibition of riba in both small and large amounts, limiting the prohibition to large amounts only.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth condition of qiyas: there must be no specific text in the branch. The example is the requirement of faith in the slave for expiation. For expiation of killing, a believing slave is required, but for expiation of oath and zihar, the Quranic text does not stipulate faith. Imam Shafi'i analogized the latter to the former, but the Hanafi view is that the text in the branch (the absolute slave) is sufficient, so qiyas is unnecessary. If a text supports the ruling obtained by qiyas, both can be cited. The passage also clarifies the fourth condition: the ruling of the original must remain unchanged after ta'lil. An objection is addressed: the Hanafis themselves, by extending the prohibition of riba from food to other items via qiyas, have restricted the general prohibition of small and large amounts to only large amounts, which appears to change the original ruling. The response is that this is a specification (takhsis) of the generality of the text, not a change in the ruling.

Key Terms
شرط رابع (shart rabi'): Fourth condition of qiyas: no specific text exists in the branch, or if text exists supporting qiyas, both can be used
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification of a general text, not considered a change in ruling
علت (illah): The effective cause (ratio legis) that allows extension of ruling via qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the fourth condition of qiyas according to this passage?
A) The branch must have a specific text
B) The original ruling must not change after ta'lil, except that it extends to the branch
C) The illah must be explicit in the Quran
D) The branch must be contradictory to the text

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition ensures that qiyas is not used when a text already addresses the branch, preserving the primacy of textual evidence.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
The Fourth Condition of Qiyas: No Text in the Branch
Expanding the fourth condition of qiyas with examples from kaffara and riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourth condition of qiyas in Hanafi usul, apply it to the kaffara example, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument using the condition.

Core Idea
If a direct text exists in the branch, qiyas is invalid — even if the original has a similar ruling.

The fourth condition of qiyas in Hanafi usul is that the branch (far') must have no direct textual ruling (nass). This lesson unpacks that condition through two classical examples: the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over whether faith is required in the expiation for oath and zihar, and the Hanafi specification of the riba prohibition to large quantities only. Both examples illustrate when qiyas is blocked or qualified by the presence of a text in the branch.

Guided Path
1
Define the fourth condition
State clearly: qiyas is valid only when the branch has no direct text (nass) from Quran or Sunnah. If a text exists, qiyas is unnecessary and invalid if it contradicts the text.
This condition is distinct from the third condition (that the ruling of the original remains unchanged).
2
Apply to the kaffara dispute
Recall the Quranic verses: for oath (5:89) and zihar (58:3-4), the expiation is freeing a slave without mentioning faith; for killing (4:92), it is freeing a believing slave. The Hanafis keep the oath/zihar texts as absolute (mutlaq).
The Shafi'i school analogizes from killing to oath/zihar, requiring faith in all three.
3
Identify the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the illa (effective cause) for expiation is the same in all three cases, so the condition of faith should apply universally.
This is a qiyas from the muqayyad to the mutlaq.
4
Evaluate using the fourth condition
The Hanafi response: since the branch (oath/zihar) has its own direct text that is absolute, qiyas is invalid. The fourth condition is violated because a nass already exists in the branch.
Even if the qiyas seems logically sound, it cannot override an explicit text.
5
Note the nuance: supportive qiyas
The passage mentions that when qiyas agrees with the nass, both can be cited together, as al-Marghinani often does in al-Hidayah. This does not violate the condition because the nass is not overridden.
The condition only blocks contradictory qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بِتَغْيِيرِهِ تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرْطِ الرَّابِعِ وَهُوَ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ النَّصُّ فِي الْفَرْعِ وَهَبْنَا النَّصُّ الْمُطْلَقُ عَنْ قَيْدِ الْإِيمَانِ مَوْجُودٌ فِي رَقَبَةِ كَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِينِ النَّصِّ بَعْدَ التَّعْلِيلِ عَلَى مَا كَانَ قَبْلَهُ إِنَّمَا صَرَّحَ بِقَيْدِ الرَّابِعِ لِئَلَّا يَتَوَهَّمَ أَنَّ الشَّرْطَ الثَّالِثَ لَمَّا تَضَمَّنَ شُرُوطًا أَرْبَعَةً كَانَ هَذَا شَرْطًا بَعْدَ التَّعْلِيلِ وَفِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَبِيعُوا الطَّعَامَ بِالطَّعَامِ لَمَّا عَلَّلْتُمْ حُرْمَةَ الرِّبَا بِالْقَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ وَعَدَّيْتُمْ إِلَى غَيْرِ الطَّعَامِ فَقَدْ خَصَصْتُمُ الْقَلِيلَ مِنَ النَّصِّ الدَّالِّ عَلَى حُرْمَةِ الرِّبَا فِي الْقَلِيلِ وَالْكَثِيرِ وَأَقْصَرْتُمْ حُرْمَةَ الرِّبَا عَلَى الْكَثِيرِ فَقَطْ. والمكره أكرمة الإنسان الخ اور کمرہ کو انسان خلاف نہ ہونے کے بیان میں خاطی اور مکروہ کی مثال دی تھی پھر یہاں اس بیان میں کہ فرع کو اصل کی نظیر ہونی چاہیے جب ہی قیاس درست ہوگا کے تحت انھیں دونوں مثالوں کو تفریح میں بیان کیا ہے مگر اس میں کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ اکثر مسائل ایسے ہیں جو اصول مختلفہ سے متفرع کئے جاتے ہیں ۔ ولا يشترط الايمان (د) اور كفارة يمين اور کفارہ ظہار میں جو غلام آزاد کیا جاتا ہے اس کے لئے ایمان کی شرط لگانا (كفارہ قتل پر قیاس کر کے درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ فرع کے بارہ میں مستقل نص وارد ہے اس لئے لازم آتا ہے کہ فرع کے بارہ میں مستقل نص ہونے کے باوجود اس کے تقاضے کو چھوڑ کر اصل کے حکم کا تعدیہ لازم آتا ہے یہ چوتھی شرط کی تفریع ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ فرع میں نص وارد نہیں ہوئی ہو اور یہاں کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین پر غلام سے آزاد کرنے کا حکم ہے اور غلام ایمان کی قید سے مطلق ہے۔ لہذا کفارہ قتل کے غلام آزاد کرنے کے حکم پر اس کو قیاس کر کے ایمان کی قید کا اضافہ کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے جس طرح کے امام شافعی نے غلام کو ایمان کی قید سے مقید کیا ہے کیونکہ یہاں خلاف قیاس نص میں وارد ہے اور بہر حال جہاں موافق قیاس ہے تو اس میں حرج نہیں ہے کہ وہاں نص اور قیاس دونوں سے حکم لگایا جائے جیسے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی عادت ہے کہ وہ ہر حکم میں دلیل منقول و معقول ہر دو سے استدلال فرماتے ہیں اس بات پر آگاہ کرنے کے لئے اگر بالفرض نص موجود نہ ہوئی تو بھی حکم قیاس سے ثابت کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
In it: Indeed most issues branch from different principles. Faith is not required in the slave of expiation of oath and zihar, because it is a transference to something in which there is a text by changing it. That is a branching on the fourth condition, which is that there should be no text in the branch. And we have a text absolute from the condition of faith present in the slave of expiation of oath and zihar, so it should not be measured upon the slave of expiation of killing which is restricted by faith, similar to what al-Shafi'i did, because qiyas is not needed with the existence of text. And this is regarding where qiyas contradicts the text of the branch; as for where it agrees, there is no harm that the ruling be established by both qiyas and text, as is the habit of the author of al-Hidayah: he adduces for every ruling by reason and transmitted proof, indicating that even if the text were not present, it would be established by qiyas as well. And the fourth condition is that the ruling of the text after the cause remains as it was before. He stated the specification of fourth only to prevent misunderstanding that the third condition, since it includes four conditions, this would be a seventh condition; so he stated 'fourth' to indicate that it is one condition. And the meaning of the ruling remaining is that it does not change from what it was except that it extends to the branch so it becomes general. And we specified small (quantity) from his statement: 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal' - this is in answer to an estimated question: You said that the ruling of the original does not change after the cause, and in his statement peace be upon him 'Do not sell food for food' when you made the cause of prohibition of riba to be quantity and genus and you extended it to other than food, then you have specified the small (quantity) from the text which indicates prohibition of riba in small and large, and you restricted the prohibition of riba to only large.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the fourth condition of qiyas: that there must be no textual ruling (nass) in the branch. The author discusses the example of expiation (kaffara) for oath (yamin) and zihar versus expiation for killing (qatl). In the Hanafi school, faith (iman) is not required for the slave freed in expiation of yamin and zihar because the Quranic texts for these expiations do not stipulate faith, whereas the text for expiation of qatl does (Quran 4:92). Imam al-Shafi'i analogized from qatl to yamin/zihar, requiring faith. The Hanafi response is that qiyas is invalid when the branch already has its own text. Even if the text agrees with qiyas, it is permissible to cite both, as the author of al-Hidayah often does. The passage then addresses an objection: how can we specify the small amount from the general hadith 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal'? The answer is that the exception indicates generality of the preceding part, but only in large amounts; small amounts are excluded by exception.

Key Terms
الشرط الرابع (al-shart al-rabi'): The fourth condition of qiyas: that there should be no text (nass) in the branch (far')
نص في الفرع (nass fi al-far'): A textual ruling (from Quran or Sunnah) that directly applies to the branch case, making qiyas unnecessary
كفارة (kaffara): Expiation for breaking an oath (yamin), zihar, or accidental killing; the ruling on faith condition differs per type

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is qiyas from kaffara qatl to kaffara yamin invalid?
A) Because the cause (illa) is different
B) Because the original (asl) does not have a ruling
C) Because the branch (far') has its own text (nass)
D) Because the branch (far') lacks a suitable attribute

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition of qiyas ensures that direct textual rulings (nass) in the branch are not overridden by analogical reasoning.

The Fourth Condition of Qiyas: The Ruling Must Remain Unchanged After Ta'lil
Explaining the fourth condition of qiyas with a worked example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourth condition of qiyas in Hanafi usul and apply it to evaluate the validity of qiyas in cases where a text conflicts with analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
The ruling after ta'lil must remain identical to before; the cause cannot alter it.

In the previous lessons, we studied the first three conditions of qiyas. The fourth condition deals with the relationship between the ruling and its cause after ta'lil is established. This condition ensures that the cause (illah) does not modify the original ruling; rather, it merely justifies applying that ruling to a new case. The passage illustrates this with the example of expiation for dhihar and yamin versus expiation for qatl, where the Shafi'i school's qiyas would add a condition of faith, which the Hanafis reject as violating this condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth condition
The text states: 'والشرط الرابع أن تبقى' — the fourth condition is that the ruling remains as it was before. Understand that this condition is separate from the third condition (which has multiple parts).
The author explicitly mentions 'رابع' to avoid confusion.
2
Understand the meaning of 'baqa' al-hukm'
Baqa' al-hukm means no change occurs in the ruling's state after ta'lil. The ruling applied to the asl (original case) must be exactly the same when applied to the far' (new case) via qiyas.
The illah is merely a connector, not a modifier of the ruling.
3
Apply the condition to the given example
In the example, the ruling for expiation of dhihar and yamin is 'free a slave' without the condition of faith. The Hanafis argue that if one performs qiyas by taking the cause (kaffarah) from these to expiation of qatl, one must not add the condition of faith, because that would change the ruling (it would become 'free a believing slave').
The text in the asl (dhihar) is 'against qiyas' (without faith), so qiyas would be invalid if it adds a condition.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument
Imam al-Shafi'i performed a different qiyas by linking expiation of qatl (which requires a believing slave) to dhihar, thereby adding the condition of faith. The Hanafi response is that this violates the fourth condition because the ruling in the asl (freeing any slave) has been changed (to freeing a believing slave) by the qiyas itself.
The Hanafis follow the explicit text for dhihar, not the qiyas.
5
Note the Hanafi method of combining naqli and aqli
The commentator (author of Hidayah) habitually uses both transmitted (naqli) and rational (aqli) evidence to show that even if no text existed, qiyas alone could establish the ruling. However, when a text exists, it is followed, and qiyas is not needed to modify it.
This highlights the importance of textual evidence overriding analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہونے کے باوجود اس کے تقاضے کو چھوڑ کر اصل کے حکم کا تعدیہ لازم آتا ہے یہ چوتھی شرط کی تفریح ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ فرع میں نصی وارد نہیں ہوئی ہو اور یہاں کفارہ تمہار اور کفارہ یمین پر غلام سے آزاد کرنے کا حکم ہے اور غلام ایمان کی قید سے مطلق ہے۔ لہذا کفارہ قتل کے غلام آزاد کرنے کے حکم پر اس کو قیاس کر کے ایمان کی قید کا اضافہ کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے جس طرح کے امام شافعی نے غلام کو ایمان کی قید سے مقید کیا ہے کیونکہ یہاں خلاف قیاس نص میں وارد ہے اور بہر حال جہاں موافق قیاس ہے تو اس میں حرج نہیں ہے کہ وہاں نص اور قیاس دونوں نے حکم لگایا جائے جیسے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی عادت ہے کہ وہ ہر حکم میں دلیل منقول و معقول ہر دو سے استدلال فرماتے ہیں اس بات پر آگاہ کرنے کے لئے اگر بالفرض نص موجود نہ ہوئی تو بھی حکم قیاس سے ثابت کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
والشرط الرابع أن تبقى (۴) اور چوتھی شرط قیاس کی یہ ہے کہ تعلیل کے بعد ویسا ہی باقی رہے جیسا کہ تعلیل سے پہلے تھا۔ شرط پر مصنف نے رابع کی قید کو صراحت سے ذکر کیا ہے تا کہ یہ وہم نہ کیا جائے کہ جبکہ شرط ثالث چار شرطوں پر مشتمل ہے تو یہ شرط سالح ہے اس لئے رابع کو صراحت سے بیان کر دیا تا کہ واضح ہو جائے کہ یہ شر را سابع نے اس لئے رابع کو صراحت سے بیان کر دیا تا کہ واضح ہو جائے کہ یہ ایک ہی شرط ہے اور بقاء حکم اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ حکم جس حال پر پہلے تھا اس پر کوئی تغیر واقع نہ ہوا ہو اس کے مواد کہ محکم فرع کی جانب متعدی ہوا ہے اس لئے اصل اور فرع دونوں کو عام ہے
Despite being existent, leaving its requirement necessitates the extension of the original ruling. This is the elaboration of the fourth condition, which is that no text has come in the branch. Here, on expiation for dhihar and expiation for yamin, the ruling is to free a slave, and the slave is absolute from the condition of faith. Therefore, applying qiyas to it on the ruling of freeing a slave for expiation of killing and adding the condition of faith is not appropriate, as Imam Shafi'i restricted the slave with the condition of faith, because here the text is against qiyas. Nevertheless, where it conforms to qiyas, there is no harm; there the ruling is given by both text and qiyas, as is the habit of the author of Hidayah, that he deduces from both transmitted and rational evidence in every ruling, to inform that even if hypothetically no text existed, the ruling could be established by qiyas. And the fourth condition is that it remains (4). The fourth condition of qiyas is that after ta'lil, it remains the same as before ta'lil. The author explicitly mentioned the qualification 'raba' (fourth) so that it might not be misunderstood that since the third condition comprises four conditions, this condition is a branch; therefore he clarified 'raba' to make it clear that this is a single condition. And the meaning of 'baqa al-hukm' (remaining of the ruling) is that no change occurs in the ruling from its previous state, as it is transmitted to the branch; therefore it is common to both the original and the branch.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth condition of qiyas in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The condition is that after establishing the cause (ta'lil), the ruling in the original case must remain exactly as it was before the ta'lil; the cause must not alter the ruling itself. The commentator clarifies that the explicit mention of 'fourth' is to avoid confusion with the third condition which consists of multiple parts. A key point is that qiyas is valid only when no explicit text (nass) exists in the branch. The text provides an example: for expiation of dhihar and yamin, freeing a slave is required without the condition of faith; the Shafi'i school analogies to expiation of killing and adds faith, but the Hanafis reject this because a text exists that does not require faith. The passage also notes the Hanafi method of using both textual and rational evidence (naqli and aqli) whenever possible, even if a text alone would suffice, to demonstrate that qiyas could still establish the ruling.

Key Terms
الشرط الرابع (al-shart al-rabi'): The fourth condition of qiyas: that the ruling remains unchanged after ta'lil as it was before.
بقاء الحكم (baqa' al-hukm): The ruling's state remains unaltered after applying the cause; it is applied to both original and branch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fourth condition of qiyas (بقاء الحكم), what must be true about the ruling after the cause (illah) is established?
A) The ruling must be mentioned in the Quran.
B) The ruling must remain exactly as it was before ta'lil.
C) The ruling must be modified to fit the new case.
D) The cause must be derived from the ruling.

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition of qiyas stipulates that the ruling cannot be altered by the cause; it must remain unchanged when applied to the branch.

Istihsan as Qiyas Khafi in Zakah: Defense of Value Substitution
Defends Hanafi use of istihsan for zakah value substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers paying value (qimah) instead of a specific goat in zakah of grazing livestock as permissible by nass (text) rather than by qiyas, and evaluate the opposing argument.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit zakah value substitution not by qiyas, but by the text's implicit allowance due to the inability of a single goat to fulfill diverse promises.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, the author addresses a common critique: that Hanafis used qiyas to override the explicit hadith requiring a goat in zakah of grazing livestock. The objection claims that by substituting value, the Hanafi method nullifies the text. The commentator defends the Hanafi practice by arguing that the transfer of the poor's right from the goat to its value is itself supported by the Qur'an and hadith, not by mere analogical reasoning. This lesson dissects the Hanafi argument and its usul roots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector's claim
The opponent argues that Hanafis invalidate the explicit hadith by using qiyas to allow value instead of a goat. Note the accusation of overriding nass through ta'lil.
The objector cites the hadith 'fi khams min al-ibil shaat' as the nass being undermined.
2
Locate the Hanafi response
The commentator asserts the transfer is by nass, not ta'lil. The right of the poor is not dropped; it moves to value by the text itself.
Key phrase: 'bi al-nass la bi al-ta'lil'
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Analyze the Qur'anic verse (Surah Hud:6) and the hadith about charity falling into Allah's hand. Interpret the lam in 'li al-fuqara' as lam al-aqibah (consequence) to show ultimate ownership by Allah.
This supports that Allah can substitute because He truly owns the obligation.
4
Understand the role of istihsan
This is an example of istihsan as qiyas khafi: the nass is not abandoned; the change is attributed to the nass itself because the single goat cannot fulfill the diverse promises of provision.
Istihsan here is a subtle analogy that aligns with the broader purposes of the Law.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical ruling: Hanafis permit paying value; other schools restrict to the specific animal. This difference affects how zakah is discharged today.
The Hanafi position allows cash payment for livestock zakah, which is more practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو (172) نور الانوار جلد سوم اپنی اصل پر باقی ہے اور وہ اباحت ہے لہذا بیع الحفنه بالحقنہ ایک مٹھی بھر چیز کی بیچ ایک مٹھی بھر چیز کے ہد نے ( جائز ہے) اس لئے ایک مٹھی چیز کی بھیج دو مٹھی چیز کے بدلے جائز ہے۔ لايقال أنه القلة ايضا حال۔ یہ اعتراض نہ کیا جائے کہ قلیل بھی تو حالت ہے لہذا یہ حالت (کلیل) بھی مستقل منہ کے تحت باقی رہے گی۔ اور حرام ہوگی لانا نقول انها حال) کیونکہ ہم جواب في خمس من الابل شاءت (پانچ اونٹوں میں ایک بکری ہے) مگر تم ۃ۔ نے اے احناف بکری میں علت یہ نکالی ہے کہ نقیر کی حاجت پورا کرنا شریعت کا اصل منشاء ہے اور یہ منشیاء اور بکری سے بھی پورا ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے فقیر کی منشاء جس چیز سے پوری ہو جائے اسکاز کوۃ میں دینا جائز ہے لہذا کمری کی قیمت دینا بھی (بکری کے بجائے) جائز ہے۔ مگر نص میں اس تقلیل کے ذریعہ تم نے صریح قید کو باطل کر دیا ہے. جو نص کے حکم میں بذریعہ قیاس تغیر نہیں تو اور کیا ہے مصنف ماتن نے اس کا جواب دیا ہے کہ فقیر کا حق صورت کے حق میں ساقط نہیں ہوا ہے مگر بصورت قیمت نقل ہوا ہے بالنص لا بالتعليل نص کی بنا پر تعلیل کی وجہ سے نہیں کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فقراء کو روزی عطا کرنے کا وعدہ فرمایا ہے بلکہ صرف فراوانی نہیں تمام عالم کے رزق دینے کا وعدہ فرمایا ہے اپنے اس قول مبارک میں کے وما من دابة في الارض الا على الله رزقها۔ (اور کوئی نہیں چلنے والا زمین پر مگر اللہ پر ہے اس کی روزی پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے رزق حاصل کرنے کا طریقہ الگ الگ تقسیم فرما دیا پس اغنیاء اور مالداروں کو روزی عطا فرمائی زراعت تجارت اور کسب وغیرہ میں اس کے بعد مال داروں پر اپنے لئے مال کا ایک حصہ مقرر کر دیا ہے اور درہ مثلاً ایک بکری ہے جس کو اللہ تعالی پہلے اپنے ہاتھ میں لیتا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا گیا ہے کہ الصدقة تقع في كف الرحمن (صدقہ فقیر کے ہاتھ میں پہنچنے سے پہلے رحمن کے ہاتھ میں پہنچتا ہے تم امر بانجاز المواعيد من ذالك اور اس مقرر شدہ حصہ مال کے ذریعہ خدا کا کیا ہوا وعدہ رزق پورا کرنے کا ہم کو حکم فرمایا جس کو اللہ تعالی نے اپنے قول سے لیا انما الصدقات للفقري والمساكين ' صدقات فقراء ' و مساکین کے لئے ہیں اور رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی ایک حدیث کے ذریعہ کہ خذها من اغنيائهم ورتها الى فقرائهم ( ان کے مالداروں سے زکوۃ وصول کیجئے اور فقراء پر خرچ کیجئے) وانما فعل ذالك الخ زکوۃ کے وصول کرنے اور اس کو اس طرح خرچ کرنے وغیرہ کا نظام اس لئے قائم کیا گیا ہے تاکہ کوئی یہ خیال نہ کرے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ فقراء کو رزق نہیں دیا اور نہ اپنا وعدہ پورا فرمایا جو ان کے حق میں کیا تھا بلکہ اس نے اغنیاء کو رزق دیا ہے اور اس لئے لام لفظ للفقري میں لام عاقبت کا ہے لام تملیک کا نہیں ہے کیونکہ زکوۃ کے مالک فقراء نہیں ہوتے بلکہ مالک اللہ تعالیٰ ہوتے ہیں اغنیاء سے ان اموام کو لینے پھر فقراء کو اچی جانب سے عنایت فرمادیتے ہیں جیسے اللہ تعالی اغنیاء کو بھی اس طرح عطاء فرماتے ہیں۔ وَذَالِكَ لا يَحْتَمِلُه مَعَ اخْتِلافِ الْمَوَاعِيْدِ وَى ذَالِكَ الْمُسمى الَّذِي هُوَ الشاةُ لاَ يُحْتَمِلُ إِنْجَارَ الْمَوَاعِيْدِ مَعَ اخْتَلَافِهَا وَكَثْرَتِهَا فَإِنَّ الْمَواعِيدَ وَالْخَيْرَ وَالإِدَامَ وَالْعَطبَ وَاللْبَاسَ وَأَمْثَالَة وَالشئأة لأتُوفِئ الأ بالدَام فَكَانَ إذنا بالاستبدال
And the right of the poor is not dropped in the form; it is the answer to another question. Its exposition: The Law obligated the goat in zakah of grazing livestock, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'In five camels, a goat.' And you (Hanafis) gave the cause (illah) that it is suitable for the poor because it is wealth that fulfills needs, and anything like that, paying its value to him would also fulfill it. Thus you nullified the explicit restriction of the goat from the text. So he answered that the right of the poor is only dropped in the form of the goat, and it transfers to the value by the text (nass), not by causation (ta'lil). For God Almighty promised the poor, indeed all creatures, in His saying: 'There is no creature on earth but that God provides its sustenance.' And He assigned to each of them a means of livelihood, making the rich dependent on agriculture, trade, etc. Then He obligated a specified wealth upon the rich for Himself, namely the goat which God takes in His hand, as it is said: 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful before it falls into the hand of the poor.' Then He commanded the fulfillment of promises from that specified amount which He took, by His saying: 'Charities are only for the poor and needy...' and by His saying: 'Take it from their rich and give it to their poor.' And He did this so that no one might think that God has not provided for the poor or failed in His promise to them; rather, He provided for them through the rich. For this reason, it is said that the lam in 'for the poor' is the lam of consequence, not of ownership, because God is the owner of it; He takes it and then gives it to the poor from Himself, just as He gives to the rich likewise. And that (the specified goat) cannot fulfill the diverse and numerous promises (of various needs like housing, clothing, etc.), so it was an permission for substitution.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul defense against the objection that Hanafis used qiyas (analogical reasoning) to replace the explicit text of the Prophet's hadith requiring a goat (shaat) in zakah for grazing livestock, by allowing its value (qimah) instead. The objector argues that the Hanafi method nullifies the explicit text by claiming the cause (illah) is to fulfill the needs of the poor, which can be done by value as well. The commentator (Ashraf al-Anwar) responds by asserting that the right of the poor is not dropped; rather, it is transferred from the goat to value by the nass (text) itself, not by ta'lil (causation). He supports this with Quranic verses (Surah Hud, verse 6) about divine providence, the hadith that charity reaches Allah's hand first, and the distribution command. The lam in 'li al-fuqara' is interpreted as lam al-'aqibah (consequence) not tamlik (ownership), emphasizing that Allah is the true owner who takes and redistributes. Since the single goat cannot fulfill all the various needs of the poor (housing, clothing, etc.), substitution (istibdal) via value is permitted by the text's implicit allowance. The initial part discusses a different issue about istihsan in sales (sale of a handful for a handful), showing that change is by nass (textual indication) not mere ta'lil.

Key Terms
نص (nass): The explicit text of the Quran or hadith that establishes a ruling directly.
تعليل (ta'lil): The process of identifying a cause (illah) for a ruling and applying it analogically.
لام العاقبة (lam al-'aqibah): The letter lam that indicates the ultimate consequence or result, not ownership.
استبدال (istibdal): Substitution of the specified item (goat) with its value in zakah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why is paying value instead of a goat in zakah of grazing livestock permissible?
A) Because qiyas allows substituting value for the goat.
B) Because the right of the poor transfers to value by the text (nass), not by causation (ta'lil).
C) Because the hadith about the goat is abrogated.
D) Because the poor prefer value over animals.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, istihsan as qiyas khafi does not override nass; rather, it is a method of discovering that the nass itself permits substitution due to underlying purposes.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

12 min
Value Substitution in Zakat of Sā'imah: A Hanafi Usul Dispute
Analyzing the Hanafi permissibility of giving value instead of sheep in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument for value substitution in zakat of sā'imah based on dalālat al-nass and evaluate the opposing criticism.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits giving cash in zakat because the nass itself, not qiyas, implies substitution to meet diverse needs.

This passage presents a key usul dispute: may a Muslim give the cash equivalent (qīmah) of the prescribed sheep in zakat of grazing animals? The opposing school claims that Hanafis nullify the explicit nass through qiyas. However, the Hanafi response shows that the substitution is grounded in the nass itself—specifically, its implicit indication (dalālat al-nass) that aims to fulfill the poor's diverse needs, which a single animal cannot satisfy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that Hanafis allow giving the value of the sheep instead of the sheep itself in zakat of sā'imah.
2
Understand the opposing argument
The critic argues that the explicit hadith (for every five camels, one sheep) fixes the species, and using 'illah to allow substitution nullifies the textual restriction.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using dalālat al-nass
The response explains that the right of the poor is not lost but transferred to value, based on the nass's implicit aim: to fulfill all needs, which a single sheep cannot do. This is not qiyas but a direct inference from the text (dalālat al-nass).
Key: The lām in 'lil-fuqarā' is for consequence, not ownership, indicating Allah's provision through zakat.
4
Evaluate the objection regarding other sources
The objection that other obligations (fitr, 'ushr, kaffarah, khums) also provide for the poor is countered by noting that only zakat is universal and obligatory continuously, making it the primary channel for all needs.

الْعُشْرُ إِذْرُبُهَا لَمْ يَدْرَعِ الْأَرْضِ الْعُشْرِيَة أَحَدٌ وَكَذَا صَدَقَةٌ الْفِطْرِ إِذْرُبُمَا لَمْ يُخْرِجْهَا أَحَدٌ وَلَيْسَ لَهَا مُطَالِبٌ مِنَ اللهِ أصلاً فَلَمْ يَبْقَ إِلَّا الزَّكَوةَ فَكَانَنْ هِيَ مَرْجَعُ كُلِّ الْحَوَائِجِ وَرُكْنَهُ مَا جَعَلَ عَلَمّا عَلَى حُكْمِ النَّص وَهُوَ الْمَعْنى الجَامِعُ المُسمَّى عِلَّةً سَمَّاهُ رُكْنًا لأنَّ مَدَارَ الْقَيَاسِ عَلَيْهِ لَا يَقُوْمُ الْقَيَاسُ إِلا بِهِ وَسَمَاهُ عَلَمًا لأَنَّ عِلَلِ الشَّرْعِ أَمَارَاتٌ وَمُعَرِّفات لِلْحُكم وَعَلا مَتُهُ عَلَيْهِ وَالْمُوْجِبُ الْحَقِيْقِي هُوَ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَإِنَّمَا إخْتَلَفُوا أَنْ ذَالِكَ الْمَعْنَى عَلَمٌ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ فِى الْفَرْعِ فَقَط أَمْ فِي الْأَصْلِ أَيْضًا وذالك لا يحتمله الخ لیکن رزق کی نوعیت مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے محض یہ اس کی تکمیل ترجمہ و تشریح کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے یعنی یہ مسمی (مقررہ) بکری مختلف قسم کی غیر ضروریات رزق کے وعدہ وعدہ کو پورا نہیں کر سکتا کیوں کہ وعدہ میں روٹی سالن لکڑی۔ لباس برتن وغیرہ ہیں اور بکری صرف سالن ہی کی ضروریات پورا کر سکتی ہے۔ فکان إذنا بالاستبدال کی اجازت ثابت ہو گئی۔ یعنی دلالة النص سے کہ بکری کو نقدین سے تبادلہ کر لیا جائے زکوہ دینے والا بکری کے بدلے قیمت دیدے یا زکوۃ لینے والا بکری کو فروخت کر کے قیمت حاصل کرلے تاکہ اس سے دوسری تمام ضروریات پوری کرسکے۔ لہذا نص کے حکم کو بدلنے کے لیئے قیاس کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ اس پر اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ اجازت ان فقراء کے لئے اس وقت مناسب تھی جب کہ ان کے لئے رزق کے دوسرے ذرائع شریعت نے متعین نہ کئے ہوتے اور رزق صرف بکری ہی میں رہتا ہو بلکہ اللہ تعالی نے ان کو صدقہ فطر کا گہوں دیا پیداوار سے عشر دیا اور کفارہ یمین سے کپڑا دیا۔ غنیمت کے خمس سے دیگر اشیاء ضروریہ دیا تو یہ لازم نہیں آتا ہے کہ رزق صرف بکری پر منحصر ہے۔ اجيب بان الزكوة لا تحلو عنها بلد من بلاد المسلمين اذ هي فرض كالصلاة فكان المصرف الاصلى للفقراء فى الزكوة بخلاف مال الغنيمة وغيرها. اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا گیا کہ زکوۃ سے تو کوئی مسلمان کا شہر خالی نہیں جہاں ادا نہ کی جاتی ہو کیونکہ زکوۃ نماز کی طرح فرض ہے لہذا مصرف اصلی فقراء کے لئے زکوۃ ہی مانی جاتی ہے بخلاف مال غنیمت وغیرہ۔
Nur al-Anwar Volume Three - Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu Commentary: This is that grazing animals (sā'imah) which spend the year in the forest filling their stomachs, so that the owner does not have to provide fodder, grain, or straw from his home. Such animals are called sā'imah. The Shari'ah has made a sheep obligatory in zakat because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'For every five camels, one sheep.' But you, O Hanafis, have extracted the cause ('illah) in the sheep that fulfilling the need of the poor is the original intent of the Shari'ah, and this intent is fulfilled by the sheep as well, so it is permissible to give whatever fulfills the poor's need in zakat; therefore giving the value of the sheep (instead of the sheep) is permissible. But by this ta'lil (rationalization) you have nullified the explicit restriction in the nass (text). If this is not changing the ruling of the nass by way of qiyas, then what is? The author of the matn replied: The poor's right has not been nullified in terms of form but has been transferred to the form of value, by the nass, not by ta'lil, because Allah has promised to provide sustenance to the poor, indeed He promised to provide sustenance to the entire world in His blessed saying: 'There is no moving creature on earth but its sustenance depends on Allah.' Then He distinguished different ways of obtaining sustenance for each of them. So He gave sustenance to the rich through agriculture, trade, and earning, etc. After that, He prescribed a portion of wealth for the rich for the sake of the poor, for example, one sheep, which Allah first takes in His hand, as it is said: 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful before it reaches the hand of the poor.' Then He commanded us to fulfill the promise of sustenance through this prescribed portion, which Allah took from His saying: 'The alms are for the poor and the needy.' And through a hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Take it from their rich and give it to their poor.' The system of collecting zakat and spending it in this manner was established so that no one would think that Allah did not give sustenance to the poor and did not fulfill His promise to them; rather, He gave sustenance to the rich, and therefore the lām in 'lil-fuqarā' is the lām of consequence, not the lām of possession, because the poor do not own the zakat; rather, Allah is the owner. He takes these wealth from the rich and then bestows them upon the poor from His side, just as He bestows upon the rich. And that (the single sheep) does not suffice with the diversity of needs, and that named thing which is the sheep cannot fulfill the diverse and numerous promises, because the promises include bread, curry, firewood, clothing, utensils, etc., and the sheep can only fulfill the need for meat. Thus, permission for substitution is established, that is, by the implicit indication of the text (dalālat al-nass) that the sheep may be exchanged for cash, so that all his needs can be met from it. Therefore, qiyas has no role in changing the nass. It was objected to this that this permission would only be suitable if their sustenance were confined to the sheep, but rather Allah gave them wheat from sadaqat al-fitr, grains from 'ushr, clothing from kaffarat al-yamin, and other types from the khums of ghanimah. So it is not necessary that sustenance is only dependent on the sheep. The answer is that zakat is not absent from any Muslim city, as it is obligatory like prayer. Thus, the primary channel for the poor is zakat, unlike ghanimah, etc., for ghanimah is distributed among Muslims, and even when it occurs, it is divided according to the Shari'ah. Similarly, kaffarah may not have anyone in need for a long time. Similarly, 'ushr, because no one may cultivate 'ushri land. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr, because no one may have given it for a long time, and there is no one to demand it from Allah at all. Thus, only zakat remains, and it is the reference for all needs. And its rukn (pillar) is what is made a sign ('alam) upon the ruling of the nass, and it is the comprehensive meaning called 'illah. He called it rukn because qiyas revolves around it; qiyas cannot stand without it. And he called it 'alam because the 'illah of Shari'ah are signs and identifiers for the ruling, and its mark upon it, while the real effective cause is Allah Almighty. They only differed whether that meaning is a sign upon the ruling in the branch only or also in the original. And that (the sheep) cannot bear it with the diversity of needs... That is, the named (prescribed) sheep cannot fulfill the diverse needs because the promise includes bread, curry, firewood, clothing, utensils, etc., and the sheep can only fulfill the need for curry. Thus, permission for substitution is established. That is, by dalālat al-nass, the sheep can be exchanged for cash: either the zakat giver gives value instead of the sheep, or the zakat receiver sells the sheep and obtains its value so that he can fulfill all his other needs. Therefore, qiyas has no role in changing the ruling of the nass. An objection was raised: This permission would be appropriate when the Shari'ah had not designated other sources of sustenance for the poor, and sustenance was limited to the sheep; rather, Allah gave them wheat from sadaqat al-fitr, grains from 'ushr, clothing from kaffarat al-yamin, and other necessary items from the khums of ghanimah. So it does not necessarily follow that sustenance is only dependent on the sheep. The answer is: Zakat is not absent from any Muslim city, because it is obligatory like prayer. Thus, the primary channel for the poor is zakat, unlike the wealth of ghanimah, etc.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning the permissibility of giving value (qīmah) instead of the specified sheep (shāt) in the zakat of sā'imah (grazing animals). The text presents a criticism of the Hanafi position that value substitution is allowed, and then provides a response from the Hanafi perspective. The critic argues that the Hanafi reliance on 'illah (the cause of fulfilling the poor's need) nullifies the explicit restriction of the nass (text) that specifies a sheep. The Hanafi response clarifies that the substitution is not based on qiyas (analogy) but on the nass itself, specifically the dalālat al-nass (implicit indication) that aims to fulfill the diverse needs of the poor. The multi-faceted needs (bread, curry, clothing, etc.) cannot be satisfied by a single sheep, so the text implicitly permits exchange. The objection that other sources (fitr, 'ushr, kaffarah, khums) also provide sustenance is countered by noting that zakat is the most universal and obligatory source, present in every Muslim community, while the others are irregular. Thus, zakat remains the primary mechanism for the poor's needs. The passage also discusses the concepts of 'illah (effective cause) and 'alam (sign), noting that the 'illah is a sign on the ruling in the branch, while the real cause is Allah. This analysis is a typical Hanafi usul approach to reconciling nass and maqsad (objective).

Key Terms
السائمة (al-sā'imah): Grazing livestock that feed themselves in the wild for most of the year, requiring zakat.
الشاة (al-shāt): The specific sheep prescribed in the hadith for zakat on camels (one sheep per five camels).
العلة (al-'illah): The effective cause or rationale behind a ruling, here identified as fulfilling the poor's needs.
دلالة النص (dalālat al-nass): The implied meaning of the text that goes beyond its literal wording, used to justify value substitution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, why is giving the value of a sheep in zakat of sā'imah permissible?
A) Because qiyas overrides the explicit nass.
B) Because the nass itself implies permission to substitute value to meet diverse needs.
C) Because the poor prefer cash over sheep.
D) Because the hadith about five camels is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi allowance of value substitution in zakat is rooted in the text's implicit indication (dalālat al-nass), not in a qiyas-based nullification of the explicit ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
