وہ ہے جو اصل سے بھی جدا نہ ہو جیسے شمنیہ ( شمن ہونا) قیمت ہونا) ہونے اور چاندی میں زکوۃ کے واجب ہونے کی علت ہے۔ جو ان دونوں میں بھی جدا نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ ان کی تخلیق ہی شمعیت کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور ثمنیت جس طرح سونا چاندی کی ڈلی میں موجود ہے اسی طرح ان سے بنے ہوئے زیورات، بر تن ، وغیرہ میں بھی پائی جاتی ہے لہذا عورتوں کے سونے اور چاندی کے زیوارت میں علت ثمنیت کی وجہ سے زکوۃ واجب ہو گی۔ اور امام شافل ثمنیت کو وجوب زکوۃ کی علت نہیں بلکہ حرمت ریوا کی علت قرار دیتے ہیں۔ لہذا ان کے نزدیک یہ علت قاصرہ ہے اس لئے نصوص کے علاوہ فرع کی طرف ان کا حکم متعدی نہیں ہوتا۔ وصف عارض کی مثال انفجار ہے ( جاری ہونا ۔ بہتا ) آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے فرمان فانها دم عرق انفجر ( یہ رگ کا بہتا ہوا خون ہے ) مستحاضہ کے لئے وضوء واجب ہونے کی علت بنائی گئی ہے اور جاری ہونا بہنا یہ خون کا وصف عارض ہے کیونکہ یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ ہر دم عرق بہنے والا ہی ہو ۔ لہذا جہاں کہیں انفجار دم پایا جائے گا مستحاضہ عدت کا ہو یا اس کے علاوہ کا یا سمیلین (بول و براز کے راستے) کے علاوہ ہرن کے دوسرے حصوں سے چارمی ہو تو وضو واجب ہو جائے گا۔ وَاسْمًا عَطَفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ وَصَفًا وَمُقَابِلُ لَهُ أَن يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ ذَالِكَ الْمَعْنَى إِسْمًا كَالدَّمِ فِى عَيْنِ هَذَا مِثَالِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ فَإِنَّهَا دَمُ عِرْقٍ انْفَجَرَ فَإِنَّهُ إِنْ اُعْتُبِرَ فِيْهِ لَفْظُ الدَّم كَانَ مِثَالاً لِلاِسْم وَإنْ أَعْتُبِرَ فِيْهِ مَعْنَى الْإِنْفِجَارِ كَانَ مِثَالاً لِلْوَصفِ الْعَارِضِ كَمَا مَرَّ وَجَلِيًّا وَخَفِيًا الظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ تَفْسِيمُ لِلْوَصفِ كَلازِم وَالْعَارِضَ فَالْوَصْف الْجَلِي هُوَ مَا يَفْهَمُهُ كُلُّ اَحَدٍ كَالطَّوَافِ لِسَوْرٍ الْهِرَّةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلاَمُ إِنَّهَا مِنَ الطَّوَّافِينَ وَالطَّوَّافَاتِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَالْوَصْف الْخَفِيُّ هُوَ مَا يَفْهَمُ بَعْضٍ دُونَ بَعْضٍ كَمَا فِي عِلَّةِ الرَّبَوَا عِنْدَنَا الْقَدْرُ وَالْجِنْسُ وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي الطِّعْمُ فِي الْمَطْعُومَاتِ وَالثَّمَنِيَةُ فِي الْأَثْمَانِ وَعِنْدَ مَالِكَ الأَقْتِيَاتُ وَالاِدْخَارُ وَحُكْمًا هَذَا مَعْطَوْفٌ وَمُقَاتِلُ لَهُ أَى يَجُورُ أَنْ يَكُونَ ذَالِكَ الْمَعْنى حُكْمًا شَرْعِيًا جَامِعًا بَيْنَ الأصْلِ وَالفَرْعِ كَمَا رُوِيَ أَنْ أَمْرَاءَ : جَاءَ تَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ إِنْ أبِي قَدْ أَدْرَكَهُ الْحَج وَهُوَ شَيْخ كَبِيرُ لاَ يَسْتَمْسِكُ عَلَى الرَّاحِلَةِ أَفَتُجِيزُنِي أَنْ أَحَج عَنْهُ فَقَالَ أَرَأَيْتَ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَى أَبِيْك دَيْنٌ فَقَيْصَيْتِهِ آمَا كَانَ يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ قَالَتْ نَعَمْ قَالَ فَدَيْنُ اللهِ أَحَق بِالْقَبُول فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَمَ الْحَجْ عَلَى دَيْنِ الْعِبَادِ وَالْمَعْنَى الْجَامِعُ بَيْنَهُما هُوَ الدِّينُ وَهُوَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ حَقٌّ ثَابِت فِى الدَّمَةِ وَاجِبُ الآدَاءِ وَالْوُجُوبُ حُكْمٌ شَرْعِيٌّ وَفَرْدًا وَعَدَدَا الظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ أَيْضًا تَقْسِيمَ لِلْوَصْفِ فَالْوَصَفُ الْفُرْدُ كَالْعِلْةِ بِالْقَدْرِ وَحْدَهُ أَوْ الْجِنْسِ وَحْدَهُ لِحُرْمَةِ النَّسَاءِ وَالْوَصْف الْعَدَدُ كَالْقَدْرِ مَعَ الجِنْسِ عِلةُ لِحُرْمَةِ التفاضل واسما اور جاتا ہے کہ وہ اسم ہو یہ وصفا پر عطف ہے اور اس کا مقابل بھی ہے یعنی جائز ہے ترجمه تشریح کہ وہ وصف ملت ہونے کے بجائے اسم ہو۔ جیسے کہ لفظ دم عید اسی مثال میں یعنی نبی علیہ الام الصلوۃ والسلام کے قول فانها دم عرق کبیر میں کیونکہ اگر اس تعلیل میں لفظ دم کا لحاظ کر لیا جائے تو علت کے اسم ہونے کی مثال بن جائے گی اور اگر جاری ہونے اور بہنے کے وصف کا لحاظ کر لیا جائے تو یہی وصف عارض کی مثال بن جائے گی جیسے کہ گذر چکا ہے۔ جلياً وخفیا خواہ وہ جلی ہو ( واضح) ہو یا خفی ہو بظاہر یہ وصف کی تقسیم ہے جیسے وصف کی ایک تقسیم لازم و عارض ہے ایسے ہی دوسری تقسیم ملی و خفی کی ہے پس وصف جلی وہ ہے جس کو ہر کوئی جان لے اور اس کو سمجھ نے جیسے علت طواف سور ھرہ میں (بلی کا بچا ہوا) آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قول انها من الطوافين صلی والطوافات . عليكم ( يہ بلی تمہارے گھروں میں بہت زیادہ آمد ورفت رکھنے والی ہے ) اس لئے اگر اس سے جھوٹے کو نجس قرار دیا جائے تو حرج لازم آئے گا۔ اور وصف کے مخفی، پوشیدہ ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس کو کچھ لوگ ( خواص سمجھیں اور کچھ لوگ (عوام) نہ سمجھ سکیں جیسے ربوا کی علت ہمارے نزدیک قدر اور جنس ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک طعم مطعومات میں ہے تو سونے چاندکی پر ثمنیت علمت ہے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک از دخار ہے (کچھ دن کے لئے ذخیرہ کر لینا) علت ہے وحکما اور جائز ہے کہ وہ حکم ہو اس کا عطف مصنف کے قول وصفا پر ہے اور وصف ہی کے مقابل بھی ہے یعنی یہ کہ جائز ہے کہ معنی (علت) حکم شرعی ہو جو اصل اور فرح میں یکساں پایا جائے جیسے روایت میں ہے کہ ایک عورت جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خدمت میں حاضر ہوئی اور کہا میرے باپ نے زمانہ حج پالیا ہے اور وہ بوڑھے ضعیف ہیں کجاوہ (سواری) پر بیٹھے نہیں سکتے ہیں پس کیا آپ مجھے اجازت دیتے ہیں کہ میں ان کی طرف سے حج کرلوں تو حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے جواب دیا اچھا بتاؤ اگر تمہارے باپ کے اوپر قرض ہو تا تو تم اس کی طرف سے ادائے گی کرتی یا نہ کرتیں۔ کیا یہ ادائیگی قرضن تمہاری طرف سے قبول نہ کیا جاتا ہو لیں ہاں یا رسول اللہ تو آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بیج کو بندوں کے قرض پر قیاس فرمایا ہے اور ان دونوں کے درمیان علت مشترکہ دینا ہے دین زمہ میں حق کے ثابت ہونے کا نام ہے جس کی ادئیگی واجب ہوتی ہے اور وجوب حکم شرع ہے۔ جس کو آپ نے دوسرے حکم شرعی یعنی قبول عند الادار کے لئے علت قرار دیا ہے فرداً وعدد أخواہ منفرد ہو یا متعدد ہو بظاہر یہ بھی وصف کے اقسام ہیں۔ وصف فرد کی مثال جیسے وہ تنہا علت جنس عورتوں کے حرام ہونے کے
It is that which is not separate from the original, like thamaniyya (being a price, value) is the cause for the obligation of zakat on gold and silver. It does not separate from both of them because their creation is for being a price, and thamaniyya is present in gold and silver bullion similarly in ornaments, vessels, etc. made from them, hence zakat is obligatory on women's gold and silver ornaments due to the cause of thamaniyya. Imam al-Shafi'i does not consider thamaniyya as the cause for obligation of zakat but as the cause for prohibition of riba. Hence in his view this cause is qasira (confined) so its ruling does not extend to a branch beyond the texts. Example of an accidental description is infijar (gushing, flowing) in the Prophet's (peace be upon him) saying 'indeed it is a blood of a gushing vein' made as a cause for obligation of wudu for mustahada. And gushing/flowing is an accidental description of blood because it is not necessary that every blood of a vein gushes. So wherever blood gushing is found, whether from mustahada of 'idda or otherwise, or from other parts of the animal except the two passages (urine and feces), if it flows? then wudu becomes obligatory. 'And as a name' is coordinated with his saying 'and as a description' and is its opposite, meaning it is permissible that that meaning be a name, like blood in the same example, and it is his saying (peace be upon him) 'indeed it is a blood of a gushing vein'. If in it the word 'blood' is considered, it becomes an example of a name; if the meaning of gushing is considered, it becomes an example of accidental description as mentioned. 'And manifest and hidden' apparently it is a division of description like necessary and accidental. So manifest description is that which everyone understands, like the frequenting of the cat in his saying (peace be upon him) 'indeed it is of those who go about among you'. And hidden description is that which some understand and others not, like the cause of riba with us is quantity and genus, and with al-Shafi'i is food-ness in foodstuffs and thamaniyya in valuables, and with Malik is staples and storage. 'And as a ruling' this is coordinated and opposite to it, i.e., it is permissible that that meaning be a legal ruling uniting the original and branch, as narrated that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: 'My father has caught the time of hajj and he is an old man who cannot sit firmly on the mount, so do you permit me to perform hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'What do you think, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be accepted from him?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then the debt of Allah is more deserving of acceptance.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) made qiyas of hajj on the debt of servants, and the common meaning between them is 'dayn' (debt), which is a term for a right established in the liability, obligatory to discharge, and obligation is a legal ruling. 'And singular and plural' apparently this too is a division of description. So singular description is like the cause by quantity alone or genus alone for prohibition of women, and plural description is like quantity with genus as a cause for prohibition of excess. 'And as a name' it comes that it is a name; this is coordinated with his saying 'and as a description' and is its opposite, meaning it is permissible that that description instead of being a description be a name, like the word 'blood' in this example, i.e., in the Prophet's saying 'indeed it is a blood of a gushing vein'. Because if in this ta'lil the word 'blood' is considered, it becomes an example of the cause being a name, and if the description of gushing and flowing is considered, it becomes an example of an accidental description as passed. 'And manifest and hidden' whether it is manifest (clear) or hidden, apparently this is a division of description, just as one division of description is necessary and accidental, similarly another division is manifest and hidden. So manifest description is that which everyone knows and understands, like the cause of frequenting in the cat's leftover (the cat is one of those who go about among you). The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed it is of those who go about among you' meaning this cat goes around your houses a lot, so if its leftover is considered impure, hardship would follow. And hidden description means that some people (elite) understand it and some (commoners) do not, like the cause of riba with us is quantity and genus, and with al-Shafi'i is taste in foodstuffs, and thamaniyya on gold and silver is the cause, and with Malik is staples and storage. 'And as a ruling' it is permissible that it be a ruling; this is coordinated and opposite to his saying 'and as a description', meaning it is permissible that the meaning (cause) be a legal ruling that is found equally in original and branch, as in the narration that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: 'My father has caught the time of hajj and he is an old man who cannot sit on the mount, so do you permit me to perform hajj on his behalf?' The Prophet (peace be upon him) replied: 'Tell me, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be accepted from you?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then the debt of Allah is more deserving of acceptance.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) made qiyas of hajj on the debt of servants, and the common meaning between them is 'dayn', which is a term for a right established in the liability, obligatory to discharge, and obligation is a legal ruling. 'And singular and plural' it says whether singular or plural; apparently this too is a division of description. So singular description is like the cause by quantity alone or genus alone for prohibition of marriage, and plural description is like quantity with genus as a cause for prohibition of excess.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, classifies the 'illah (cause/effective cause) in qiyas according to multiple categories. It begins by illustrating a necessary (lazim) description: thamaniyya (the quality of being a price or standard of value) is the cause for zakat on gold and silver. Since thamaniyya is inherent in both bullion and jewelry, zakat is obligatory on both. This is contrasted with Imam al-Shafi'i's view, who restricts thamaniyya to riba, making it a confined cause (qasira) that does not extend beyond the texts. The accidental ('arid) description is then exemplified by the gushing of blood in istihadah; the flow (infijar) is not essential to blood but accidental, yet when present, it triggers the ruling of wudu. Next, the passage discusses whether the 'illah can be a name (ism) or a description (wasf). Using the same hadith, if one considers the word 'blood' it is a name; if one considers the meaning of gushing it is a description. Then the distinction between manifest (jali) and hidden (khafi) descriptions is explained: manifest is understood by all (e.g., a cat's frequenting is obvious), while hidden is understood only by some (e.g., quantity and genus as cause for riba, disputed among madhahib). Finally, the ruling (hukm) can serve as the 'illah itself, as in the hadith where the common meaning of debt (dayn) – a right in the liability – is used to analogize hajj. The description can be singular (fard) as in quantity alone, or multiple (adad) as in quantity with genus. The commentary enriches each distinction with Hanafi examples and inter-madhhab disputes.

Key Terms
فرد (fard): A single description serving as the 'illah, e.g., quantity alone.
عدد (ʿadad): A combination of descriptions serving as the 'illah, e.g., quantity with genus for riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, what is the compound 'illah for the prohibition of excess (riba al-fadl)?
A) Quantity alone
B) Genus alone
C) Quantity and genus together
D) Taste and thamaniyya

Key Takeaway
An 'illah can be composed of one or multiple descriptions; the combination determines the scope of analogical extension.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Conditions of the 'Illah: Suitability and Justness
Explaining the conditions of the 'illah and first manifestation type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions of salah and 'adalah for an 'illah, apply the witness analogy, and identify the first type of manifestation.

Core Idea
The 'illah must be suitable and just – its effect appears in the genus of the ruling before qiyas.

The commentator establishes that a description (wasf) used as an 'illah in qiyas must meet two conditions: being suitable (salih) and just ('adil). He draws a powerful analogy to a witness: just as a witness must be suitable (of upright character and capability) and just (proven integrity) before being accepted, so too must the 'illah. The suitability is defined as the appearance of the 'illah's effect in the genus of the ruling being reasoned to, from outside, before qiyas is applied. The passage then introduces four types of manifestation, detailing the first type where the very same description's effect appears in the very same ruling, using the cat hadith as an example.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Witness Analogy
The text compares the 'illah to a witness in a courtroom. Just as a witness must be both suitable (salih) and just ('adil) for their testimony to be accepted, the 'illah must satisfy these two conditions to be valid in qiyas. Reflect on the requirements for a witness: suitability (being of sound mind and not a minor) and justness (being of proven integrity, not sinful).
This analogy is foundational – it sets the epistemological standard for the 'illah.
2
Define Salah (Suitability) for the 'Illah
Suitability means that the effect (athar) of the 'illah appears in the genus (jins) of the ruling (hukm) from outside (min kharij) before qiyas is performed. This does not require the effect to be in the very same ruling; it can be in a similar type of ruling. For example, if the 'illah is 'circumambulation', its effect (purity of leftover water) appears in the genus of purity rulings even before we apply it to a new case.
The phrase 'from outside' means the effect is observed independently, not forced by analogy.
3
Define 'Adalah (Justness) for the 'Illah
Justness means the 'illah's effect is consistent and not subject to arbitrary variation. Just as a witness must be consistently truthful, the 'illah must produce its effect reliably across similar rulings. If the effect fluctuates, the 'illah is not 'adil and cannot be used as a valid cause.
Consistency is key – an 'illah that gives different results in similar cases is weak.
4
Identify the First Type of Manifestation
The text explains that the effect can appear in four ways, but only the first is detailed here: the effect of the very same description appears in the very same ruling (athar 'ayn al-wasf fi 'ayn al-hukm). This is agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh). The example: the cat's circumambulation (wasf) affects the ruling of its leftover water (hukm) – the water is pure because the cat is like a frequent visitor.
The other three types are referenced but not elaborated in this passage.

Source Text

وَيَجُوزُ فِي النَّص وَغَيْرِهِ إِذا كان ثَابِتا به أَى يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ ذَالِكَ الْمَعْنى مَنْصُوصاً فِي النَّصْ كَالطَّرَافِ فِي سَورٍ الْبِرَّةِ وَأَنْ يَكُوْنَ فِي غَيْرِ النَّصَّ وَلَكِن ثابتا به كَالأَمْثَلَةِ الَّتِي مَرْتِ الآن ثُمَّ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ مَا يَعْلَمْ بِهِ أَنْ هَذَا الْوَصَف وَصَفٌ دَوْنَ غَيْرِهِ فَقَالَ دَلالَةٌ كَوْنِ الوصف عِلْةُ صلاحه وعدالته فَإِن الوصف فِي الْقَيَاسِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الشَّاهِدِ فِي الدُّعْوى فَكَمَا يَسْتِرِطُ فِي الشَّاهِدِ لِلْقَبُول أَنْ يَكُونَ صَالِحًا وَعَادِلاً فَكَذَا فِي الْوَصفِ وَكَمَا أَنْ فِي الشَّاهِدِ لا يَجُوزُ الْعَمَلُ قَبْلَ الصَّلاح وَلا يَجِبُ قَبْلَ الْعَدَالَّة فَكَذَا فِي الْوَصْفِ ثُمَّ بَيْنَ مَعْنَى الصَّلاح وَالْعَدَالَّة عَلَى غَيْر تَرْتِيب اللف فَبَدَأ أولاً بذكر الْعَالَةِ بِقَوْلِهِ يَظُهُورِ آثَرِهِ فِى جِنْسِ الْحُكْمِ لِلْمُعَلَّلِ بِهِ أَيْ بِأَنْ ظَهَرَ أَثَرُ الْوَصْفِ فِي جِنْسِ الْحُكم لمُعَلَّلِ بِهِ مِنْ خَارِج قَبْلِ الْقَيَاسِ وَإِنْ ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهِ فِي عَيْنٍ ذَالِكَ الْحُكْمِ الْمُعَلَّلِ بِهِ مِنْهُ فَبَاطَرِيقِ الأَوْلَى وَجَعَلَتُهُ تَرْتَفِي إِلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَنْوَاعِ الْأَوَّلُ أَنْ يَظْهَرَ أَثَرُ عَيْنِ ذَالَكَ الْوَصْفِ فِى عَيْنِ ذَالِكَ الحُكْم وَهُوَ مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ كَاثْرٍ عَيْنِ الطواف في عين سور الهرة والحاصل أن قوله اسماً وحكما حاصل کلام یہ ہے کہ مصنف کا قول اسماء حکماً بلا شبہ ترجمه و تشریح وصف کے مقابل ہے اور مصنف کا قول لازما د عا رضا اس میں شرک نہیں کہ یہ دونوں وصف کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ اور بہر حال جلی و مخفی اور اسی طرح فرد و عد و بطور مقابلہ اور مداخل کے ذکر کئے ہیں لیکن بہر حال بظاہر یہ چہار وہ صف کی ہی دو قسمیں ہیں اس وجہ سے فرد و عدد کی کوئی مثال ہی سوائے وصل کے ہم کو نہیں علی علت کا جامع ترین نام اس کی اصطلاح میں وصف مطلق ہے برابر ہے یہ علت اصل ہی ہو یا اہم اور یا حکم شرعی ہو جیسا کہ مصنف کے کلام میں عنقریب آجائے گا ملت کے یہ مختلف نام صرف امام الشعر اسلام کا اپنا محمد و اور تفن ہے اور دوسرے لوگوں نے ان کی اتباع فرمائی - ويجوز في النص وغيره ۔
And it is permissible in the text and other than it, if it is established by it, i.e., it is permissible that that meaning be explicitly mentioned in the text, like circumambulation in the chapter of the cat, and that it be in other than the text but established by it, like the examples that have just passed. Then he began to explain by what it is known that this description is a description rather than another, saying: ‘An indication of the description being a cause is its suitability and its justness.’ For the description in qiyas is like a witness in a claim; just as in the witness for acceptance it is required that he be suitable and just, so too in the description. And just as in the witness action is not permissible before suitability nor obligatory before justness, so too in the description. Then he explained the meaning of suitability and justness without regard to order, so he began first by mentioning the cause by his saying: ‘The appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling for the thing being reasoned by it,’ i.e., that the effect of the description appears in the genus of the ruling for the thing being reasoned by it from outside before qiyas. And if its effect appears in the very same ruling being reasoned by it, then by way of priority. And he made it divided into four types: first, that the effect of the very same description appears in the very same ruling, and this is agreed upon, like the effect of the very [circumambulation] in the [ruling] of the cat’s leftover. The summary: his saying ‘name and ruling’ means that the author’s statement is undoubtedly opposite to the description, and his saying ‘necessary and accidental’ does not doubt that these two are two divisions of the description. In any case, clear and hidden, and similarly singular and plural, are mentioned by way of contrast and overlap, but apparently these four are only two divisions of the description. For this reason, we have no example for singular and plural except in the division of the description. The comprehensive name for the cause in his terminology is ‘description’ absolutely, whether it is a cause in the original, or a ruling, or a legal ruling, as will come in the author’s speech shortly. These different names are only from Imam al-Islam’s own creative thinking, and other people follow him. And it is permissible in the text and other than it.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for a description to be considered a valid 'illah in qiyas. The commentator states that the 'illah can be explicitly mentioned in the text (like circumambulation in the cat hadith) or derived from the text (like the examples of Hajj analogized to debt). Then he introduces the requirement that the 'illah must be suitable (salih) and just ('adil). He draws an analogy between the 'illah in qiyas and a witness in a claim: a witness must be suitable (i.e., of upright character and capable) and just (i.e., of proven integrity). Similarly, the 'illah must be suitable (salih) meaning its effect appears in the genus of the ruling being reasoned to, and just ('adil) meaning its effect is consistent. The commentator then explains that suitability means that the effect of the 'illah appears in the genus of the ruling from outside before qiyas is performed, not necessarily in the very same ruling. If it appears in the very same ruling, then it is even more prior. He then enumerates four types of manifestation of the 'illah’s effect: 1) the effect of the very same description appears in the very same ruling (agreed upon, e.g., circumambulation causing impurity of cat’s leftover water). The rest of the four types are not elaborated in this passage but referenced. The passage ends with a summary in Urdu reiterating the classification and naming the comprehensive term ‘description’ as used by Imam al-Islam (Imam Abu Hanifa or the leading scholar). The overall purpose is to guide the student in identifying a sound 'illah for qiyas.

Key Terms
الصَّلاح (as-salah): Suitability of the 'illah: its effect appears in the genus of the ruling from outside before qiyas.
الْعَدَالَة (al-‘adalah): Justness of the 'illah: its effect is consistent and not subject to arbitrary change.
أَثَر (athar): The effect of the 'illah that manifests in the ruling.
الطَّوَّافِينَ (al-tawwafin): Those who go around (circumambulators); used in the hadith to describe the cat's habit as a basis for the 'illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the suitability (salah) of an 'illah require?
A) The 'illah must be explicitly mentioned in the Quran.
B) The effect of the 'illah must appear in the very same ruling being reasoned to.
C) The effect of the 'illah must appear in the genus of the ruling from outside before qiyas.
D) The 'illah must be approved by a majority of scholars.

Key Takeaway
An 'illah is valid only if it is suitable (its effect appears in the genus of the ruling from outside) and just (its effect is consistent), analogous to a credible witness in a claim.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Four Types of Effect Proving the 'Illah
Explaining the four types of effect proving the 'illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the four types of effect (athar) that demonstrate a description's reliability as a cause ('illah) in Hanafi qiyas.

Core Idea
A description's validity as a cause is proven by its effect—just as a witness must be reliable.

This lesson explores how Hanafi usul scholars determine whether a description (wasf) can serve as an effective cause in qiyas. The passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains that a cause must demonstrate its reliability through observable effects, categorized into four types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification of descriptions
The passage notes that a description can be a name (ism), ruling (hukm), necessary (lazim), or accidental ('arid). Recognize these categories as potential bases for a cause.
These are covered in the first part of the source.
2
Understand the analogy to witnesses
Just as a witness must be sound (salih) and reliable ('adil) for acceptance, a description must show its effect to be accepted as a cause. This justifies the need for empirical evidence.
The analogy is key to Hanafi methodology.
3
Define salah and 'adalah in context
Salah (soundness) means the description is fit to be a cause; 'adalah (reliability) means it consistently produces its effect. These are proven by the appearance of its athar.
These terms are critical for understanding the condition.
4
List and explain the four types of effect
The four types are: (1) the very description affects the very ruling, (2) the very description affects the genus of the ruling, (3) the genus of the description affects the very ruling, (4) the genus affects the genus (implied). Study the examples given: circumambulation, childhood, and unconsciousness.
The passage cuts off before fully explaining the fourth type, but the first three are detailed.
5
Apply the concept to a new scenario
Given a new potential cause (e.g., intoxication for prohibition of alcohol), determine which type of effect would prove its reliability and why.
This step solidifies understanding through application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أن قوله اسماً وحكما لا شك فيه أنه مقابل للوصف وأن قوله لازماً عارضاً لا شك فيه أن هما قسم الوصف. وأما الجلي والخفي وكذا الفرد والعدد فقد أورده على سبيل المقابلة والتداخل والظاهر أنه قسم الوصف إذ لم تجد له مثالاً إلا في قسم الوصف. وقد يسمى المعنى الجامع الوصف مطلقا عرفهم سواء كان وصفاً أو اسماً أو حكماً على ما سيأتي. وهذا كله من تفنن فكر الإمام والناس أتباع له.
ويجوز في النص وغيره إذا كان ثابتا به أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى منصوصا في النص كالطواف في سورة البرة وأن يكون في غير النص ولكن ثابتا به كالأمثلة التي مرت الآن.
ثم شرع في بيان ما يعلم به أن هذا الوصف وصف دون غيره فقال: دلالة كون الوصف علة صلاحه وعدالته. فإن الوصف في القياس بمنزلة الشاهد في الدعوى. فكما يسترط في الشاهد للقبول أن يكون صالحا وعادلا فكذا في الوصف. وكما أن في الشاهد لا يجوز العمل قبل الصلاح ولا يجب قبل العدالة فكذا في الوصف. ثم بين معنى الصلاح والعدالة على غير ترتيب اللف فبدأ أولاً بذكر العدالة بقوله: بظهور أثره في جنس الحكم للمعلل به أي بأن ظهر أثر الوصف في جنس الحكم لمعلل به من خارج قبل القياس وإن ظهر أثره في عين ذلك الحكم المعلل به منه فبطريق الأولى وجعلته ترتقي إلى أربعة أنواع: الأول أن يظهر أثر عين ذلك الوصف في عين ذلك الحكم وهو متفق عليه كأثر عين الطواف في عين سورة البرة. والثاني أن يظهر عين ذلك الوصف في جنس ذلك الحكم وهو الذي ذكره المصنف كالصغر ظهر تأثيره في جنس حكم النكاح وهو ولاية المال للولي فكذا في ولاية النكاح. والثالث أن يؤثر جنسه في عين ذلك الحكم كإسقاط قضاء الصلوة المتكثرة بعد الإغماء فإن الجنس الإغماء وهو الجنون أثراً في عين الحائض فإن لمنسيه وهو مشتقة السفر تأثيرا في جنس سقوط الصلوة وهو سقوط الركعتين. وهذه الأقسام كلها مقبولة ولم يطل الكلام فيها صاحب التوضيح كم ذكر بيان الصلاح فقال ونعني
The summary is that his saying 'as a name and a ruling' is undoubtedly in contrast to the description, and his saying 'necessary and accidental' undoubtedly that these two are divisions of the description. As for the clear and obscure, and likewise the individual and the number, he presented them in a way of contrast and overlap, and apparently they are a division of the description, since you find no example for them except in the division of the description. The comprehensive meaning may be called 'description' absolutely in their convention, whether it is a description, a name, or a ruling, as will come. All this is from the innovative thought of the Imam, and the people follow him.
It is permissible in the text and other than it if it is established by it, i.e., it is permissible that that meaning be textually stated in the text, like circumambulation in the matter of the cow, and that it be in other than the text but established by it, like the examples that have just passed.
Then he began to explain how it is known that this description is a description rather than another, so he said: The indication of the description being a cause is its soundness and its reliability. Indeed, the description in analogy is like a witness in a claim. Just as in a witness for acceptance it is required that he be sound and reliable, so too in the description. And just as in a witness, action is not permissible before soundness and not obligatory before reliability, so too in the description. Then he explained the meaning of soundness and reliability without following the order of the word [in the text], so he began first by mentioning reliability with his saying: 'By the appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling for the thing being reasoned by it,' i.e., that the effect of the description appears in the genus of the ruling for the thing being reasoned by it from outside before the analogy. If its effect appears in the very ruling being reasoned by it, then it is by first priority. And he made it elevate to four types: The first is that the very description's effect appears in the very ruling, and it is agreed upon, like the effect of the very circumambulation in the very matter of the cow. The second is that the very description appears in the genus of that ruling, and it is what the author mentioned, like childhood: its effect appeared in the genus of the ruling of marriage, which is the guardianship of property for the guardian, so likewise in the guardianship of marriage. The third is that its genus affects the very ruling, like dropping the making up of many prayers after unconsciousness, for the genus of unconsciousness (which is insanity) had an effect in the very matter of menstruation, for its masdar (which is the source of travel) has an effect in the genus of dropping prayer, which is dropping two rak'ahs. These types are all acceptable, and the author of al-Tawdih did not go on at length about them. As he mentioned the explanation of soundness, he said: 'And we mean...'
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar is an expanded commentary on the nature and conditions of the 'illah (cause) in qiyas. It begins by clarifying that the description (wasf) as a legal cause can be categorized as a name (ism), ruling (hukm), necessary (lazim), or accidental (‘arid). The author then notes that the comprehensive meaning is called 'description' in their convention. The key point is that a description's validity as a cause is proven by its 'soundness' (salah) and 'reliability' ('adalah). Just as a witness must be sound and reliable for acceptance, so too a description must show its effect (athar) in the ruling. The commentator then explains the four types of effect that demonstrate reliability: 1) The very description affects the very ruling (e.g., circumambulation affects the ruling of Ihram in Sura al-Baqara). 2) The very description affects the genus of the ruling (e.g., childhood affects guardianship of property, so it also affects guardianship in marriage). 3) The genus of the description affects the very ruling (e.g., the genus of unconsciousness, which includes insanity, affects the dropping of prayer for a woman in menstruation). 4) The genus affects the genus (implied, not detailed). All these types are accepted. The discussion follows the methodology of Hanafi usul, emphasizing the necessity of empirical evidence for the cause's validity.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The effective cause (ratio legis) that connects a ruling to its basis in qiyas.
وصف (wasf): A description or attribute that serves as the cause in qiyas; it can be a name, ruling, necessary, or accidental.
أثر (athar): The effect of the description that appears in the ruling, proving its validity as a cause.
صلاح (salah): Soundness: the state of being fit to be a cause, proven by the appearance of its effect.
عدالة ('adalah): Reliability: the description's consistency in producing its effect across similar rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the first type of evidence that proves a description (wasf) is a reliable cause (ʿillah)?
A) The very description affects the very ruling.
B) The description's genus affects the genus of the ruling.
C) The description is textually stated in the Quran.
D) The description is mentioned in a hadith.

Key Takeaway
A description is a valid cause only if its effect is observable in the ruling or its genus, analogized to the reliability requirement of a witness.

The Four Types of 'Adalah of a Descriptor in Qiyas
Defines 'adalah of a descriptor with four scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four ways a descriptor's effect can appear to establish its 'adalah (reliability), and apply the Hanafi criterion to determine if a descriptor is fit to serve as a cause in qiyas.

Core Idea
A descriptor's reliability is proven by its effect appearing in the same genus of the ruling.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a descriptor (wasf) used as a cause ('illah) in qiyas must be reliable ('adil). This passage draws an analogy with a witness: just as a witness must be reliable and suitable, a descriptor must show its suitability and reliability. The author then defines 'adalah as the appearance of the descriptor's effect in the same genus of the ruling being explained, and outlines four accepted forms of such appearance. This lesson will break down these four forms and their application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Witness Analogy
Recognize the parallel between a descriptor in qiyas and a witness in court. A witness must be reliable ('adil) and suitable (salih); similarly, a descriptor must possess these qualities before it can be used as a cause.
This analogy sets the stage for the definition of 'adalah.
2
Define 'Adalah of a Descriptor
Identify the definition: 'adalah is proven by the appearance of the descriptor's effect in the same genus (jins) of the ruling being explained.
The passage specifies 'in the genus of the ruling' – not necessarily the exact ruling.
3
Distinguish the Four Forms of Appearance
List the four scenarios: (1) same descriptor appears in same ruling, (2) same descriptor appears in same genus of ruling, (3) genus of descriptor appears in same ruling, (4) genus of descriptor appears in same genus of ruling.
Each form is a valid proof of 'adalah; the passage states all are accepted.
4
Apply the Criterion to an Example
Take a concrete Hanafi example: consider the descriptor 'smallness' (saghar) as a cause for guardianship in marriage. Its effect appears in the genus of marriage (guardianship of wealth). This is form (2) – same descriptor, same genus.
The example is from the passage: saghar's effect in guardianship of wealth proves its 'adalah for guardianship of marriage.

And it is permissible for the sign (comprehensive) to be present in the text itself or not, but it must be established from it; i.e., it is permissible for this meaning, this cause, to be present in the text as a specific instance, like (in) the matter of tawaf of Surah? And it is also permissible for it to be in other than the text but established by the requirement of the text, as in these examples we have mentioned. After explaining the types and kinds of 'illah, the author (matn) is stating the criterion by which a cause is distinguished from a non-cause, i.e., it is not the text but the descriptor, not the other. So he said: 'And the indication of the descriptor being [something]' and the descriptor's suitability and reliability indicate its capability of being a cause. Therefore, the status of causality in the chapter of qiyas is like the status of a witness in a claim. So just as for accepting a witness it is required that he be reliable (adil) and suitable (salih), similarly, the descriptor-cause requires that it possesses suitability and reliability. And just as for a witness, action on his testimony is not permissible before suitability, and before reliability action is not obligatory, similarly the descriptor-cause: before suitability appears, acting upon it is not correct, and before reliability is confirmed, action is permissible but not obligatory. Then he explained the meaning of suitability and reliability. After that, the author is explaining the meaning and details of suitability and reliability in a non-chronological arrangement. So he first mentions reliability: 'By the appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling being explained' – before analogy in the genus of the ruling being explained, the effect of the descriptor (cause) must have appeared in the genus of the ruling being explained from an external source. (i.e., the descriptor being designated as a cause for some ruling must have been proven by another text to be a cause in the same genus of the ruling; if its effect has appeared exactly in proving this ruling, then a fortiori its reliability becomes apparent.) The result is that the proof of a descriptor's reliability has four forms. First: if the effect of the same cause appears in the same ruling by the assistance of another text, such an effect is unanimously effective, i.e., the cause is effective, like the cause of tawaf being the reason for the ruling of Surah? The second: that the same descriptor appears in the genus of that ruling, which is what the author mentioned, like smallness (saghar) – its effect appeared in the genus of the ruling of marriage, namely the guardianship of wealth for the guardian, so likewise in the guardianship of marriage. The third: that the genus of that descriptor appears in the same ruling, like the dropping of repeated prayers after fainting, because the genus of fainting is insanity and it had an effect in the same [ruling] from the menstruating woman? The fourth: that the genus of the descriptor appears in the genus of the ruling, like the hardship of travel having an effect in the genus of dropping prayer, which is dropping two rak'ahs. And all these divisions are accepted, and the author of al-Tawdih has elaborated on them, then he mentioned the explanation of suitability and said: ...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion on the concept of 'adalah (reliability) of a descriptor (wasf) that serves as a cause ('illah) in qiyas. The commentator begins by reiterating that a valid cause can be explicitly stated in the text or derived from it. He then introduces the key criteria: the descriptor must have salah (suitability) and 'adalah (reliability). To illustrate, he draws a parallel with a witness in court: a witness must be 'adil (reliable) and salih (suitable) for testimony to be accepted. Similarly, a descriptor must show that it is fit to be a cause. The passage focuses on 'adalah, defining it as the appearance of the descriptor's effect in the same genus (jins) of the ruling being explained. Four scenarios are enumerated: (1) the same descriptor appearing in the same ruling, (2) the same descriptor appearing in the same genus of the ruling, (3) the same genus of the descriptor appearing in the same ruling, and (4) the same genus of the descriptor appearing in the same genus of the ruling. All four are accepted as proof of 'adalah. The commentator notes that Sadr al-Shari'ah (author of al-Tawdih) has discussed these at length.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adalah): The reliability of a descriptor, proven when its effect appears in the same genus of the ruling or the same ruling, making it fit to serve as a cause in qiyas.
وصف (wasf): A property or attribute considered as the potential cause ('illah) for a legal ruling in qiyas.
جنس (jins): Genus; a broader category that encompasses multiple specific rulings. In this context, the genus of a ruling is a type of legal effect (e.g., guardianship, prohibition, reduction of prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an accepted form of establishing a descriptor's reliability ('adalah)?
A) The same descriptor appears in the same ruling, proven by another text.
B) The same descriptor appears in a different genus of ruling without any link.
C) The descriptor is mentioned in a dream of a scholar.
D) The descriptor is rejected by the majority of jurists.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a descriptor's 'adalah (reliability) is established by the appearance of its effect in the same genus or same ruling, following four accepted forms.

The Suitability (Salah) of the Descriptor: The Example of Marriage Guardianship
Defines salah and illustrates with marriage guardianship dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi criterion of salah (suitability) for a descriptor in qiyas and apply it to evaluate the 'illah in a madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
A descriptor is suitable only if it harmonizes with the 'illal transmitted from the Prophet, Companions, and Successors.

This lesson introduces the second criterion for a valid 'illah in Hanafi usul: salah, or suitability. Unlike the first criterion of reliability (thubut), suitability concerns the substantive harmony of the proposed cause with the established 'illal from the early authorities. The text defines salah and then illustrates it with the Hanafi use of minority (saghar) as the 'illah for marriage guardianship, contrasting with the Shafi'i position of virginity (bikarah). By the end, you will see how this concept of suitability anchors Hanafi qiyas in transmitted precedent.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of salah
The text states: 'We mean by the suitability of the descriptor: its harmony.' Harmony means the descriptor must agree with the transmitted 'illal from the Prophet and the Salaf.
2
Identify the criterion of suitability
A descriptor is suitable if it does not deviate (nabiya) from the transmitted 'illal. It must be in accordance (muwafaqa) with them.
The text uses 'nabiya' to indicate conflict.
3
Examine the Hanafi example
The Hanafi 'illah for marriage guardianship is minority (saghar). The text shows that this 'illah has an effect (athar) and is based on transmitted 'illal (e.g., in property guardianship).
The example demonstrates how a suitable 'illah is derived from earlier precedents.
4
Compare with the opposing school
The Shafi'i 'illah is virginity (bikarah). The four-case analysis (virgin minor, non-virgin adult, etc.) shows the practical consequences and why the Hanafi 'illah is considered suitable for protecting the minor's interest.
The dispute illustrates the application of the suitability criterion.

وَنَعْنِي بصلاح الْوَصفِ مُلايَمَتَهُ وَهِيَ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَلَى مُوَافَقَة الْعَلَلِ الْمَنْقُولَة عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ وَعَنِ السَّلْفِ بِأَنْ تَكُونَ عِلَّةُ هَذَا الْمُجْتَهِدِ مُوَافِقَةٌ لِعَلَّةٍ اسْتَبَطَ بِهَا النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَالصَّحَابَةُ وَالتَّابِعُونَ وَلَا تَكُونَ نَابِيَةً عَنْهَا كَتَعْلِيلِنَا بِالصَّغَرِ فِي وَلَايَةِ الْمُنَاكِحِ جَمْعِ مَنْكَحٍ بِمَعْنَى النَّكَاحِ وَقِيلَ جَمْعُ مَنْكُوحَةٍ وَهُوَ ضَعِيفٌ وَاخْتُلِفَ فِي عِلَّةِ وَلَايَةِ النِّكَاحِ فَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْبَكَارَةُ وَعِنْدَنَا الصَّغَرُ وَبَيْنَهُمَا عُمُومٌ وَخُصُوصٌ مِنْ وَجْهٍ فَالصَّغِيرَةُ يَجُوزُ أَنْ تَكُونَ بِكْرًا وَأَنْ تَكُونَ ثَيِّبًا وَكَذَا الْبِكْرُ يَجُوزُ أَنْ تَكُونَ صَغِيرَةً وَأَنْ تَكُونَ بَالِغَةً فَالْبِكْرُ الصَّغِيرَةُ يُولَى عَلَيْهَا اتِّفَاقًا وَالثَّيِّبُ الْبَالِغَةُ لَا يُولَى عَلَيْهَا اتِّفَاقًا وَالثَّيِّبُ الصَّغِيرَةُ يُولَى عَلَيْهَا عِنْدَنَا دُونَ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَالْبِكْرُ الْبَالِغَةُ يُولَى عَلَيْهَا عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ لَا عِنْدَنَا فَعِنْدَنَا لِلصَّغَرِ تَأْثِيرٌ فِي وَلَايَةِ النِّكَاحِ
We mean by the suitability of the descriptor: its harmony, i.e., that it is in agreement with the transmitted causes from the Messenger of Allah and from the predecessors (salaf), such that the cause of this mujtahid is in accordance with a cause derived by the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the Companions and the Successors, and not deviant from them, like our explanation using smallness (saghar) in guardianship of marriage (wilayat al-manakih) – 'manakih' is the plural of 'mankah' meaning marriage, and it is also said plural of 'mankuhah' which is weak. And there is a difference of opinion regarding the cause of guardianship in marriage: according to al-Shafi'i it is virginity (bikarah), and according to us it is minority (saghar). Between them there is a general-special relationship from one perspective: a minor girl can be a virgin or a non-virgin; similarly, a virgin can be a minor or an adult. So a virgin minor is agreed upon to be under guardianship; a non-virgin adult is agreed not to be under guardianship; a non-virgin minor is under guardianship according to us but not according to al-Shafi'i; and a virgin adult is under guardianship according to al-Shafi'i but not according to us. So according to us, minority has an effect in guardianship of marriage.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage defines the second criterion for a valid descriptor: salah (suitability). A descriptor is suitable when it is in harmony with the 'illal transmitted from the Prophet, the Companions, and the Successors. In other words, the mujtahid's 'illah must align with the 'illal that these authorities used, and not be in conflict with them. The commentator provides the example of the Hanafi 'illah for guardianship in marriage: they use minority (saghar) while al-Shafi'i uses virginity (bikarah). The passage then details the implications of this difference in the four possible combinations of a female (minor/adult, virgin/non-virgin). In Hanafi law, the presence of minority gives guardianship, whereas in Shafi'i law, virginity gives guardianship. This difference shows that the Hanafi 'illah is not arbitrary; it is based on transmitted 'illal that connect minority to guardianship in property matters, and thus it is suitable. The passage concludes that minority has an effect (ta'thir) in the context of marriage guardianship.

Key Terms
صلاح (salah): Suitability of a descriptor, meaning it is in harmony with the 'illal transmitted from the Prophet, Companions, and Successors, and not deviant from them.
علة ('illah): The cause or effective attribute that serves as the basis for extending a ruling via qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, which descriptor is the correct 'illah for guardianship of a minor in marriage?
A) Virginity (bikarah)
B) Minority (saghar)
C) Adulthood (bulugh)
D) Beauty (jamal)

Key Takeaway
A descriptor is suitable for qiyas only if it harmonizes with the 'illal transmitted from the early authorities, not merely because it seems reasonable.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Suitability of the Attribute in Qiyas: The Hanafi View on Guardianship
Explaining the condition of suitability for an attribute to be a valid cause in qiyas, with the example of guardianship in marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition of suitability (salahiyya) for a legal cause in qiyas and apply it to the dispute over guardianship in marriage, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
An attribute is a valid cause only if it harmonizes with the causes of the Prophet and Salaf — like minority in marriage because it causes necessity.

In this lesson, we examine a key condition in Hanafi qiyas: the attribute used as a legal cause must be 'suitable' (mulaim), meaning it aligns with causes derived from revelation and the early Salaf. Using the classic dispute over guardianship in marriage, you will see how the Hanafis justify minority as the cause, while the Shafi'is propose virginity. This analysis will sharpen your ability to evaluate legal analogies within the Hanafi usul framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed 'illa
State the cause each school claims for guardianship in marriage: Shafi'i says virginity (bikara); Hanafi says minority (sighar).
2
Understand the condition of suitability
Explain that suitability means the proposed cause must conform to the causes derived by the Prophet, Companions, and Successors — it must lead to the same type of necessitating factor (e.g., hardship/incapacity).
3
Apply the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis argue that minority is suitable because it already serves as a cause for guardianship over property (by consensus) and because it entails incapacity, analogous to the necessity that made the cat's leftover water pure.
The hadith about the cat's tawaf shows that necessity can render an impure thing pure; similarly, minority necessitates guardianship.
4
Map the four scenarios
List the four combinations of virgin/minor and determine which school grants guardianship in each: minor virgin (both), adult non-virgin (neither), minor non-virgin (only Hanafi), adult virgin (only Shafi'i). This shows the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text prefers the Hanafi position because it aligns with the transmitted cause of necessity (as in the cat hadith) and is supported by consensus on property guardianship.
Tarjih authority: The text (Ashraf al-Anwar) favours Hanafi view.

بصلاح الْوَصفِ مُلايَمَتَهُ وَهِيَ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَلَى مُوَافَقَة الْعِلَلِ الْمَنْقُولَة عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ وَعَنِ السَّلْفِ بِأَنْ تَكُونَ عِلَّةُ هَذَا الْمُجْتَهِدِ مُوَافِقَةً لِعِلَّةٍ اسْتَنْبَطَ بِهَا النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَالصَّحَابَةُ وَالتَّابِعُونَ وَلَا تَكُون نَابِيَةً عَنْهَا كَتَعْلِيلِنَا بِالصَّغَرِ فِي وَلَايَةِ الْمُنَاكِحِ جَمْعِ مَنْكَحٍ بِمَعْنَى وَجْهٍ فَالصَّغِيرَةُ يَجُوزُ أَنْ تَكُونَ بِكْرًا وَأَنْ تَكُونَ ثَيِّبًا وَكَذَا الْبِكْرُ يَجُوزُ أَنْ تَكُونَ صَغِيرَةً وَأَنْ تَكُونَ بَالِغَةً فَالْبِكْرُ الصَّغِيرَةُ يُوَلَّى عَلَيْهَا اتِّفَاقًا وَالثَّيِّبُ الْبَالِغَةُ لَا يُوَلَّى عَلَيْهَا اتِّفَاقًا وَالثَّيِّبُ الصَّغِيرَةُ يُوَلَّى عَلَيْهَا عِنْدَنَا دُونَ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَالْبِكْرُ الْبَالِغَةُ يُوَلَّى عَلَيْهَا عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ لَا عِنْدَنَا فَعِنْدَنَا لِلصَّغَرِ تَأْثِيرٌ فِي وَلَايَةِ النِّكَاحِ ترجمه و تشریح والثانى اثر عين ذالك الوصف (۲) دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ بعینہ اس وصف کا اثر اس حکم کے جنس میں ظاہر ہو جس کو مصنف نے ذکر کیا ہے جیسے صغر سنی وصف علم ہے جس کی تاثیر حکم النکاح کی جنس میں ظاہر ہوئی ہے اور وہ صغیر کے مال میں ولی کی ولایت ہے چونکہ لڑکی صغیرہ ہے اس لئے اس کے مال کی ولایت ولی کو حاصل ہوگی (تو اس پر قیاس کر کے ایسا ہی ولایت نکاح میں بھی صغر سنی علت ہے) جو ولی کو حاصل ہو گی۔ والثالث :- تیسری اس وصف کے ہم جنسی وصف کا اثر بعینہ حکم معلل بہ میں ظاہر ہو جیسے اعمار کے عذر کی وجہ سے کثیر نمازوں کی قضاوں کا مغمی علیہ سے ساقط ہو جانا کیونکہ جس اغماء اور غماء جنون بے ہوشی کو کہتے ہیں ۔ اور اسی طرح عذر حیض پر قیاس کر کے جس کا اثر بعینہ سقوط صلوۃ کثیرہ میں ظاہر ہو چکا ہے (مقیس علیہ یہاں پر حائضہ سے کثیر صلواۃ کی قضاء کا ساقط ہوتا ہے اور عذر حیض ہے اسی طرح عذر اغماء ہے جس کی وجہ سے کثیر صلوۃ کی قضا اس سے ساقط کر دی گئی ہے۔ چہارم (۴) اس وصف کے ہم جنس وصف کا اثر حکم معلل بہ کے ہم جنس حکم میں ظاہر ہو ۔ جیسے بحالت حیض کلیه حائضہ سے وقت یہ نمازوں کا ساقط ہو جانا کیونکہ اس کے ہم جنس اور وہ سفر کی مشقت ہے جس کو تاثیر حاصل ہے جنس سقوط صلوۃ میں۔ ( یعنی چونکہ مہ حمت کے عذر سے جنس صلوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے یعنی چار کے بجائے دورہ جاتیں ہیں قصر واجب ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح اس وصف علت کی جنس ہے مشقت و دشواری کا عذر ہے جس کی وجہ سے حائضہ سے ستقوم و صلوۃ کا حکم دیا گیا ہے سے) وهذه الاقسام عدالت وصف کی یہ تمام قسمیں مقبول ہیں صاحب توضیح علامہ صدر الشریعہ نے اس پر کافی طویل بحث بھی فرمائی ہے وصف عدالت کو بیان کرنے کے بعد اب ماتن وصف کی صلاحیت کا بیان شروع فرمایا ہے فرمایا یعنی اصلاح الوصف ملائمتہ اور صلاح وصف سے ہماری مراد یہ ہے کہ وصف حکم سے مناسبت رکھتا ہو یعنی وصف ان علتوں کے موافق ہو جو جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور سلف صالحین سے منقول ہیں۔ بایں طور کہ اس مجتہد کی استنباط کی ہوئی علت اس علمت کے موافق ہو جیسے جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم حضرات صحابہ کرام اور تابعین نے استنباط کیا ہو۔ انکے خلاف نہ ہو تابعة عنہا ان کے خلاف اور بعید نہ بو كتعليلنا بالمصفر في ولاية المناكح جیسا کہ ہم نے نکاح کی ولایت کیلئے صغر کو علت قرار دیا ہے۔ مناکح منكح کی جمع ہے معنی نکاح کے ہیں اور مصدر میمی ہے اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ مناکح منکوحہ کی جمع ہے مگر یہ قول ضعیف ہے ولایتہ نکاری کی علت میں اختلاف ہے امام شافعی کے نزدیک بکار و علت ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک صغر علت ہے، بکار ۃ و صفر دونوں کے درمیان عموم و خصوص من وجہ کی نسبت ہے (اس نسبت میں تین مادہ ہوتے ہیں) ایک مادہ اجتماعی وہ لڑکی جس میں صفر و بکار ناردونوں جمع ہوں دو مار کے افتراقی صغیرہ ہو بکارت زائل ہو گئی ہو بکارت موجود ہو مگر صغیرو نہ ہو تو اجتماعی بادہ میں دونوں کا اتفاق ہو گا مار و افتراقی میں صغیرہ کے لیئے احناف کے نزدیک ولایت حاصل ہے امام شافعی کے نزدیک ولایت حاصل نہ ہو گی بکار ہو صغیر و نہ ہو بالغہ ہو تو امام شافعی سین کے نزدیک وہاں ولایت حاصل ہو گی۔ اس مضمون کو مصنف کی عبارت میں سنئے۔ فالصغيرة يجوز مغیرہ جائز ہے کہ ہاکرہ ہو (۲) صغیرہ ہو اور شیبہ ہو یا کرہ نہو ا یسے ہی باکرہ جائز ہے کہ صغیرہ ہو۔ اور یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ بالغہ ہو لہذا ان تینوں صورتوں میں پاکرہ صغیرہ میں ولایت بالاتفاق حاصل اور ٹیبہ غیر با کره) بالغہ کی ولایت بالا تفاق کسی کو حاصل نہیں اور ثیبہ صغیرہ ہمارے احناف کے نزدیک ولایت حاصل ہے امام شافعی کے نزدیک ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے کیونکہ ٹیہ ہے اور باکرہ بالغہ میں ولایت حاصل ہو گی امام شافعی کے نزدیک نہ کہ ہمارے نزدیک لہذا ہمارے نزدیک مغر سنی علت موثر ہے ولایت نکاح میں۔ لمَا يَتُصِلُ به مِنَ الْعِجْزِ إِذَا الصَّغِيرَةُ عَاجِرَةٌ عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ فِى نَفْسِهَا وَمَالِهَا. وَلَا تَهْتَدِى إِلَيْهِ سَبِيْلاً وَقَدْ ظَهَرَ تَاثِيرُهُ فِي وَلَايَةِ الْمَالِ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ فَكَذَا فِي وِلَآيَةٍ النّكَاح فَإِنَّهُ أي الصَّغَرُ مُؤثِرٌ فِي إِثْبَاتِ الْوِلايَةِ مَثْلُ تَاثِيرُ الطَّوَافِ فِي طَهَارَةِ سُورِ الْهِرْةِ لِمَا يَأْصِلُ بِهِ مِنَ الضَّرُورَةِ وَالْحَرَجِ فِي كَثُرَةِ الْمُزَاوَلَةِ وَالْمَجِي فَالْحَاصِلُ أن وصف الصَّغْرِ الَّذِى نَقُولُ بِهِ فِى ولايَةِ النِّكَاحِ مُوَافِقُ لَوصْفِ الطَّوَافِ الَّذِئ قَالَ بِهِ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلاَمُ فِى سُورِ الْهِرَّةِ فِي كَوْنِهِمَا مَفْضِبًا إلى الحَرَج وَالضَّرُورَةِ فَكَمَا أَنَّ الطَّوَافَ فِي البِرَّةِ صَارَ ضَرُورَةٌ لَأَزِمَةٌ لِطَهَارَةِ السُّورِ فَكَذَا الصَّغْرُ فِي النِكَاحِ صَارَ ضَرُورَةُ لأَزِمَةٌ لِوِلَايَةِ النِّكَاحِ دُونَ العِرَادِ مُتَعَلِّق بِقَوْلَه صَلاحَه وعَدَالَيْهِ أَيْ دَلِيْلُ كَوْنِ الْوَصفِ عِلَّةٌ صَلَاحِهِ وَعَدَ اللَّهِ
With the suitability of the description: its harmonization, and it is that it be in agreement with the causes transmitted from the Messenger of Allah and from the Salaf, such that this mujtahid's cause is in conformity with a cause derived by the Prophet (peace be upon him), the Companions, and the Successors, and not divergent from them, like our making minority the cause in the guardianship of marriage (al-manakih, plural of mankah meaning marriage; and it is said plural of mankuhah, but that is weak). There is disagreement over the cause of guardianship in marriage: according to al-Shafi'i, it is virginity; according to us, it is minority. Between them is general and specific from some respects. So a minor girl may be a virgin or a non-virgin; likewise a virgin may be a minor or an adult. So the minor virgin is guardianship over by agreement; the adult non-virgin is not under guardianship by agreement; the minor non-virgin is under guardianship according to us but not al-Shafi'i; the adult virgin is under guardianship according to al-Shafi'i but not us. So in our view, minority has effect in guardianship of marriage. Translation and explanation: The second: the effect of the very same description. The second case is that the effect of the very same description appears in the genus of that ruling which the author mentioned, like minority as the description is known, its effect appears in the genus of the ruling of marriage, and that is the guardian's authority over the minor's property. Since the girl is minor, the guardian has authority over her property; so by qiyas, similarly in guardianship of marriage, minority is the cause. The third: the effect of a description of the same genus as this description appears in the very same ruling, like the dropping of many prayers from the unconscious person due to the excuse of unconsciousness, which is like the excuse of menstruation by qiyas, whose effect appears in the dropping of many prayers. The fourth: the effect of a description of the same genus as this description appears in a ruling of the same genus as the ruled ruling, like the dropping of prayers from a menstruating woman during menses because its counterpart is the hardship of travel which has effect in the genus of dropping prayer. And these categories are all accepted regarding the justness of the description. The author of al-Tawdih, 'Allama Sadr al-Shari'a, has discussed this at length. After explaining the justness of the description, the text now begins to explain the suitability of the description: i.e., the rectification of the description is its harmonization. Our meaning of suitability of the description is that the description has appropriateness to the ruling, i.e., the description conforms to the causes transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (SAW) and the righteous Salaf, such that the cause derived by this mujtahid conforms to the cause derived by the Prophet, the Companions and the Successors, not opposing them, like our making minority the cause in guardianship of marriage. For what attaches to it of incapacity, since the minor is incapable of managing herself and her property and finds no way to it, and its effect has appeared in guardianship of property by agreement, so likewise in guardianship of marriage. Indeed, minority has effect in establishing guardianship, like the effect of circumambulation on the purity of the leftover water of the cat, because of the necessity and hardship attached to it due to frequent moving about. The conclusion is that the description of minority which we adopt in guardianship of marriage conforms to the description of circumambulation which the Prophet adopted regarding the leftover of the cat, in that both lead to hardship and necessity. Just as circumambulation became a necessary cause for the purity of the leftover water, so minority in marriage became a necessary cause for guardianship of marriage, not (other) customs.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains the condition of 'suitability' (salahiyya) of an attribute to serve as a valid legal cause ('illa) in qiyas. The commentator states that an attribute is suitable if it harmonizes with the causes derived from the Prophet, Companions, and Successors — meaning the mujtahid's cause must align with those transmitted causes and not contradict them. The example given is the Hanafi position that minority (sighar) is the cause for guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah). This sets up an inter-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i holds that virginity (bikara) is the cause, while Hanafis hold minority. The passage then analyzes the overlapping relationships between these two attributes: a minor can be virgin or non-virgin; a virgin can be minor or adult. This yields four cases: (1) minor virgin — guardianship by agreement; (2) adult non-virgin — no guardianship by agreement; (3) minor non-virgin — guardianship by Hanafis only; (4) adult virgin — guardianship by Shafi'i only. This shows the practical effect of the disagreement. The commentator then explains why minority is a suitable cause: because the minor is incapable of managing her own affairs (property and self), and minority already serves as a cause for guardianship over property by consensus. Thus, by qiyas, it also serves for marriage. To further demonstrate suitability, the author draws an analogy with the cat's leftover water: the Prophet ruled that tawaf (circumambulation) causes the purity of the cat's leftover water due to necessity and hardship, though the cat is impure. Similarly, minority necessitates guardianship due to the minor's inherent incapacity and the need for protection. This analogy shows that the attribute of minority leads to the same type of necessity/ hardship that the Prophet recognized in a different context, thereby fulfilling the condition of suitability—the Hanafi 'illa aligns with the Prophetic 'illa of necessity.

Key Terms
صلاح الوصف (salahiyyat al-wasf): Suitability of the attribute/description as a legal cause, meaning it harmonizes with the causes transmitted from the Prophet and the Salaf.
ملاءمة (mulaiama): Harmonization or congruence between the attribute and the transmitted causes.
علة ('illa): The legal cause or effective attribute that justifies a ruling in qiyas.
ولاية النكاح (wilayat al-nikah): Guardianship in marriage; the authority of a guardian to contract a marriage on behalf of a minor or insane person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the underlying cause ('illa) for guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah) over a minor girl?
A) Virginity (bukara)
B) Minority (sighar)
C) Both virginity and minority
D) Adulthood (bulugh)

Key Takeaway
An attribute is suitable as a legal cause only if it harmonizes with the causes derived from revelation and the Salaf, producing necessity — like minority in marriage.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Mu'aththir vs Tard in 'Illa Validation
Explaining that suitability and justice of a description prove it is an effective cause, not mere correlation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mu'aththir (effectiveness) and tard (consistency) in validating an 'illa and apply the Hanafi criterion to a given case.

Core Idea
A cause is proven by its suitability and effectiveness, not by mere correlation.

In Hanafi usul, not every description that accompanies a ruling is a valid cause. This passage explains that a description must be effective (mu'aththir) — meaning it is suitable and just, conforming to revealed causes — rather than merely consistent (tard). Through the example of guardianship in marriage, we see how the Hanafis argue for minority as the cause against the Shafi'i use of virginity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods of validating 'illa
Recognize that the text contrasts mu'aththiriyya (effectiveness) with tardiyya (consistency). Mu'aththir is based on suitability (salah) and justice ('adala); tard relies on co-rotation of ruling with description.
The Hanafi school accepts only mu'aththir as proof.
2
Understand the Hanafi criterion for mu'aththir
A description is suitable if it conforms to the causes used by the Prophet and the salaf, and it is just if it is not far-fetched. The description must have a proportional relationship (munasaba) with the ruling.
This is the standard for effective causality.
3
Examine the example: wilayat al-nikah
The Hanafi position uses minority (saghir) as the cause; the Shafi'i uses virginity (bikr). Analyze the three cases: common (both present), minor non-virgin, adult virgin.
Disagreement arises only in the exclusive cases.
4
Follow the Hanafi proof via analogy
Minority implies incapacity, proven in property guardianship by consensus. Analogy (qiyas) transfers this to marriage. A second analogy with the cat's mouth hadith shows that necessity and hardship justify the cause.
Both analogies highlight effectiveness (mu'aththir).
5
Conclude why tard is rejected
Tard may be coincidental (e.g., a condition that accompanies a ruling without causing it). Non-existence of the ruling when the description is absent is irrelevant to causality. Thus, tard does not prove causality.
The text explicitly states tard is not a proof according to the Hanafis.

عِنْدَ وَجُودِهِ وَلَا يَسْطَرَطُ عَدَمَهُ عِنْدَ عَدَمِهِ وَعَلَى كُلِّ تَقْدِيرِ لَيْسَ هُوَ بِحُجْةٍ عِنْدَنَا حَاكِمْ يَظْهَرُ تَاثِيرُهُ لانَّ الْوُجُودَ قَدْ يَكُونُ اِتِّفَاقِيًا كَمَا فِي وُجُودِ الْحُكْمِ عِنْدَ الشَّرْطِ فَلاَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى كَوْنِهِ عِلَّةَ وَالْعَدَمُ لاَدْخَلَ لَهُ فِى عِلْيَةٍ شقي بَالْبَدَاهَةِ وَلِظُهُورِهِ لَمْ يَتَعَرَّضَ لَهِ وَمِثْلَة التَّعْلِيلُ بِالنَّفْي أى مِثْلُ الإطرَارِ فِي عَدَم صَلاحِيَتِهِ لِلدَّلِيلِ التَّعْلِيْلِ بِالنَّفْيِ وَوَقَعَ فِي بَعْضِ النُّحْ قَوْلُهُ وَمِنْ جِنْسِهِ. لِمَا يَتَّصِيلُ بِه مِن الْعِجْزِ - کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ بجز اور مجبوری وابستہ ہے کیونکہ صغیرہ ترجمه و تشریح لڑکی اپنے نفس میں تصرف کرنے سے عاجز ہوتی ہے تصرف کرنے کا راستہ نہیں جانتی کہ کس طرح صحیح ڈھنگ سے سر انجام دے۔ اور عدم بلوغ کا اثر ماں کی ولایت میں بالاتفاق ظاہر ہو بھی چکا ہے تو اس پر قیاس کر کے ولی کو ولایت نکاح کا حق حاصل ہونا چاہیے۔ فَإِنَّه أَي الصَّغْرُ مُؤثرُ فِي اثْبَاتِ الوِلايَةِ یہ تو " صغر " موثر ہے ولایت کے اثبات میں جس طرح طواف مؤثر ہے سورہرو کی طہارت میں لما يتصل بها الخ کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ بھی ضرورت اور مجبوری وابستہ ہے کہ گھر کے اندر بلی کا رہن سہن اور بار بار گھر کے اندر آنے اور جانے کی وجہ سے اس سے بچنار شوار ہے اور تنگی کا سبب ہے پس حاصل یہ ہے کہ مغر کا وصف جس کو ہم ولایت نکاح میں موثر مانتے ہیں یہ اس وصف (یعنی طواف) کے موافق ہے جس کو جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سور ہرہ کے حکم کے بارے میں اعتبار فرمایا ہے۔ کیونکہ حرج اور ضرورت دونوں میں پائی جاتی ہے لہذا جس طرح سور ہرہ میں طواق لازمی ضرورت قرار پاگئی ہے۔ سور ہرہ کی طہارت کے لئے اسی طرح صغر سنی بھی نکاح کے حکم میں ولایت نکاح کے لئے ضرورت لازمہ بن گئی ہے دون الاطراد اور اطراد دلیل نہیں ہے مصنف کے قول صلاحیه وعد الله سے دون الاطر از کا تعلق ہے جس کا نام طرحیت رکھا جاتا ہے اور اطراد کے معنی وصف کے ساتھ ساتھ حکم کا دائر ہوتا ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں تلازم ہو اور ایک دوسرے کے تابع ہو۔ نوٹ :۔ قیاس کی علت بننے کے لئے وصف کی صلاحیت و عدالت ہی دلیل ہے جس کا دوسر ا موثر ہوتا بھی ہے لیکن امر او مطرو ہونا کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے اس کو کر دیت بھی کہتے ہیں وجوداً أو عدما اورجوداً فقط وجود اور عدم دونوں میں بانتقاء جود میں مصنف نے یہ اس لئے کہا ہے کہ چونکہ خود اطراد کے معنی میں اختلاف واقع ہوا ہے بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اطراد کے معنی ہی ہیں کہ
He began saying: i.e. the suitability of the description and its appropriateness. What we mean by suitability of the description is that the description has a proportionality (munasaba) with the ruling, i.e. the description conforms to those causes (ilal) that are transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and the pious predecessors. Such that the cause deduced by this mujtahid conforms to the cause that the Prophet (peace be upon him), the Companions, and the Followers deduced. It should not oppose them nor be far-fetched. Like our using minority (saghir) as the cause for guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah). For example, we have made minority the cause for guardianship in marriage. 'Manakih' is the plural of 'mankah' meaning marriage, and it is a verbal noun (masdar mimi). Some have said that 'manakih' is the plural of 'mankuha', but this saying is weak. There is disagreement over the cause of guardianship in marriage: according to Imam al-Shafi'i, virginity (bikr) is the cause, and according to us, minority is the cause. Between virginity and minority there is a relationship of generality and specificity from one aspect (umum wa khusus min wajh). (In this relationship there are three cases: one common case: a girl in whom both minority and virginity are combined; two exclusive cases: a minor whose virginity is removed, and a virgin who is not a minor). In the common case, both agree. In the exclusive cases: for a minor (thayyiba) the Hanafis hold guardianship, while Shafi'i does not; for a virgin adult, Shafi'i holds guardianship, while we do not. So listen to this meaning in the author's expression: "So the minor girl is permissible even if she is not a virgin (thayyiba), and similarly the virgin is permissible if she is a minor, and the adult (non-virgin) is also permissible." Thus in these three cases: for the minor non-virgin, guardianship is established by consensus; for the adult non-virgin, no one has guardianship by consensus; for the minor non-virgin (thayyiba saghira), we Hanafis hold guardianship, while Shafi'i does not because she is thayyiba; for the adult virgin, guardianship is established according to Shafi'i, not according to us. Therefore, according to us, minority is an effective cause (mu'aththir) in guardianship in marriage. Because it is connected with incapacity (al-'ajz). Indeed, the minor girl is incapable of managing her own affairs and her wealth, and she does not know the way to it. And its effect has already appeared in guardianship over property by consensus, so likewise in guardianship in marriage. Verily, minority is effective in establishing guardianship, like the effect of tawaf (going around) in the purification of the mouth of a cat, because it is connected with necessity and hardship due to frequent contact and coming and going. So the conclusion is that the description of minority, which we use in guardianship in marriage, conforms to the description of tawaf which the Prophet (peace be upon him) applied in the matter of the cat's mouth, in that both lead to hardship and necessity. Just as tawaf in the cat became a necessary necessity for the purification of its mouth, so minority in marriage became a necessary necessity for guardianship in marriage, not consistency (tard). The statement "salahiyya and 'adala" refers to the proof that the description is a cause: its suitability and its justice (i.e., being appropriate and not far-fetched). And this is called mu'aththiriyya (effectiveness), not tardiyya (consistency). The meaning of tard (consistency) is the co-rotation (dawaran) of the ruling with the description in existence and non-existence, or in existence only. He said that because they differed over its meaning. Some said: the existence of the ruling when it exists and its non-existence when it is absent. Others said: its existence when it exists, and its non-existence when it is absent is not required. In any case, it is not a proof according to us, because existence may be coincidental, as in the existence of the ruling at the condition (shart), so it does not indicate that it is a cause. And non-existence has no bearing on causality, obviously. And due to its obviousness, he did not discuss it. And like it is the reasoning by negation: i.e. like tard in its lack of suitability for proof, the reasoning by negation. And in some copies occurs his statement "and of its kind". Because it is connected with incapacity (al-'ajz): the translation and explanation: The minor girl is incapable of acting in her own person and wealth and does not know the path to it. And the effect of non-bulugh has already appeared in guardianship over property by consensus, so analogically the guardian should have the right of guardianship in marriage. "Verily, minority is effective in establishing guardianship." This is that minority is effective in establishing guardianship, just as tawaf is effective in the purification of the cat's mouth, because it too is connected with necessity and hardship: the cat's living in the house and frequent coming and going make it difficult to avoid and cause hardship. So the conclusion is that the description of minority which we consider effective in guardianship in marriage conforms to the description (i.e., tawaf) which the Prophet (peace be upon him) considered in the ruling concerning the cat's mouth, because hardship and necessity are found in both. Therefore, just as tawaf in the cat became a necessary necessity for its purification, so minority in marriage became a necessary necessity for guardianship in marriage. Not tard (consistency). Tard is not a proof. The author's statement "salahiyya and 'adala" is connected to "not tard", which is called tardiyya. And the meaning of tard is that the ruling revolves with the description in existence and non-existence, or existence only. Note: For a description to be a cause in qiyas, its suitability and 'adala are the proof, which is also called mu'aththir. But the mere fact of being consistent (tard) is not a proof; it is called tardiyya. Existence and non-existence, or existence only: The author said that because they differed on its meaning. Some said the meaning of tard is the existence of the ruling when it exists and its non-existence when it is absent; others said its existence when it exists, and non-existence when absent is not required.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage discusses the validation of a description (wasf) as a cause ('illa) for a ruling in qiyas. The author explains that a description is considered effective (mu'aththir) if it is suitable (salah) and just ('adala), meaning it is appropriate and not far-fetched, and it conforms to the causes used by the Prophet and the early scholars. Mere correlation (tard), where the ruling always accompanies the description, is not sufficient proof. The author uses the example of guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah) to illustrate the Hanafi position. The Hanafis consider minority (saghir) as the effective cause, because a minor is incapable of managing her own affairs. This is based on analogy with guardianship over property, where minority is accepted by consensus. The Shafi'is use virginity (bikr) as the cause. The author then explains the relationship between the two descriptions and the three possible cases: common (both minority and virginity), exclusive to minority (minor non-virgin), and exclusive to virginity (adult virgin). In the common case, both schools agree on guardianship; in the exclusive cases, each school sticks to its cause. The author further supports the Hanafi cause by drawing an analogy with the purification of a cat's mouth. The Prophet allowed tawaf (circumambulation) to purify a cat's mouth due to necessity and hardship. Similarly, minority necessitates guardianship in marriage due to the minor's incapacity. Finally, the author clarifies that tard (consistent co-rotation) is not a valid proof for establishing a cause, because coincidence is possible, and non-existence has no bearing on causality. Thus, only mu'aththir (effectiveness) based on suitability is acceptable.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illa): The description (wasf) that necessitates a ruling and is used in qiyas.
المؤثرية (al-mu'aththiriyya): The quality of a description that shows it is effective in producing the ruling, proven by its suitability and justice.
الاطراد (al-ittirād): The consistent co-rotation of the ruling with the description in existence or both existence and non-existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, which of the following is the correct cause for guardianship in marriage?
A) Virginity (al-bikr)
B) Majority (al-bulugh)
C) Minority (al-sighar)
D) Consent (al-rida)

Key Takeaway
A description's effectiveness (mu'aththir) is established by its suitability and alignment with revealed causes, not by mere correlation (tard).
